ORDINANCE NO. 707
AN ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF GOODING, IDAHO, PROVIDING FOR AN OFFICIAL
NEWSPAPER AND REPEALING ORDINANCE NO. 664; AND PROVIDING FOR AN EFFECTIVE
DATE.
WHEREAS, Idaho Code §50-213, provides that cities are required to designate an official
newspaper.
THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED BY THE MAYOR AND COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF
GOODING, IDAHO AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1: That Gooding City Ordinance No. 664 is hereby repealed in its entirety.
Section 2: That the Courier News, a weekly newspaper with general circulation within the
City, is designated and constituted the official newspaper of the City of Gooding, Idaho. All
such writings as are required by virtue of a state statute or the governing body of the City shall
be published in said newspaper.
Section 3: All provisions of the current Municipal Code of the City of Gooding that conflicts
with the provisions of this Ordinance are hereby repealed to the extent of such conflict.
Section 4: This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after its passage and
publication as provided by law.
Passed and approved by the City Council and approved by the Mayor of the City of Gooding,
County of Gooding, State of Idaho, this 3rd day of December, 2018.
CITY OF GOODING
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.

ORDINANCE NO. 708
AN ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF GOODING, STATEOF IDAHO, A MUNICIPAL
CORPORATION, REPEALING CITYORDINANCE NUMBER 670, AND REPEALING CITY
ORDINANCE NUMBER 475; CREATING AND ESTABLISHING A COMMISSION TO BE KNOWN
AS THE GOODING AIRPORT COMMISSION; PROVIDING FOR THE APPOINTMENT OF
MEMBERSTO THE COMMISSION; FIXING AND DETERMINING THE NUMBER OF MEMBERS;
PROVIDING FOR THE ORGANIZATION THEREOF; FIXING AND DESCRIBING THE DUTIES
AND AUTHORITY OF SAID COMMISSION; REPEALING CONFLICTING ORDINANCES; AND
PROVIDING AN EFFECTIVE DATE.
NOW, THEREFORE, be ordained by the Mayor and City Council of the City of Gooding,
State of Idaho as follows:
Section 1: That Gooding CityOrdinance Number 670 and GoodingCity Ordinance Number
475 be repealed in their entirety.
Section 2: The Gooding Airport Commission is hereby created and established.
Section 3: The Mayor with the consent of the Council may appoint a Gooding Airport
Commission consisting of five members. Members should include at least two active pilots and
three members representing business interests suchas agriculture, medical,banking, manufacturing
or any other business. Such members shall hold their office for three years from the date of their
appointment, and until their successors are appointed, but upon their first appointment they shall
divide themselves at their firstmeeting by lot,into three classes:Two members shallform the first
class and shall servefor one year;Two members shall form the second classand shall servefor two
years; One member shallform the thirdclass and shallserve for threeyears. No compensation shall
be paid or allowed any member of the Commission, but actual and necessary expense may be
allowed with prior approval of the City Council.
Section 4: The duties of the Commission shall be advisory and shall include:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 3/336
A. Annual reviewof operations and maintenance functions with
emphasis on safetyand compliance with FAA regulations.
B. Annual review of the Airport Capital Improvement Plan.
C. Recommend and promote compatible development of the Gooding
Airport.
Report to the Mayor and Council at a regularly scheduled Council meetingon a quarterly basis or more
oftenas needed or appropriate.
Section5: All Ordinances, Resolutions, and parts thereof,in conflict with the provisions of this
Ordinance, to the extent of such conflict, are hereby repealed.
Section 6: This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after its passage and
publication.
Passed by the City Councilof the City of Gooding,County of Gooding,State of Idaho, this 4th
day of February, 2019.
CITY OF GOODING
By: /s/ Jeff Brekke

/s/ Hollye Lierman
PREFACE
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 4/336
This City Code of the City of Gooding, as supplemented, contains ordinances up to and including
ordinance 703, passed April 3, 2017. Ordinances of the City adopted after said ordinance supersede
the provisions of this City Code to the extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult
the City office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the Code has been amended,
superseded or repealed.
The Gooding City Code has been kept current by regular supplementation. In 2005, Sterling Codifiers
began providing supplement service for the City Code.
Sterling Codifiers
Coeur d'Alene, Idaho
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE NO. 437
AN ORDINANCE PROVIDING FOR THE REVISING, COMPILING AND CODIFYING OF THE
GENERAL ORDINANCES OF THE CITY OF GOODING AND PROVIDING FOR THE ADOPTION OF
SUCH REVISION.
BE IT ORDAINED by the Mayor and City Council of the City of Gooding, Gooding County, Idaho:
Section 1: That all ordinances of a general nature now in force in the City of Gooding, Gooding
County, Idaho, as revised, codified and compiled and hereinafter set forth, be, and they are hereby
adopted, passed, published and declared to be the compiled ordinances of the City of Gooding,
pursuant to Chapter 9 of Title 50 of the Idaho Code, empowering any city to revise, codify and compile
its ordinances.
Section 2: That this Ordinance and all said Ordinances of a general nature compiled and codified as
above stated, shall be in full force and effect upon the passage, approval and publication of this
Ordinance in one issue of the official newspaper of the City.
PASSED and APPROVED this 6th day of July, 1970.
Title 1
ADMINISTRATIVE
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 5/336
Chapter 1
OFFICIAL CODE
1-1-1: TITLE:
Upon adoption by the City Council of the City of Gooding, this City Code, is hereby declared to be and
shall hereafter constitute the official City Code of the City of Gooding. Any reference made to the
number of any section contained herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the same
number, its appropriate chapter and title heading, and to the general penalty clause relating thereto,
as well as to the section itself, when reference is made to this City Code by title in any legal document.
(1970 Code)
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
This City Code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received without further proof
in all courts and in all administrative tribunals of this State as the ordinances of the City of a general
and permanent effect. (1970 Code)
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
Any ordinance amending this City Code shall set forth the title, chapter and section number of the
section or sections to be amended, and this shall constitute a sufficient compliance with any statutory
requirement pertaining to the amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this City Code. All
such amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to the codifiers and the
said ordinance material shall be prepared for insertion in its proper place in each copy of this City
Code. Each such replacement page shall be properly identified and shall be inserted in each copy of
the City Code within thirty (30) days from the date of its final passage. (1970 Code)
1-1-4: CONSTRUCTION OF WORDS:
A. Whenever any word in any section of this City Code importing the plural number is used in
describing or referring to any matters, parties or persons, any single matter, party or person shall
be deemed to be included, although distributive words may not have been used.
B. When any subject matter, party or person is referred to in this City Code by words importing the
singular number only, or the masculine gender, several matters, parties or persons and females as
well as males and bodies corporate shall be deemed to be included; provided, that these rules of
construction shall not be applied to any section of this City Code which contains any express
provision excluding such construction or where the subject matter or content may be repugnant
thereto. (1970 Code)
1-1-5: INTERPRETATIONS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 6/336
In the determination of the provisions of each section of this Code the following rules shall be
observed:
A. Intent To Defraud: Whenever an intent to defraud is required in order to constitute an offense, it
shall be sufficient if an intent appears to defraud any person.
B. Liability Of Employers And Agents: When the provisions of any section of this City Code prohibits
the commission of an act, not only the person actually doing the prohibited act or omitting the
directed act, but also the employer and all other persons concerned with or in aiding or abetting the
said person shall be guilty of the offense described and liable to the penalty set forth. (1970 Code)
Chapter 2
SAVING CLAUSE
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
All general ordinances of the City passed prior to the adopting date of this City Code are hereby
repealed, except such as referred to herein as being still in force or are by necessary implication
herein reserved from repeal (subject to the saving clauses contained in the following section), from
which are excluded the following ordinances which are not hereby repealed: sales and use tax
ordinances; tax levy ordinances; appropriation ordinances; ordinances relating to boundaries and
annexations; franchise ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to persons or
corporations, contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a contract or the
issuance of warrants; salary ordinances; ordinances establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or
other public places; improvement ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances relating to elections;
ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the City, and all special
ordinances. (1970 Code)
1-2-2: PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroads or railroad crossings with streets and other public ways, or relating
to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public utilities shall be repealed by virtue of the adoption of
this City Code or by virtue of the preceding section, excepting as this City Code may contain
provisions for such matters, in which case this City Code shall be considered as amending such
ordinance or ordinances in respect of such provision only. (1970 Code)
1-2-3: COURT PROCEEDINGS:
A. No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a former ordinance, whether such former
ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as to any offense committed against such former ordinance
or as to any act done, any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued or
claim arising under the former ordinance, or in any way. whatever to affect any such offense or act
so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so incurred or any right accrued
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 7/336
or claim arising before the new ordinance takes effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter
shall conform to the ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding, so far as practicable.
B. If any penalty, forfeiture or punishment be mitigated by any provision of a new ordinance, such
provision may be by the consent of the party affected, applied to any judgment announced after
the new ordinance takes effect.
C. This Section shall extend to all repeals, either by express words or implication, whether the repeal
is in the ordinance making any new provisions upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
D. Nothing contained in this Chapter shall be construed as abating any action now pending under or
by virtue of any general ordinance of the City herein repealed and the provisions of all general
ordinances contained in this Code shall be deemed to be continuing provisions and not a new
enactment of the same provision; nor shall this Chapter be deemed as discontinuing, abating,
modifying or altering any penalty accrued or to accrue, or as affecting the liability of any person,
firm or corporation, or as waiving any right of the City under any ordinance or provision thereof in
force at the time of the adoption of this City Code. (1970 Code)
1-2-4: HEADLINES:
The headlines of the several sections of this Code are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the
contents of the section and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections, nor as any part
of the section, nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such sections,
including the headlines, are amended or reenacted. (1970 Code)
1-2-5: AMENDMENTS:
Any additions or amendments to this Code, when passed as ordinances amending this Code, and
which indicate the intention of the Council to make the same a part hereof, shall be deemed to be
incorporated in this Code so that a reference to the Code shall be understood as including them.
(1970 Code)
Chapter 3
DEFINITIONS
1-3-1: DEFINITIONS, GENERAL:
Whenever the following words or terms are used in this Code they shall have the meanings herein
ascribed to them, unless the content makes such meaning repugnant thereto:
AGENT: A person acting on behalf of another.
CITY: The City of Gooding, in the County of Gooding, State of Idaho, except as otherwise provided.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 8/336
CODE: Unless otherwise specifically stated shall mean this City Code.
COMPUTATION OF TIME: The time within which any act provided by law is to be done shall be
computed by excluding the first day and including the last, unless the last day is Sunday or a legal
holiday, and then it shall also be excluded. If the day succeeding such Sunday or holiday is also a
holiday or a Sunday, then such succeeding day shall also be excluded.
COUNCIL: The City Council of the City of Gooding, Idaho.
EMPLOYEES: Whenever reference is made in this Code to a City employee by title only, this shall be
construed as though followed by the words "of the City of Gooding".
FEE: A sum of money charged by the City for the carrying on of a business, profession or occupation.
GENDER: Words importing the masculine gender shall include the feminine and neuter.
KNOWINGLY: A word importing only a knowledge that the facts exist which brings the act or omission
within the provisions of this Code. It does not require any knowledge of the unlawfulness of such act
or omission.
LICENSE: The permission granted for the carrying on of a business, profession or occupation.
MISDEMEANOR: Any offense deemed a violation of the provisions of this Code which is a lesser
offense than a felony or an infraction as defined by State law.
NEGLIGENT: The word "negligent" as well as "neglect", "negligence", and "negligently" imports a want
of such attention to the nature or probable consequences of the act or omission as a prudent man
ordinarily bestows in acting in his own concern.
NUISANCE: Anything offensive or obnoxious to the health and welfare of the inhabitants of the City; or
any act or thing repugnant to, or creating a hazard to, or having a detrimental effect on the property of
another person or to the community.
OCCUPANT: As applied to a building or land shall include any person who occupies the whole or any
part of such building or land whether alone or with others.
OFFENSE: Any act forbidden by any provision of this Code or the omission of any act required by the
provisions of this Code.
OFFICERS: Whenever reference is made in this Code to a City officer by title only, this shall be
construed as though followed by the words "of the City of Gooding".
OPERATOR: The person who is in charge of any operation, business or profession.
OWNER: As applied to a building or land, this term shall include any part owner, joint owner, tenant in
common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of such building or land.
PERSON: This term shall include the singular and the plural and shall also mean and include any
person, firm, corporation, association, partnership or any other form of association or organization.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Shall include every description of money, goods, chattels, effects, evidence
of rights in action and all written instruments by which any pecuniary obligation, right or title to property
is created, acknowledged, transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished and every right
or interest therein.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 9/336
RETAILER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, this term shall be understood to relate to the sale of
goods, merchandise, articles or things in small quantities sold direct to the consumer.
SIDEWALK: That portion of a street between the curb lines or the lateral lines of a roadway and the
adjacent property lines, intended for the use of pedestrians.
STREET: Includes alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public squares, public places and
sidewalks.
TENANT: As applied to a building or land shall include any person who occupies the whole or any part
of such building or land whether alone or with others.
WHOLESALER: The words "wholesaler" and "wholesale dealer" as used in this Code, unless
otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to relate to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles
or things in quantity to persons who purchase for the purpose of resale.
WILFULLY: When applied to the intent with which an act is done or omitted, implies simply a purpose
or willingness to commit the act or make the omission referred to. It does not require any intent to
violate law, or to injure another, or to acquire an advantage.
WRITTEN, IN WRITING: The words "written" or "in writing" may include printing and any other mode
of presenting words and letters, but when the written signature of any person is required by law to any
official or public writing or bond required by law, it shall be in proper handwriting of such person, or in
case he is unable to write, by his proper mark. (1970 Code)
Chapter 4
PENALTY
1-4-1: PENALTY:
Any person convicted of a violation of any section of this Code shall be fined in a sum not to exceed
three hundred dollars ($300.00) for any one offense and such person may be confined in the City jail
for a period of not more than six (6) months. (Ord. 528, 12-15-1980)
1-4-2: DEFAULT:
Any person in default of payment of any fine imposed shall be imprisoned in the City jail for a period of
one day for each five dollars ($5.00) of such fine. (1970 Code)
1-4-3: DRIVING WHILE INTOXICATED:
(Rep. by Ord. 528, 12-15-1980)
1-4-4: LABOR:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 10/336
Any person imprisoned under the provisions of this Chapter may be put to work for the benefit of the
City for the term of his imprisonment.
No female prisoner shall be required to work in public, nor shall any prisoner be required to work on
Sunday. (1970 Code)
1-4-5: LICENSE:
When a person is convicted of a violation of any section of this Code, any license previously issued to
him by the City may be revoked by the court or by the governing body of the City. (1970 Code)
1-4-6: APPLICATION:
The penalty provided in this Chapter shall be applicable to every section of this Code the same as
though it were a part of each and every separate section. Any person convicted of a violation of any
section of this Code, where any duty is prescribed or obligation imposed, or where any act which is of
a continuing nature is forbidden or declared to be unlawful, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor.
A separate offense shall be deemed committed upon each day such duty or obligation remains
unperformed or such act continues, unless otherwise specifically provided in this Code. (1970 Code)
1-4-7: RECKLESS DRIVING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to recklessly, carelessly or heedlessly or without due caution and
circumspection or in a manner so as to endanger or to be likely to endanger any person or property,
ride any horse or other animal, or any bicycle or motorcycle, or drive any automobile, motor vehicle or
other vehicle in whatsoever manner propelled, upon any street, alley or sidewalk of the City. (Ord.
365, 11-21-1955)
Chapter 5
MAYOR
1-5-1: ELECTION; DUTIES:
A. Election: The Mayor shall be elected for a period of four (4) years, and he shall take office at the
time and in the manner provided for installation of Councilmen and shall have the qualifications as
prescribed by the laws of the State of Idaho.
B. Duties: The Mayor shall be the chief administrative official of the City, preside over the meetings of
the City Council and determine the order of business subject to such rules as the Council may
prescribe, have a vote only when the Council is equally divided, have the superintending control of
all the officers and affairs of the City, preserve order and take care that the provisions of this Code
are complied with and enforced. (Ord. 432, 8-4-1969)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 11/336
1-5-2: CONTRACT:
The Mayor is authorized and empowered to sign his name officially for and in behalf of the
Municipality on all contracts, documents and papers to which the Municipality is a party, and to require
that the conditions in any instrument are faithfully performed. He may borrow money on the credit of
the Municipality when so authorized by the Council. (1970 Code)
1-5-3: REWARD:
The Mayor, whenever he deems it expedient, is hereby empowered to offer a reward not exceeding
one hundred dollars ($100.00) for the arrest and conviction of any person charged with violating any of
the provisions of this Code. (1970 Code)
1-5-4: PARDONS:
The Mayor is empowered to grant a pardon to any person imprisoned for a violation of any of the
provisions of this Code, and to remit so much of any fine or forfeiture as in his judgment he may deem
just and reasonable, and he shall report such remittance or pardon to the Council at its next meeting.
(1970 Code)
1-5-5: VETO POWER:
The Mayor shall have power to veto or sign any ordinance passed by the Council; provided, that any
ordinance vetoed by the Mayor may be passed over his veto by a vote of two-thirds (2/3) of the
members of the Council, and should the Mayor neglect or refuse to sign any ordinance, the same shall
become law without his signature after the next regular meeting of the Council. (1970 Code)
1-5-6: ACCOUNTS OF OFFICERS:
The Mayor shall have the power to require any officer of the Municipality to exhibit his accounts or
other papers and to make reports to the Council in writing on any subject or matter pertaining to the
office. (1970 Code)
1-5-7: POLICE POWER:
The Mayor shall have jurisdiction over all places within five (5) miles of the corporate limits of the
Municipality for the enforcement of any health or quarantine ordinance and regulation and shall have
jurisdiction in all matters, excepting taxation, within one-half ('/2) mile of the corporate limits of the
Municipality. (1970 Code)
1-5-8: MAY REQUIRE AID:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 12/336
The Mayor is hereby authorized to call on every male inhabitant of the Municipality over the age of
eighteen (18) and under the age of fifty (50) years to aid in enforcing the law. (1970 Code)
1-5-9: OTHER POWERS:
The Mayor shall have all other powers provided by State statute or by specific provisions of this Code.
(1970 Code)
Chapter 6
COUNCIL
1-6-1: ELECTION:
The legislative authority of the City shall be vested in a Council consisting of four (4) members, onehalf
(1/2) of whom shall be elected at each general City election and which said Councilmen shall be
elected at large and shall have the qualifications as prescribed by the laws of the State of Idaho and
each such Councilman shall hold office for a term of four (4) years and until his successor is elected
and qualified. (Ord. 432, 8-4-1969)
1-6-2: VACANCIES:
In the event an office of Councilman shall become vacant through death, removal of residence, or for
any other cause, the Mayor shall appoint with the approval of the Council, a resident of the City to fill
the unexpired portion of the term to serve until the next general election, at which time the unexpired
term shall be filled by regular election. (1970 Code)
1-6-3: TIME AND PLACE OF MEETING:
The Council shall hold regular sessions in the Municipal Hall on the first and third Monday of each
month at seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. (Ord. 593, 11-21-1994)
1-6-4: HOW TO CONDUCT COUNCIL MEETINGS:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing rules and regulations for the conduct of
Council meetings, the book entitled "How to Conduct a Municipal Council Meeting" prepared by the
Idaho Municipal League and published by Sterling Codifiers, Inc., three (3) copies of which shall be on
file in the office of the Clerk, and the same is hereby adopted and incorporated as fully as if set out at
length herein. (1970 Code)
1-6-5: ELECT PRESIDENT OF THE COUNCIL:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 13/336
At the time of taking office, the Council shall elect one of its members President of the Council who
shall preside at all meetings of the Council and perform all other duties of the Mayor in the absence of
the Mayor; and, in the absence of the President of the Council shall elect one of their members to
occupy his place temporarily, who shall be styled Acting President of the Council, and the President
and Acting President, when occupying the place of Mayor, shall have the same privileges as other
members of the Council and all actions of the President and Acting President, while so acting, shall be
binding upon the Council and the Municipality as if performed by the Mayor. (1970 Code)
Chapter 7
APPOINTIVE OFFICERS
1-7-1: APPOINTMENTS:
The Mayor shall appoint, subject to approval of the Council, a Clerk, Attorney, Engineer, Police Chief,
Fire Chief, Treasurer and Superintendent. The Mayor may appoint, subject to approval by the Council
such other officers as may be deemed necessary for the efficient operation of the business of the City.
(1970 Code)
1-7-2: TERMS OF OFFICE:
All appointments shall be made for a specified term. (1970 Code)
1-7-3: REMOVAL FROM OFFICE:
Any appointed officer may be removed from office by the same authority and in the same manner as
he was originally appointed. (1970 Code)
1-7-4: BONDS OF OFFICERS:
Certain officers shall give bonds in favor of the Municipality with two (2) or more sureties, or surety
bonds may be furnished in lieu of personal bonds as follows:
Clerk $25,000.00
Treasurer 5,000.00
Deputy Clerk 25,000.00
Chief of Police 1,000.00
(Ord. 494, 2-22-1977; amd. Ord. 497, 7-18-1977)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 14/336
Chapter 8
CLERK
1-8-1: APPOINTMENT:
The Clerk shall be appointed by the Mayor subject to the approval of the Council. He shall hold office
for the duration of his appointment unless sooner removed by the Mayor with the concurrence of the
Council. (1970 Code)
1-8-2: DUTIES:
In all cases where the duty is not expressly charged to any other department or office, the Clerk shall
have supervision, control and responsibility of all of the records of the Municipality. He shall serve as
Clerk of the governing body and perform such other duties of a like nature as shall be required by that
body. (1970 Code)
1-8-3: RECORDS OF THE GOVERNING BODY:
The Clerk shall be responsible for the recording, filing, indexing and safekeeping of all proceedings of
the governing body and shall have published all proceedings, legal notices, ordinances and
resolutions that are required to be published by this Code or by State statute. (1970 Code)
1-8-4: ORDINANCES:
The Clerk shall record in full, uniformly and permanently, all ordinances and shall authenticate the
same. (1970 Code)
1-8-5: ELECTION RECORDS:
The Clerk shall keep and maintain all election records and have custody of all property used in
connection with elections. (1970 Code)
1-8-6: NOTIFY OF TERM EXPIRATIONS:
The Clerk shall notify the appointing authority of the impending expiration of the term of office of a
member of any board or commission at least thirty (30) days before the expiration of said term. (1970
Code)
1-8-7: OFFICIAL SEAL:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 15/336
The Clerk shall be the custodian of the official seal of the Municipality1. (1970 Code)
1-8-8: COPIES OF RECORDS:
The Clerk shall furnish to any member of the governing body a certified copy of any record or
document in his custody and he may furnish such a copy to any other person upon payment of a fee
to be determined by the governing body. (1970 Code)
1-8-9: COLLECTIONS TO TREASURER:
Within ten (10) days after the first day of each month the Clerk shall turn over to the Treasurer all
funds collected by him during the preceding month. (1970 Code)
1-8-10: LICENSES:
In all cases where the duty is not expressly charged to any other department or office, the Clerk shall
issue all licenses in accordance with the provisions of this Code. A record of all licenses issued,
including the name of the person to whom issued, the amount of the license fee and the purpose of
the license shall be kept by the Clerk. (1970 Code)
1-8-11: BONDS:
The Clerk shall keep a complete record of all out-standing bonds of the Municipality and report such
record regularly to the governing body. (1970 Code)
1-8-12: WARRANTS:
The Clerk shall countersign all warrants and keep a "Warrant Register and Abstract of Expenditures"
showing the number and amount of warrants issued and the person to whom issued, the date
redeemed, the interest paid and the several funds against which each of said warrants is drawn. (1970
Code)
1-8-13: CLAIMS:
All claims against the Municipality must be filed in writing with the Clerk. Claims must present a full
account of the items and must contain a verification under oath by the claimant to the effect that the
claim is correct, reasonable and just and that no part of said claim has been paid. All such claims must
be approved by the governing body before payment can be made. (1970 Code)
1-8-14: DAMAGES:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 16/336
All claims for damages against the Municipality must be filed with the Clerk within six (6) months after
such time as the damage is alleged to have occurred. All such claims shall specify the time, place,
character and cause of damage and no action shall be maintained against the Municipality for any
claim for damages until after sixty (60) days have elapsed after such presentation. Allowance of any
claim for damages against the Municipality shall be made only by ordinance. (1970 Code)
Chapter 9
ATTORNEY
1-9-1: APPOINTMENT:
The Attorney shall be appointed by the Mayor subject to the approval of the Council. He shall hold
office for the duration of his appointment unless sooner removed by the Mayor with the concurrence of
the Council. (1970 Code)
1-9-2: SUITS AND ACTIONS:
The Attorney shall prosecute or defend any and all suits or actions at law or equity to which the
Municipality may be a party, or in which it may be interested, or which may be brought against, or by,
any officer of the Municipality on behalf of the Municipality, or in the capacity of such person as an
officer of the Municipality. (1970 Code)
1-9-3: JUDGMENTS:
It shall be the duty of the Attorney to see to the full enforcement of all judgments or decrees rendered
or entered in favor of the Municipality, and of all similar interlocutory orders. (1970 Code)
1-9-4: ADVICE:
The Attorney shall be the legal advisor of the Municipality, and shall render advice on all legal
questions affecting the Municipality whenever requested to do so by any Municipal official. Upon
request by the Mayor or by the Council, he shall reduce any such opinion to writing. (1970 Code)
1-9-5: SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS:
It shall be the duty of the Attorney to see to the completion of all special assessment proceedings and
condemnation proceedings. (1970 Code)
1-9-6: ORDINANCES AND DOCUMENTS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 17/336
It shall be the duty of the Attorney to draft or supervise the phraseology of any contract, lease or other
documents or instruments, to which the Municipality may be a party; and upon request of the Council
to draft ordinances covering any subjects within the power of the Municipality. (1970 Code)
Chapter 10
CHIEF OF POLICE
1-10-1: APPOINTMENT:
The Chief of Police shall be appointed by the Mayor subject to the approval of the Council. He shall
hold office for the duration of his appointment unless sooner removed by the Mayor with the
concurrence of the Council. (1970 Code)
1-10-2: RANK:
The Chief of Police shall be the head of the Police Department and have supervision over all the
officers and members thereof. The Chief of Police may, with the approval of the Mayor, appoint such
special police as may be required from time to time; however, such appointment may not be for a
period of longer than ten (10) days and special police shall not be reappointed following the specified
ten (10) days without the consent of the Council. (1970 Code)
1-10-3: DUTIES OF CHIEF:
A. The Chief of Police shall keep such records and make such reports concerning the activities of his
Department as may be required by statute or by the Mayor. He shall be responsible for the
performance of the Police Department and of its functions and all persons who are members of the
Police Department shall serve subject to his orders.
B. It shall be the duty of the Chief of Police to see to the enforcement of all provisions of this Code and
of all applicable statutes and to preserve order and prevent infractions of the law and arrest
violators thereof. He shall have authority to call upon any citizen or bystander to assist him in the
execution of his duty. He shall serve all processes issued to him and enforce all orders and
judgments of the Court. (1970 Code)
1-10-4: STOLEN PROPERTY:
The Chief of Police shall have the custody of all lost, abandoned or stolen property recovered within
the Municipality. (1970 Code)
Chapter 11
CITY ENGINEER
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 18/336
1-11-1: APPOINTMENT:
The Mayor may appoint, with the approval of the Council, an Engineer who shall hold his office for the
duration of his appointment or until such time as he may be removed by the Mayor with the
concurrence of the Council. (1970 Code)
1-11-2: PUBLIC WORKS APPROVAL:
The Engineer shall approve all public works and all plans and specifications for public works,
construction for which the expenditure will be two thousand dollars ($2,000.00) or more, except that
the Engineer's direct supervision and approval must be obtained on all work where the public health or
safety is involved. (1970 Code)
1-11-3: QUALIFICATIONS:
Any person appointed as Engineer shall be a competent engineer and surveyor and shall be duly
licensed as such by the State of Idaho. (1970 Code)
Chapter 12
TREASURER
1-12-1: APPOINTMENT:
The Treasurer shall be appointed by the Mayor subject to the approval of the Council. He shall hold
office for the duration of his appointment unless sooner removed by the Mayor with the concurrence of
the Council. (1970 Code)
1-12-2: DUTIES:
In all cases where the duty is not expressly charged to any other department or office, the Treasurer
shall act to promote, secure and preserve the financial and property interest of the Municipality. He
shall safely keep in designated depositories all funds belonging to the Municipality and all other
securities in safety deposit boxes of an approved institution designated by the Council. (1970 Code)
1-12-3: ACCOUNTS:
The Treasurer shall keep in proper books a full and accurate account of all the monies received and
disbursed by him in behalf of the Municipality, specifying the time of receipt and disbursement, from
whom received and to whom disbursed, and on what account received and disbursed, and how paid.
(1970 Code)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 19/336
1-12-4: MONIES:
The Treasurer shall receive and have custody of all monies paid to the Municipality and shall disburse
monies upon the official warrant or check of the Municipality when so ordered by the Council. (1970
Code)
1-12-5: COLLECTIONS:
The Treasurer shall demand and receive all monies and fees owning to the Municipality whenever any
person is indebted to the Municipality in any manner, and the means of collection of such debt is not
otherwise provided for by law. When any claim shall not be collectible by other means, he shall report
the same to the Attorney for prosecution. (1970 Code)
1-12-6: WARRANTS:
Warrants shall be paid by the Treasurer from funds available in the order in which the warrants are
presented for payment. When a warrant is presented for payment and no funds are available, the
Treasurer shall plainly mark the warrant "Not Paid for Want of Funds" and enter the same in a book
maintained for such purpose which shall be known as the "Warrant Register". Such warrants shall
bear interest at the rate of six percent (6%) per annum from the date of presentation until paid.
Warrants shall be called for payment in the order in which they were presented whenever sufficient
funds are available to the Treasurer to make such payment. (1970 Code)
1-12-7: CANCELLATION OF WARRANTS:
The Treasurer shall cancel all warrants and other evidences of debt against the Municipality,
whenever paid by him, by writing or stamping across the face thereof the words "Paid By The
Treasurer" with the date of payment written or stamped thereon. These warrants and evidences of
debt, so cancelled, shall be delivered immediately to the Clerk. (1970 Code)
1-12-8: MONTHLY REPORT:
The Treasurer shall make a detailed report to the Council during the first week of each month showing
the business of his office during the month preceding, showing the balance on hand to the credit of the
different funds, the amounts received during the month, and on what account, together with such other
information as may be required by the Council. (1970 Code)
1-12-9: QUARTERLY REPORT:
The Treasurer shall cause to be published for at least one insertion in a newspaper of general
circulation in the Municipality a full statement of the receipts and expenditures of the Municipality,
showing sources of revenue and disposition of funds. This quarterly report shall be published before
the third Monday of the months of April, July, October and January. (1970 Code)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 20/336
1-12-10: DELIVERY TO SUCCESSOR:
The Treasurer shall deliver to his successor in office all materials, records, and resources of the office.
(1970 Code)
1-12-11: DEPOSITORY:
The First Security Bank of Idaho, N.A., Gooding Branch and the Bank of Idaho, Gooding Branch, are
hereby designated as the official depositories for the City. (1970 Code)
Chapter 13
WARDS
1-13-1: WARDS:
The city shall be divided into two (2) wards. All that part of the city being on the east side of Main
Street shall be known and designated as the first ward and all that part of the city being on the west
side of Main Street shall be known and designated as the second ward. (1947 Code § 1-201)
Chapter 14
SALARIES
1-14-1: SALARIES OF ELECTED OFFICIALS:
Commencing January 1, 2016, the salaries of the elected officials of the city shall be as follows:
Mayor $800.00 per month
Councilmen 600.00 per month
(Ord. 695, 8-17-2015)
1-14-2: SALARIES OF APPOINTIVE OFFICERS:
The mayor, together with the approval and consent of the council, shall from time to time adopt a
schedule and fix the salaries and rates of compensation for all appointive officers and other
employees of the city. (Ord. 432, 8-4-1969)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 21/336
Chapter 15
SEAL
1-15-1: CORPORATE SEAL; DESIGN:
The Corporate Seal of the City shall be circular in form, with an inner and an outer circle. The outer
circle shall be one and seven-eighths inches (17/8") in diameter and it shall bear upon the space
between the two (2) circles the words "City of Gooding, Gooding County, Idaho", and upon the space
within the inner circle the words "Incorporated Nov. 21, 1910" and across the center of the Seal shall
be the word "Seal". (1970 Code)
1-15-2: ADOPTION OF SEAL:
The Seal herein above described is hereby adopted as the Corporate Seal of the City of Gooding,
Gooding County, Idaho. (1970 Code)
1-15-3: CUSTODIAN:
The Clerk shall be custodian of the Corporate Seal and shall affix said Seal's imprint upon all official
documents, records, licenses, warrants and/or checks. (1970 Code)
Chapter 16
CLAIMS AND WARRANTS
1-16-1: TIME FOR FILING:
Any person having claims against the city shall file the same with the clerk on the Friday before the
next regular meeting of the council. Such claims or accounts shall be verified, stating the item in detail
and for what and when the same accrued, and every claim or account shall contain all the items of
account and demands which claimant has against the city up to the time of filing the same. (1947
Code § 1-601)
1-16-2: BILLS ALLOWED:
No bill shall be allowed or warrants ordered drawn except at the first monthly meeting of the council,
unless such delay will cause service termination or cause the city to incur a penalty. (Ord. 669, 5-17-
2010)
1-16-3: TIME FOR PRESENTATION:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 22/336
No claim against the city will be allowed by the council unless the same is presented within six (6)
months after the same becomes due and payable. (1947 Code § 1-603)
1-16-4: WARRANTS:
All claims and accounts against the city shall be paid by a warrant on the treasurer, signed both by the
mayor and city clerk and having the seal of the city thereon. (1947 Code § 1-604)
1-16-5: PAYMENT OF WARRANTS:
All warrants shall be presented to the treasurer for payment. If there shall not be sufficient funds in the
fund or funds upon which the warrants have been drawn to pay the same, the treasurer shall register
such warrants, and they shall thereafter be paid in the order of their registration. (1947 Code § 1-605)
1-16-6: RATE OF INTEREST ON REGISTERED WARRANTS:
All warrants issued by authority of the council which are presented for payment and not paid for want
of funds shall bear interest at the rate of six percent (6%) per annum from and after their date of
registration to ten (10) days after the date such warrants are called for payment, at which time the
interest shall cease, unless the warrants have been paid before the expiration of the said ten (10)
days. (1947 Code § 1-606)
Chapter 17
ELECTIONS
1-17-1: ELECTION OF OFFICERS:
The council shall, at its first regular meeting in October, prior to each biennial election, appoint four (4)
capable and discreet persons, possessing the qualification of electors, for each polling place as
election officers. Two (2) of such persons shall be designated as judges of election and two (2) of such
persons shall be designated as clerks of election. (1947 Code § 1-1001)
1-17-2: TERM:
Such officials shall hold office for the period of two (2) years and shall be the officials of all elections,
both general and special, during that period. (1947 Code § 1-1002)
1-17-3: NOTICE OF APPOINTMENT; DECLINATION:
The clerk shall give such appointees notice of their appointment and shall request each appointee to
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 23/336
give notice of his acceptance or declination of his appointment to the clerk within ten (10) days
thereafter. (1947 Code § 1-1003)
1-17-4: VACANCIES:
Any vacancies arising in the office of election officials shall be filled by the council at any regular
meeting or at any special meeting called for that purpose. If such vacancy does not become apparent
until the time of the opening of the polls, the qualified electors present may fill such vacancies from
any electors present. (1947 Code § 1-1004)
1-17-5: POLLING PLACES:
A. Supplies: The council shall designate suitable polling places and cause the same to be provided
with suitable voting compartments, supplies, official stamps, ballot boxes and such other supplies
as county commissioners are required to provide for state elections. (1947 Code § 1-1005; amd.
Ord. 646, 9-19-2005)
B. Hours: The polls for all general and special city elections shall be open from twelve o'clock (12:00)
noon Mountain Time and remain open until eight o'clock (8:00) P.M. Mountain Time. (Ord. 646, 9-
19-2005)
1-17-6: COMPENSATION:
The compensation of judges and clerks of election shall be such amounts as may be from time to time
fixed and determined by the council. (1947 Code § 1-1006)
1-17-7: PRECINCT:
The city of Gooding shall be comprised of one precinct. (Ord. 646, 9-19-2005)
Chapter 18
INSPECTORS
1-18-1: ELECTRICAL INSPECTOR:
The Council shall have the power to appoint some person qualified and experienced in electrical work
to be Electrical Inspector who shall hold said office at the discretion of the Mayor and Council. (3-301;
1947 Code)
1-18-2: DUTIES OF ELECTRICAL INSPECTOR:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 24/336
It shall be the duty of the Electrical Inspector to attend to the enforcement of the provisions of this
Code as same shall pertain to the inspection and supervision of all electrical wiring within the limits of
the City. He shall render to the Clerk within two (2) days thereafter, a written report of each inspection
made by him, the report to be in such form as shall be prescribed by the Council. One copy of such
report shall be by him furnished to the contractor, owner or person for whom the inspection is made
(3-302. 1947 Code)
1-18-3: NONCOMPLYING INSTALLATIONS:
If the report be that the installation is not up to the established standard, the contractor or owner or
person for whom the inspection is made, shall alter the installation so that it shall comply therewith. A
reinspection shall then be asked for in the same form as a first inspection and a like report made by
the Electrical Inspector. (3-303; 1947 Code)
1-18-4: PLUMBING INSPECTOR; APPOINTMENT:
There is hereby created the office of Plumbing Inspector. The Mayor by and with the approval of the
Council shall appoint a competent person to fill the office of Plumbing Inspector and he shall perform
such duties as shall be prescribed by the provisions of this Code or orders of the Mayor and Council.
(3-402; 1947 Code)
1-18-5: BUILDING INSPECTOR:
There is hereby created the office of Building Inspector. The Mayor, with the consent and approval of a
majority of the Council, shall appoint a competent person to fill the office of Building Inspector and he
shall perform such duties as shall be prescribed by the provisions of this Code, by the provisions of
the Uniform Building Code or as may be prescribed by the Mayor and Council. (1970 Code)
1-18-6: SALARIES:
All inspectors appointed by the Mayor in accordance with the provisions of this Chapter shall receive
such compensation as may be determined by the Council and as provided in the annual appropriation
bill. (1970 Code)

OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER

1-19-1: OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER DESIGNATED:
The Times-News, a daily newspaper with general circulation within the city is designated and

Chapter 20
CAPITAL IMPROVEMENTS FUND
1-20-1: ESTABLISHMENT OF FUND:
There is hereby established a capital improvements fund of the city for the purpose of the purchase of
new equipment or real property, replacement, care and maintenance of existing equipment, necessary
for the continued efficient use of the sewer system, waterworks, streets, parks, recreational and other
integral facilities of the city. (Ord. 553, 8-17-1987)
1-20-2: TAX LEVIED:
There is hereby levied a special tax in the amount of four (4) mills, pursuant to the provisions of
section 50-236, Idaho Code, on all taxable property within the city for the establishment of such fund,
annually, until such fund shall aggregate the sum of money which is equivalent to four tenths of one
percent (0.4%) of the market value for assessment purposes of the city. (Ord. 553, 8-17-1987)
Chapter 21
POLICE JUDGE
(Rep. by Ord. 497, 7-18-1977)
Chapter 22
INITIATIVE AND REFERENDUM
1-22-1: CREATION OF RIGHT:
The people of this City shall have the right to enact ordinances through the initiative process, and to
repeal ordinances through the referendum process, according to the procedures set forth herein. (Ord.
511, 3-5-1979)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 26/336
1-22-2: NUMBER OF PETITIONERS REQUIRED:
To enact an ordinance by initiative or to repeal an ordinance by referendum, there shall be attached or
appended to the petition the signatures of the legal voters of the City equal to at least twenty percent
(20%) of the total number of voters registered to vote at the last general election in the City. (Ord. 511,
3-5-1979)
1-22-3: TIME FOR FILING PETITIONS:
Referendum petitions with the requisite number of signatures attached shall be filed with the City Clerk
not less than sixty (60) days following the final adoption of the ordinance to be subject to referendum.
(Ord. 511, 3-5-1979)
1-22-4: TIME FOR ELECTION:
A special election for initiative or referendum shall be provided not more than ninety (90) days
following the certification of the petition, provided that in the event a Municipal election will occur within
ninety (90) days, the initiative and referendum shall be submitted at the time of the Municipal election.
(Ord. 511, 3-5-1979)
1-22-5: REQUIREMENTS FOR SIGNATURE, VERIFICATION OF VALID PETITIONS,
PRINTING OF PETITION AND TIME LIMITS:
Referendum and initiative petitions shall conform with the requirements for signature, verification of
valid petitions, printing of petitions and time limits, except as expressly modified to meet the purposes
of initiative and referendum to be as nearly as practicable as provided in sections 34-1701 through 34-
1705, Idaho Code. (Ord. 511, 3-5-1979)
Title 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
Chapter 1
BOARD OF ADJUSTMENT
2-1-1: ORGANIZATION; MEMBERS:
There shall be a Board of Adjustment consisting of the members of the Council and Mayor each of
whom shall have an equal vote. The Board of Adjustment shall appoint a Building Inspector who shall
serve at the pleasure of the Board. (Ord. 417, 11-8-1966)
2-1-2: DUTIES AND POWERS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 27/336
The Board shall adopt such rules and regulations as it may deem necessary to carry into effect the
provisions of Title 11, Zoning, of this Code. Meetings shall be held at such times as may be necessary.
The Board shall keep minutes of its proceedings, showing the vote of each member upon every
question. Such Board shall hear and decide appeals from and review any order, requirement, decision
or determination made by the Building Inspector under the provisions of this Code. (Ord. 388, 6-20-
1960)
2-1-3: VOTING:
The concurring vote of three (3) members of the Board shall be necessary to reverse any order,
requirement, decision or determination made by the Building Inspector or to effect any variance
provided by this Code. (Ord. 388, 6-20-1960)
2-1-4: SPECIAL PERMITS; FEES:
Application for a special permit shall be filed with the Building Inspector in writing, together with all
facts bearing on the proposed occupancy or variance. The applicant shall pay to the Building
Inspector a filing fee of ten dollars ($10.00), except that in all cases where it is necessary to have an
ownership or radius plat prepared, when the value of any construction connected therewith exceeds
two thousand five hundred dollars ($2,500.00), the applicant shall pay the Building Inspector a filing
fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00). The Building Inspector shall forthwith transmit to the secretary of
the Board all papers with reference to the proposal. The Board shall cause a public hearing to be held
before such permit is acted upon. Notice of the time and place of such hearing shall be published in
the official paper of the City, one time at least fifteen (15) days before such hearing; provided,
however, the holding of a public hearing shall be within the discretion of the Board of Adjustment.
(Ord. 388, 6-20-1960; amd. Ord. 417, 11-8-1966)
2-1-5: SPECIFIC CASES:
When in its judgment the public convenience and welfare will be substantially served or the
appropriate use of neighboring property will not be substantially or permanently injured, or when there
are practical difficulties or unnecessary hardship in the carrying out the strict letter of the zoning
provisions of this Code, the Board of Adjustment may, in specific cases, after public notice and
hearing and subject to appropriate conditions and safeguards, determine and vary the application of
the regulations established in Title 11, Zoning, of this Code in harmony with their general purpose and
intent. (Ord. 388, 6-20-1960)
2-1-6: APPEALS:
Any decision of the Building Inspector or his duly authorized representative made in the enforcement
of the zoning provisions of this Code may be appealed to the Board of Adjustment by any person
affected by such decision. The appellant shall file with the secretary of the Board a notice of appeal,
specifying the ground thereof and a copy of such notice with the Building Inspector, together with a
filing fee of ten dollars ($10.00). The Building Inspector shall forthwith transmit to the Board all the
papers constituting the record upon which the appeal is taken. The Board shall fix a reasonable time
for the hearing of the appeal and give due notice thereof to the parties, and decide the same within a
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 28/336
reasonable time. Upon hearing, any party may appear in person or by agent or attorney. The Board
may reverse or affirm, wholly or partly, or modify the order, requirement, decision or determination, if,
in its opinion such changes ought to be made in the premises, and to that end shall have all the power
of the Building Inspector. (Ord. 388, 6-20-1960)
Chapter 2
LIBRARY BOARD
2-2-1: APPOINTMENT; TERM OF OFFICE:
The Mayor with the consent of the Council may appoint a Library Board consisting of five (5)
members, one of which shall be a member of the Council and one a nonvoting, ex-officio member,
who may, at the time of appointment be under twenty one (21) years of age. Such members shall hold
their office for five (5) years from the date of appointment, and until their successors are appointed. No
compensation shall be paid or allowed to any member of the Library Board in any manner whatsoever.
The youth member shall be appointed for a term up to one year and may be reappointed up to four (4)
successive terms. (Ord. 614, 5-15-2000)
2-2-2: ORGANIZATION AND POWERS:
Said Board shall, immediately after their appointment meet, and organize by the election of one of
their number President, and by the election of such other officers as they may deem necessary. They
shall make and adopt such rules and regulations as may be expedient. They shall have exclusive
control of the expenditure of all monies collected and the supervision, care and custody of all buildings
used for library purposes. They may appoint a librarian and assistants and prescribe rules for their
conduct. (1970 Code)
2-2-3: DAMAGING OR RETAINING LIBRARY PROPERTY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully or intentionally cut, tear, deface, break, injure or destroy
any book, map, chart or other property belonging to the public library.
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully retain any property belonging to the public library for more
than thirty (30) days after notice in writing to return the same given after the expiration of the time
within which, by the rules of such library, such article or property may be kept. (1970 Code)
This section has been affected by a recently passed ordinance, 708 - AIRPORT COMMISSION. Go to
new ordinance.
Chapter 3
GOODING AIRPORT COMMISSION
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.

2-3-1: GOODING AIRPORT COMMISSION:
Pursuant to the provisions of the Idaho Code and particularly, section 50-210, Idaho Code, the
Gooding Airport Commission is hereby created and established. (Ord 475, 4-7-1975)
This section has been affected by a recently passed ordinance, 708 - AIRPORT COMMISSION. Go to
new ordinance.
2-3-2: APPOINTMENT; TERM OF OFFICE:
The Mayor with the consent of the Council may appoint a Gooding Airport Commission consisting of
six (6) members, one of which shall be a member of the Council and one of which may be at the time
of his/her appointment under twenty one (21) years of age. Such members shall hold their office for
three (3) years from the date of appointment, and until their successors are appointed, but upon their
first appointment they shall divide themselves at their first meeting by lot, into three (3) classes: Two
(2) members shall form the first class and shall serve for one year; two (2) members shall form the
second class and shall serve for two (2) years; and one member shall form the third class and shall
serve for three (3) years. The youth member shall be appointed to a term of one year and may be
reappointed up to four (4) successive terms. No compensation shall be paid or allowed any member of
the said Commission, but actual and necessary expenses may be allowed with prior approval by the
Council. (Ord 614, 5-15-2000)

new ordinance.
2-3-3: ORGANIZATION:
Said Commission shall, immediately after their appointment meet, and organize by the election of one
of their number as chairman and by the election of such other officers as they may deem necessary.
They shall make and adopt such rules and regulations as may be expedient. They shall keep and
maintain a record of their acts and proceedings. (Ord 475, 4-7-1975)
