new ordinance.
2-3-4: DUTIES:
The duties of the commission shall be advisory in nature and shall include:
A. Review of the annual budget, to include:
1. Capital improvement program.
2. Operations and maintenance.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 30/336
B. Review operations and maintenance functions, to include:
1. Recommendation and review of airport specific regulations.
2. Conduct periodic safety inspections of the airport.
3. Receive credentials, establish qualifications, evaluate, and recommend hiring of airport
manager.
C. Review long range plan for airport development, to include:
1. Capital improvement program including federal-state-local funding anticipated.
2. Operations and maintenance plans.
3. Recommendation to local planning and zoning authority for protection of the airport through
zoning for obstructions and compatible land use.
4. Recommend and promote orderly but compatible development of adjacent land to its maximum
revenue generating capacity.
D. Provide liaison between airport users and city council. (Ord. 670, 7-6-2010)
Chapter 4
GOODING CITY PLANNING COMMISSION
2-4-1: CREATED:
There is hereby created and established a commission to be known as the "Gooding city planning
commission". (Ord. 464, 3-18-1974)
2-4-2: MEMBERSHIP; TERMS OF OFFICE:
A. Membership: The planning commission shall consist of five (5) members to be appointed by the
mayor with the consent and approval of the council. One member may, at the time of appointment
be under twenty one (21) years of age.
B. Term Of Office: The term of office for the first appointive members appointed to such commission
shall be two (2), four (4) and six (6) years, to be determined by lot. Thereafter the term of office for
such appointed commission member shall be six (6) years. The youth member shall be appointed
to a term of up to one year and may be reappointed to up to four (4) successive terms. (Ord. 680,
6-19-2013)
2-4-3: VACANCY; REMOVAL; COMPENSATION:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 31/336
A. Vacancies: Vacancies occurring otherwise than through the expiration of terms shall be filled by the
mayor and confirmed by the council.
B. Removal: Members may be removed by a majority vote of the body confirming the original
appointment.
C. Compensation: Members shall be selected without respect to political affiliation and may receive
such mileage and per diem compensation not to exceed ten cents ($0.10) per mile and ten dollars
($10.00) per day as may from time to time be determined by the council of the city. (Ord. 464, 3-
18-1974)
2-4-4: ORGANIZATION; RULES:
The commission shall elect its own chairman, and may create and fill such other offices as it may
determine necessary. (Ord. 464, 3-18-1974)
2-4-5: MEETINGS:
A. Meetings: The commission shall hold one regular meeting each month for not less than nine (9)
months of each year. A majority of the appointive members of the commission shall be necessary
to constitute a quorum at any meeting.
B. Rules And Regulations: Written rules consistent with the laws of the state of Idaho shall be adopted
for the transaction of business and a written record of business, resolutions, findings and
determinations shall be kept. All meetings and records shall be open to the public. (Ord. 464, 3-18-
1974)
2-4-6: POWERS; DUTIES:
A. Powers: It shall be the duty of the commission to recommend and make suggestions to the city
council for the adoption of a long range comprehensive plan for the physical development of the
city; for the formation of zoning districts; to make suggestions concerning the laying out, widening,
extending and locating of streets, roads and highways for the relief of traffic, to make suggestions
concerning density of population and development of land within the jurisdiction of the city; to make
suggestions concerning the future growth, development and beautification of the city in respect to
its public buildings, streets, parks, grounds and lands consistent with the future growth and
development of the city in order to promote the public health, morals, safety and welfare of the
inhabitants thereof; and to do all such other things and acts as may be provided by title 50, chapter
11 of the Idaho Code and amendments and additions thereto.
B. Duties: The Commission may cooperate with other and like commissions for the purposes as
herein set forth and set forth in the statutes of the State of Idaho. (Ord. 464, 3-18-1974)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 32/336
2-4-7: AREA OF CITY IMPACT DESIGNATED:
A. The designated area of City impact for the City of Gooding within the incorporated areas of the
County of Gooding, State of Idaho, shall be as follows:
Beginning at the Northeast corner of Section 32, Township 5 South, Range 15 E.B.M.;
Thence West along the North boundary of Section 32 to the Big Wood River;
Thence following the meander line of the Big Wood River westerly to its intersection with the West
boundary line of Section 31, Township 5 South, Range 15 E.B.M.;
Thence South to the Southwest corner of Section 7, Township 6 South, Range 15 E.B.M.;
Thence West to the Southeast corner of Section 8, Township 6 South, Range 15 E.B.M.;
Thence North to the Point of Beginning.
As of January 1, 1995 this area was also described by the following postal designations;
Beginning at the corner of 1700 South 2000 East, Gooding County, Idaho;
Then following the line of 1700 Southwest to the Big Wood River;
Following the Big Wood River meandering to the West to a point intersecting Gooding County
Road designate 1800 East;
Thence South on the 1800 East extended South to road designated as 2000 South;
Thence East to road designated as 2000 East;
Thence North to the Point of Beginning. (Ord 594, 4-3-1995)
B. The plan of the City Planning Commission, and all amendments thereto are hereby made
applicable to the area defined in subsection A above.
C. The Zoning and Subdivision Ordinances subsequent amendments thereto as officially adopted by
the City of Gooding shall apply to the Area of City Impact as above defined. (Ord. 485, 2-2-1976)
Title 3
DEPARTMENTS
Chapter 1
FIRE DEPARTMENT
3-1-1: DEPARTMENT ESTABLISHED:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 33/336
There is hereby established a volunteer fire department for the City to be known as the GOODING
FIRE DEPARTMENT. (1-701; 1947 Code)
3-1-2: EQUIPMENT:
The equipment of the Fire Department shall consist of the hose, motorized equipment, and the
apparatus now owned by the City and such additional equipment which may hereafter be purchased
by the City or acquired by said Fire Department, together with the fire station and equipment in the
nature of fire plugs and fire hydrants. (1-702; 1947 Code)
3-1-3: MEMBERS; QUALIFICATIONS:
The number of active members of such Fire Department shall be such number, as from time to time,
may be fixed and determined by the Council. (Ord. 477,4-21-1975)
3-1-4: APPOINTMENTS:
The Fire Chief and Assistant Fire Chief shall each be appointed by the Mayor, by and with the consent
of the Council, and shall hold office until the expiration of the term of the appointing power, unless
sooner removed by the Mayor. (1-704; 1947 Code)
3-1-5: OATH OF OFFICE:
Before entering upon the duties of said offices, said officers shall take and subscribe an oath to
support the Constitution and laws of the State of Idaho and the provisions of this Code, and to
faithfully perform the duties of their respective offices according to the best of their ability. (1-705; 1947
Code)
3-1-6: FIRE CHIEF IN CHARGE:
The Fire Chief shall have absolute control of the Department at all times, shall call meetings of the
members and shall direct or cause to be directed all improvements of the several companies and shall
see to it that they keep the apparatus and machinery under their care in proper order and ready at all
times for active duty, and he shall supervise and direct said Department in fighting fires, or prevention
of fires, and do all things required to be done to safeguard the City against loss by fire. (1-706; 1947
Code)
3-1-7: INSPECTIONS:
It shall be the duty of the Fire Chief to inspect or cause to be inspected by the Fire Department, its
officers or members, as often as may be necessary, but not less than twice a year in the outlying
districts, and four (4) times a year in closely built portions of the City, all buildings, premises and public
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 34/336
thoroughfares, except interior of private dwellings, for the purposes of ascertaining any conditions
liable to cause fire, or any violations of regulations promulgated by the City for the purpose of reducing
fire hazards. (1-707; 1947 Code)
3-1-8: COMBUSTIBLE MATERIAL:
It shall be the duty of the Fire Chief and any police officer who shall find in any building or upon any
premises any combustible or explosive matter, dangerous accumulations, rubbish, waste paper,
boxes, shavings, unnecessary accumulations or other inflammable material especially liable to fire, to
order and require the removal of such objectionable material without delay. (1-708; 1947 Code)
3-1-9: ASSISTANT IN CHARGE:
It shall be the duty of the Assistant Fire Chief to attend upon the Fire Chief and assist him in the
performance of his duties and in the absence of the Fire Chief he shall perform the duties of that
office. (1-709; 1947 Code)
3-1-10: POLICE AUTHORITY:
When on active duty the Fire Chief and Assistant Fire Chief shall each be invested with the authority
of police officer of the City with authority to make arrests, and shall each likewise have such police
authority for the purpose of enforcing any provision of this Code relating to matters of fire protection or
prevention. (1-710; 1947 Code)
3-1-11: POLICE SUBJECT TO FIRE CALLS:
The Chief of Police, night police and other police officials shall be subject to duty and call at all fires
and said police shall respond and assist in every way they can in getting the apparatus to the fire and
shall take charge and protect any property needing their protection, and shall keep back the people
from getting in the way or in any way interfering with the firemen in the discharge of their duties, and
each of the said police officers shall be under the orders of the Fire Chief during a fire. (1-711; 1947
Code)
3-1-12: REPORT OF FIRE CHIEF:
It shall be the duty of the Fire Chief to submit an itemized report to the Clerk of the attendance of the
members of the Department drills and at each fire, the date and place of fire, and the amount due
each member for attending drills and for services rendered at each fire. (1-713; 1947 Code)
3-1-13: APPROACH TO FIRE LIMITED:
Whenever a fire shall occur in the City, the Fire Chief or Acting Fire Chief is hereby empowered during
the continuance of such fire, to prescribe the limits within which it shall be unlawful for any person to
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 35/336
come excepting members of said Fire Department, the owners of the premises included in such limits,
and such other persons as may be specially admitted by the said Fire Chief or Acting Fire Chief. It
shall be unlawful for any person other than those above specified to enter within such limits at any
time during the progress of a fire. (1-714; 1947 Code)
3-1-14: INTERFERENCE WITH EQUIPMENT:
It shall be unlawful for any person other than members of the Fire Department or police officers,
without permission of the Fire Chief or Acting Fire Chief to knowingly or wilfully handle, stand upon or
otherwise interfere with any fire apparatus while the same is being used to extinguish any fire or to
approach nearer than one hundred feet (100') to the building or fire. (1-715; 1947 Code)
3-1-15: REMOVAL OF EQUIPMENT:
It shall be unlawful for any person unless specifically permitted so to do by the Fire Chief to remove
any fire apparatus, equipment, tools or accessories from the place where same are kept or to interfere
with any fire hydrant, either by turning the water on or off or attaching any hose, pipe or other
connections thereto or interfering therewith in any manner whatsoever. (1-716; 1947 Code)
3-1-16: FIRE HYDRANTS:
It shall be unlawful for any person in any manner to obstruct the view of any fire hydrant or place any
material or vehicle in front thereof or within fifteen feet (15') of either side thereof. (1-717; 1947 Code)
3-1-17: CROSSING FIRE HOSE:
It shall be unlawful for the owner, driver or operator of any vehicle to drive, haul, or propel same on or
across any of the hose belonging to the Fire Department or to drive or leave such vehicle on any
street in such a manner as to interfere with or obstruct any of the fire apparatus or the workings
thereof at a fire when an alarm has been struck. (1-718; 1947 Code)
3-1-18: DUTY OF DRIVER OF VEHICLE:
The driver of any vehicle, upon the sounding of the fire alarm, shall immediately draw up said vehicle
as near as practicable to the right hand curb, remain standing still until the fire apparatus has passed.
(Ord. 385, 11-2-1959)
3-1-19: COMPENSATION OF MEMBERS:
The rate of compensation for participating in fire drills and the rate of compensation for each fire
attended shall be fixed and determined by the Council and shall be in the form of a schedule, which
schedule shall be filed with the Clerk and which may be amended or altered by the Council, by
resolution, or motion, from time to time. (Ord. 477, 4-21-1975)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 36/336
Chapter 2
POLICE DEPARTMENT
3-2-1: CHIEF OF POLICE:
The chief of police under the direction of the mayor shall direct and control the police of the city. He
shall preserve the peace and good order of the city, quell all riots, arrest and bring all violators of this
code before the proper judge for trial, either with or without process, serve all processes issued by the
proper judge to him directed, and enforce all orders and judgments of said court and take such
measures as shall secure the peace and good order of all public meetings. The chief of police, in the
execution of his duty, with or without warrant, in arresting any person accused or suspected of crime
or in the suppression of any riot or unlawful assembly or in the prevention of violation of this code,
shall have the power to call upon any citizen or bystander to assist said chief in the execution of his
duty. He shall inquire into and report to the proper judge all violations of this code and criminal laws of
this state, and cause all laws of the city to be enforced. He shall take into custody with or without
process, any person found violating this code and bring such person before the proper judge to be
dealt with according to law. (1970 Code; amd. Ord. 497, 7-18-1977)
3-2-2: CHIEF OF POLICE TO KEEP RECORD:
The chief of police shall keep a record in a book provided for that purpose, of all monies belonging to
the city which may come into his hands from whatever source, stating from whom and on what
account received and pay the same into the treasury. He shall also record the name, if known, of
every person arrested, the date and cause of arrest, and such other facts as may be deemed
important and report an abstract thereof to the council monthly or more often if required. (1970 Code)
Title 4
BUILDING REGULATIONS
Chapter 1
DANGEROUS BUILDINGS
4-1-1: DETERMINATION OF DANGER:
Whenever it shall come to the attention of the Council that any tree, building or structure within the
City, because of neglect or decay or any other cause, is so dilapidated, dangerous or in such condition
as to menace the public health or the safety of persons, passers-by or adjacent property, or is in such
condition as to constitute an unreasonable fire hazard or an obstruction of public travel and rights or is
in such condition as to be subversive of public order, decency or morals, then it shall be the duty of the
Council to make an inspection and examination of said building, tree or structure and of immediate
surroundings, aided by such City officials and employees as the Council may deem advisable. (Ord.
314, 10-16-1950)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 37/336
4-1-2: HEARING:
If upon making such inspection and examination the Council shall consider that any tree, building or
structure within said City, because of neglect or decay or any other cause, is so dilapidated,
dangerous or in such condition so as to menace the public health or the safety of persons, passers-by
or adjacent property, or is in such condition as to constitute an unreasonable fire hazard or an
obstruction of public travel and rights or is in such condition as to be subversive of public order,
decency or morals, then the Council shall hold a hearing relative to said tree, building or structure and
shall cause a notice to be served upon the person holding, owning or maintaining such building, tree
or structure, specifying a time and place when and where a hearing will be had relative thereto before
the Mayor and Council. The time for such hearing shall be not less than ten (10) days from the date of
the notice. If the building or property be vacant and the owner absent from the City, such notice may
be served by posting a copy thereof on the front door of said premises and by mailing a copy thereof
to the owner at the address of such owner as shown on such records. At such hearing witnesses may
be heard and evidence received on behalf of the City or the person owning, holding or maintaining
such tree, building or structure, and the hearing will be conducted as nearly as practicable in the
manner prevailing in courts of law. (Ord. 314, 10-16-1950)
4-1-3: ORDER OF REMOVAL:
If after such hearing the Council officially determines that the tree, building or structure, because of
neglect or decay or any other cause, is so dilapidated, dangerous or in such condition as to menace
the public health or the safety of persons, passers-by or adjacent property, or is in such condition as to
constitute an unreasonable fire hazard or an obstruction of public travel and right or is in such
condition as to be subversive of public order, decency or morals, then the Council may declare such
tree, building or structure to be a nuisance and thereupon the Council shall cause an order to be
entered and served upon the person holding, owning or maintaining such tree, building or structure,
advising of such official determination and directing that unless the objectionable conditions which
shall be specified in the order are remedied to the reasonable satisfaction of the Council within such
reasonable time as may be fixed in the order, which shall be not less than fifteen (15) days, the
Council will cause the tree, building or structure to be repaired, destroyed or removed. Such order
shall be served in the manner provided for the service of the notice in the Idaho Statutes. (Ord. 314,
10-16-1950)
4-1-4: ASSESSMENT OF COSTS:
If the person owning, holding or maintaining such tree, building or structure does not comply with the
provisions of such order within the time therein specified, the Council may cause the repair,
destruction or removal of such tree, building or structure at the expense of the person holding, owning
or maintaining the same, and may levy a special assessment on the land or premises whereon the
nuisance is situated to defray the cost or to reimburse the City for the cost of repair, destruction or
removal of said tree, building or structure so declared to be a nuisance. (Ord. 314, 10-16-1950)
Chapter 2
BUILDING CODE
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 38/336
4-2-1: CODES ADOPTED:
The approved editions of the following nationally recognized codes, as adopted by the State of Idaho
or the Idaho Building Code Board, are adopted as the official building codes of the City of Gooding,
State of Idaho, except as provided in subsection B of this section:
International Building Code B;
International Building Code, parts I - IV and IX;
International Energy Conservation Code.
A. The adopted versions of the foregoing codes shall be deemed superseded by successive versions
of such codes as they are adopted or approved by the Idaho Building Code Board, or the State of
Idaho, effective on the date any such codes are made effective by the Idaho Building Code Board
or Idaho legislation.
B. At this time there will be no exceptions to the codes as adopted.
C. Agricultural buildings are exempt from the building codes adopted herein but shall remain subject to
placement requirements established by zoning regulations. (Ord. 628, 12-16-2002)
4-2-2: VALUATION AND PERMIT FEE SCHEDULE ADOPTED:
(Rep. by Ord. 631, 6-16-2003)
4-2-3: AREA OF CITY IMPACT:
All the regulations, provisions, penalties and conditions of the Uniform Building Code shall apply and
be enforced by the City in the area of City impact, as now described in section 2-4-7 of this Code and
as described in ordinance 20 of the ordinances of Gooding County, or as said area may hereafter be
fixed and described. (Ord. 537, 3-15-1982)
4-2-4: FENCE PERMIT1:
Prior to the erection of any fence, by any person, corporation or other entity upon any land located
within the City boundaries, the person or entity constructing the same shall first obtain a fence permit
from the City building inspector. The Gooding City Council is authorized to establish, by resolution, the
fee for such fence permit. (Ord. 650, 1-17-2006)

The Uniform Plumbing Code of the City,establishing rules and regulations for the installation of

Chapter 4
ELECTRICAL CODE
4-4-1: CODE ADOPTED:
All installation of electrical wiring and apparatus shall meet the specifications and requirements for
such wiring and installation of apparatus set forth and in conformity with the provisions of the National
Electrical Code of 1971, as approved by the American Standards Institute, together with all
amendments, supplements and revisions thereof. Such National Electrical Code of 1971, together with
all amendments, supplements and revisions thereof, is hereby adopted as the "Electrical Code" of the
City under and by virtue of the provisions of Idaho State law. Three (3) copies of said National
Electrical Code of 1971 shall be on file in the office of the Clerk and properly identified as being the
officially adopted Electrical Code of the City. Reference to such Codes so on file with the Clerk may be
had by any person during business hours. (Ord. 512, 3-19-1979)
Chapter 5
GAS FITTING CONTRACTORS
4-5-1: DEFINITION OF GAS:
The word "gas" as used in this Chapter shall be construed to mean natural gas, manufactured gas,
hydrocarbon gas or any mixture of gases produced, transmitted, distributed or furnished by any gas
utility or agency, except liquefied petroleum gas as defined and regulated under Chapter 39 Idaho
Session Laws of 1945. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-2: GAS INSTALLATIONS:
The term "gas installations" as used in this Chapter shall be construed to mean the installation of all
facilities for producing, transmitting and distributing gas and all accessory equipment, appurtenances
and appliances necessary for the control and utilization of gas. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-3: GAS PRODUCTION FACILITIES:
Any and all equipment or facilities used for the total or partial production of a gas supply for a piped
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 40/336
system shall be proposed in conformance with the requirements of Section 1 of State of Idaho Public
Utility Commission General Order No. 98, and shall be constructed in accordance therewith only after
approval and acceptance as to need and location by the public authority having jurisdiction. (Ord. 372,
1-7-1957)
4-5-4: CONSTRUCTION, OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE:
The minimum standards applying to transmission and distribution facilities shall be as stipulated in
ASA B31.1.8-1955 of the American Standards Association, with the exceptions and additions as
provided under Rules 3 and 4, Section 11 of Idaho Public Utilities Order No. 98. Work and permits
related to alignment, right of way, easements, trenching and backfilling and repair of streets and
pavements shall be performed in accordance with existing statutes and provisions of this Code
applicable to such work. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-5: POWERS AND DUTIES OF CITY INSPECTOR:
The City Building Inspector and his assistants are hereby authorized, empowered and directed to
inspect and supervise the installation, construction, reconstruction and repair of all gas house piping,
gas appliances, fixtures and apparatus now or hereafter to be placed in or in any manner directly
attached to any building or structure within the City. The Building Inspector and his assistants shall be
subject to the orders and directions of the Mayor and Council and are hereby vested with full authority
to enter any building or premises at any time in the discharge of their duties herein imposed, after
having presented the proper identification. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-6: PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
Any person legally entitled to receive a permit shall make application at the Building Inspector's office
on the form provided. A description of the work proposed to be done, location, ownership, occupancy
and use of the premises shall be given. The Building Inspector may require plans and specifications
and such other information as may be deemed necessary and pertinent for examination before
granting the permit. When it has been determined that the information furnished by the applicant is in
compliance with this Chapter, the permit shall be issued upon payment of the required fees as
hereinafter fixed.
No gas house piping shall be installed, constructed, reconstructed or repaired until a permit to do such
work shall have first been obtained from the Building Inspector. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-7: BOND REQUIRED:
Every gas fitting contractor, before securing a license as provided for in this Chapter, must furnish a
suitable bond to the City in the sum of five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) conditioned to indemnify and
save harmless said City from all loss or damage that may arise through carelessness, neglect or the
violation of any of the provisions of this Code; and must further post a certificate of insurance with the
City evidencing the insurance of the gas fitting contractor against property damage in an amount not
less than fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00); and bodily injury with limits of not less than ten thousand
dollars ($10,000.00) per person and fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) total for each occurrence.
(Ord. 375, 9-16-1957)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 41/336
4-5-8: WORK NOT REQUIRING PERMITS:
A permit shall not be required for the clearing of stoppages or repairing of leaks in pipes, valves or
fixtures when such repairs do not involve or require the replacement or rearrangement of pipes, valves
or fixtures. It shall be required that work of this nature be performed by persons qualified under this
Chapter as competent to do such work. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-9: COST OF PERMIT:
The applicant shall pay to the Clerk for each permit issued at the time of issuance a permit fee of one
dollar ($1.00) plus an inspection fee in accordance with the following schedule:
For service line to building (if not furnished by Gas Co.
as part of distribution system) and piping system in
building $1.00
For each installed domestic gas range .50
For each installed gas fired incinerator $ .50
For each installed gas water heater .50
For each installed gas fired room heater .50
For each installed central heating gas appliance 1.00
Miscellaneous counter appliances, each .25
Capped outlets for future connection, each .50
For each installed refrigerator using gas fuel .50
For each installed gas fired duct furnace 1.00
For each installed gas plate or laundry stove .50
For each installed gas fired clothes dryer .50
For each installed hotel or restaurant range or unit broiler 1.00
For each installed hotel or restaurant deep fat fryer .50
For each installed hotel or restaurant gas bake or roast oven 1.00
For each installed conversion burner 1.00
For each installed gas engine 1.00
For each installed industrial boiler installation 1.00
(Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-10: INSPECTION BY GAS SUPPLIER:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 42/336
The right is reserved for entry to the premises by the Gas Company or Utility, after having presented
the proper identification, and it shall be required that said supplier make its own inspection of all
facilities before connecting the meter and admitting gas to the system. The Gas Company or Utility
shall make a second inspection of all facilities after gas is admitted to the system to assure in the
presence of the permit holder the proper functioning of the system and all appliances. (Ord. 372, 1-7-
1957)
4-5-11: QUALIFIED INSTALLING AGENCY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the work or business of making gas installations in the
City unless such person or responsible person representing the firm or corporation as hereinafter
prescribed has successfully passed an examination conducted by the Board of Examiners and has
issued to him a Certificate of Competency by said Board in accordance with the provisions of this
Chapter. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-12: CLASSIFICATIONS OF QUALIFIED AGENCIES:
There shall be three (3) classifications of competency as herein defined:
A. Gas Fitting Contractor: A gas fitting contractor shall be any person skilled in the planning and
supervision of the installation of gas piping, venting and equipment, and who is familiar with the
laws, rules and regulations covering the same and who is competent to assume work on a contract
basis and to direct the work of qualified employees.
A gas fitting contractor who in person does gas fitting work shall also be qualified as a journeyman
gas fitter, or have in his employ on all gas fitting work, a qualified journeyman gas fitter.
B. Journeyman Gas Fitter: A journeyman gas fitter shall be any person who as part of his principal
occupation is engaged in the practical installation of gas piping and equipment, and who is familiar
with the Code requirements governing the same, and who works under the direction of a gas fitting
contractor.
C. Apprentice Gas Fitter: An apprentice gas fitter is any person other than a journeyman, who as a
part of his principal occupation is engaged in learning and assisting in the installation of gas piping
and equipment. Apprentices shall not perform gas installation work except under the supervision of
a licensed journeyman gas fitter. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-13: LICENSES REQUIRED:
Before any person shall carry on or engage in the work or business of making gas installations, he
shall procure a license applicable to the classification in which he proposes to work and pay the
annual license fee imposed on such classification. The license shall not be transferable. Every
applicant for license shall present a Certificate of Competency as proof that he has been approved by
the Board of Examiners as competent for the classification sought. If the applicant be a partnership,
firm or corporation, the application shall be made by a bona fide member or agent thereof, who shall
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 43/336
at all times be in actual charge of the applicant's gas installation business. When any person is
designated and authorized to be or act as an agent for the applicant, such authorization shall be in
writing, signed by the applicant and the person designated, one copy of which shall be filed with the
Examining Board and one copy filed in the office of the Building Inspector or the Clerk. (Ord. 372, 1-7-
1957)
4-5-14: LICENSE FEES:
Before any license is issued, the applicant shall pay to the Clerk a license fee in accordance with the
following schedule:
Gas Fitting Contractor $25.00
Journeyman Gas Fitter 2.00
Apprentice Gas Fitter No fee
Upon payment of the above fee and presentation of a valid Certificate of Competency, the Clerk shall
issue a License Certificate, indicating clearly thereon the name of the holder, classification and year
for which it is valid. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-15: EXPIRATION AND RENEWAL OF LICENSES:
Gas fitter licenses shall expire on December 31 each year unless sooner revoked and shall be
renewed not later than the following January 15 upon payment of five dollars ($5.00) for gas fitting
contractor and two dollars ($2.00) for journeyman gas fitter. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-16: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
Any person holding a license shall not lend such license to any other person or allow any other person
to do gas installation work under his license except licensed journeymen in his employ. Violation of
this provision shall be cause for revocation of license in addition to other penalties provided hereafter.
(Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-17: DISPLAY OF LICENSE:
All persons holding a valid gas fitting contractor license shall display for public view such license
certificate in their place of business. All journeymen and apprentice gas fitters holding a valid license
shall have available on his person during working hours his certificate of competency card with his
current license number endorsed thereon. It shall be unlawful for any person to display evidence of
license or competency unless so qualified under this Chapter. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-18: DISPOSITION OF LICENSE FEES:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 44/336
All money derived from gas fitter licenses shall be placed in the General Fund. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-19: EXAMINING BOARD:
A board to be known as the "Gas Fitters Examining Board" shall be appointed by the Mayor. It shall
consist of three (3) members selected from nominees recommended by an organized and generally
recognized association of responsible firms or individuals engaged in the gas fitting or related pipe
fitting industry and who shall qualify as hereinafter prescribed. The members of the first Board shall be
appointed within sixty (60) days after the adoption hereof and shall serve for the following terms: One
member for one year, one member for two (2) years and one member for three (3) years. Thereafter
upon the expiration of each term the Board members shall be appointed for a term of three (3) years.
All Board members shall be subject to removal by the Mayor for malfeasance in office, neglect of duty
or incapacity to serve. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-20: QUALIFICATIONS OF BOARD MEMBERS:
All members of the Board shall be United States citizens, residents of the State of Idaho for not less
than one year, engaged in a responsible capacity in the gas fitting business prior to appointment and
during the term of office and qualified by integrity, knowledge and experience to judge the competency
of applicants for gas fitters certificates. Not less than one member of the Board shall have had five (5)
years or more experience as a gas fitting contractor, or gas fitting journeyman, or as an engineer
experienced in the design, construction and operation of gas systems. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-21: DUTIES AND POWERS OF EXAMINING BOARD:
The Board shall conduct examinations for the purpose of determining the competency of applicants
who are required to have a license under this Chapter and to issue certificates of competency to such
persons as may be entitled thereto. The Board shall elect a chairman from its members who shall be
the executive officer and preside at all meetings and a secretary who shall keep such records as are
proper for efficient discharge of the Board's duties, which records pertaining to an applicant's
qualifications shall be kept intact and available in the event of dispute for a period of not less than one
year following the date of issuance of the certificate of competency. The Board shall determine the
character and extent of the examination based on the requirements of this Code, and shall grade and
pass or reject the applicant on the basis of equaling or exceeding, or failing to equal a minimum
percentage grade of seventy percent (70%). The Board shall issue certificates of competency to
successful applicants and shall have the power to revoke such certificates under conditions
hereinafter prescribed. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-22: APPLICATION FOR EXAMINATION:
Any person required by this Chapter to be licensed shall make application on the form provided to the
Clerk, acting for the Board, for the examination for a certificate of competency and pay the
examination fee. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-23: EXAMINATION FEE:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 45/336
The applicant shall pay to the Clerk at the time of making application an examination fee in
accordance with the following schedule:
Examination for journeyman gas fitter certificate $15.00
Apprentice gas fitters shall not be required to be examined but shall be registered with the Board and
shall maintain their certificate cards showing classification. The Board shall notify the Clerk of this
registration. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-24: TIME OF EXAMINATION:
The Board shall so schedule its meetings to examine a single applicant, or as many applicants at one
time, as circumstances dictate, but in no case shall an applicant be required to delay his examination
more than sixty (60) days from the date the application is accepted. Each applicant shall be notified by
the Board of the time and place for examination not less than forty eight (48) hours prior to
examination time. Notification by registered letter directed to the address given on the application shall
be considered notification. Failure of the applicant to appear for examination does not entitle him to a
refund of the examination fee. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-25: RE-EXAMINATION:
Any person who for sufficient cause in the judgment of the Board was unable to appear for
examination at the stated time, may apply and be given an examination after thirty (30) days for the
original fee payment. Any person who fails to pass the examination may apply for re-examination after
a period of thirty (30) days upon payment of the examination fee. Should any person fail to pass the
examination the second time, the Board may refuse the application until the expiration of six (6)
months. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-26: CERTIFICATE OF COMPETENCY:
Upon successful completion of an examination, the Board shall issue to the applicant a certificate of
competency in the form of a card, providing thereon the applicant's name, classification, year which
current, space for the applicant's signature and license number, and the signature of the Chairman of
the Board of Examiners. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-27: REVOCATION OF CERTIFICATE:
A certificate of competency may be revoked by the Board if it has good and sufficient evidence that
such certificate was obtained by fraud, or if the holder demonstrates lack of knowledge or
incompetency in matters relevant to such certificate. In such cases the Board may order reexamination
or may refuse application for re-examination as conditions may dictate. (Ord. 372, 1-7-
1957)
4-5-28: COMPENSATION OF BOARD MEMBERS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 46/336
The members of the Examining Board shall each receive from the City as the only compensation for
their services the sum of five dollars ($5.00) for each journeyman fitter examined. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-29: DISPOSITION OF EXAMINATION AND RENEWAL FEES:
All monies derived from the payment of examination fees shall be placed in the General Fund. (Ord.
372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-30: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS:
A. The piping shall be constructed and installed so as to be durable, substantial and gas tied.
B. Piping shall be of a size and so installed as to provide a supply of gas sufficient to meet the
maximum demand without undue loss of pressure between the point of supply at the meter and the
appliance or appliances.
C. The building structure shall not be weakened by the installation of the piping.
D. Piping containing gas under pressure shall not be cut into or opened.
E. No flame or fire in any form shall be used in attempting to locate a gas leak or where there is an
odor of gas present. Checking for a gas leak with a soap and water solution is recommended.
F. All gas piping or gas appliance installation shall be performed with the gas turned off to eliminate
hazards from leakage of gas.
G. When working on piping which contains or has contained gas, smoking shall not be permitted.
H. When interruptions in work occur, the system shall be left in a safe and satisfactory condition. (Ord.
372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-31: HOUSE PIPING PRACTICE:
A. The Building Inspector may require a plan of a proposed gas piping job which shall be subject to his
approval consistent with the requirements of this Chapter. Adequate consideration should be given
to future demands and provisions made for added gas service. When an additional appliance is to
be served through an extension of present piping, capacity of the existing lines shall be verified.
B. The size of pipe to be used in piping buildings and structures shall be governed by the following
factors:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 47/336
1. The length of pipe and number of fittings.
2. The maximum gas consumption to be provided for.
3. Allowable loss in pressure from meter to appliance (shall not exceed 0.3 inch water column at
the maximum probable gas demand).
4. Diversity factor.
C. For accuracy, the manufacturer's BTU rating appearing on name plate of appliances shall be used.
In the absence of such information, the following table showing maximum demand required for
some common gas appliances may be used.
TABLE 1

Conversion burners, unit heaters, warm air furnaces and gas boilers: Rating on the appliance
name plate or rating shown in manufacturer's catalog shall be used.
D. Size and length of pipe for average, domestic conditions:
1. The diameter of the supply line from the meter shall not be less than one and one-fourth inch
(1'/4"), in any case, and may be governed by the following specifications for minimum size of
house piping from meter to kitchen in houses, flats and apartments:
a. Less than six (6) rooms - 11/4 inch diameter.
b. Six (6) to nine (9) rooms - 11/2 inch diameter.
c. Nine (9) to twelve (12) rooms - 2 inches diameter.
d. For houses containing twelve (12) rooms or more, for commercial and industrial buildings and
installations, and where conditions are unusual, consult the Building Inspector or the Gas
Company for specifications.
2. Outlets to appliances should be of a diameter not less than the diameter of the inlet connection
on the appliance. The outlet to serve the kitchen range should not be less than three-fourths inch
(3/4") in diameter.
3. Capacity of Pipe: Capacities of different sizes and lengths of pipe in cubic feet per hour with a
pressure drop of 9.3 inch of water column for gas of 0.60 sp. gr. are shown in Table 2. In using
this table, no allowance for an ordinary number of fittings is necessary.
