4. Diversity Factor: The diversity factor is the percentage of the total connected load in use at any
one time. For single-family dwelling units it is not necessary to consider this factor. However, it
may be an important factor in determining the correct pipe size to be used in multi-family
dwellings served from one gas meter. It is dependent upon the number and kinds of gas
appliances being installed. Where applicable, consult the Building Inspector for the diversity
factor to be used.
5. Extensions: Extensions to existing piping shall conform to Table 2. Existing piping shall be
converted to the proper size of pipe where necessary. In no case shall extensions be made to
existing pipe which is smaller than permitted by Table 2.
E. Size And Length Of Pipe For Special Conditions: For conditions not covered in Table 2, such as
longer runs or larger sizes of pipe, greater gas demands, application of a diversity factor when
piping multiple-family dwellings, pressures higher than fifteen inches (15") or lower than four
inches (4") of water column pressures, or specific gravity that does not fall within the range of 0.55
to 0.75, the size and lengths of piping required shall be calculated in a manner satisfactory to both
the Building Inspector and the Gas Company.
F. Pipe And Fittings:
1. All the pipe and fittings used for gas house piping shall be commercially perfect material, clear
and free from cutter burrs and defects in structure and threading. Wrought-iron or wrought-steel
pipe that complies with the American Standard for wrought-iron and wrought-steel pipe, ASA
B36.10-1950 or its latest revision, shall be considered as compliance with this requirement. All
pipe fittings (except stop cocks or valves) shall be malleable iron or steel when used with
wrought-iron or steel pipe, except that in size of four inches (4") and larger, cast iron may be
used.
2. Pipe and fitting threads shall comply with the American Standard for Pipe Threads, ASA B2.1-
1945. Pipe with threads which are stripped, chipped, corroded or otherwise damaged shall not
be used.
3. In no case shall it be permissible to repair defects in pipe or fittings, but having been located, the
defective pipe or fitting must be removed and replaced.
G. Concealed Piping:
1. No pipe smaller than standard one-half inch ('/2") iron pipe size shall be used in any concealed
location.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 50/336
2. Concealed piping shall be located in hollow rather than solid partitions and must have a suitable
protective coating if in contact with corrosive material.
3. Piping in solids, such as concrete, shall be laid in channels in the floors suitably covered to
permit access to the piping with a minimum of damage to the building.
4. Piping shall not be installed in chimneys, flues or ventilating ducts or shafts.
5. No unions, running threads, right and left couplings, and swing joints made by combinations of
fittings, shall be used in a concealed location. When necessary to insert fittings in piping which
has been installed in a concealed location, the piping may be reconnected by use of a ground
joint union with the nut "center punched" to prevent loosening by vibration.
6. The unthreaded portion of concealed piping, and other house piping, shall extend at least one
inch (1") through finished ceilings and walls, and not less than two inches (2") above floors.
Concealed piping must be securely supported.
H. Pipe bending must be minimized, and where the same is necessary, extreme care must be
exercised in making such bends. Bends when approved shall be free from kinks, and shall not be
less than the radius below:
Size of Pipe (Inches) Min. Radius of Bend (Inches)
3/8 10
1/2 12
3/4 14
1 16
11/4 18
11/2 20
2 24
I. White lead or other joint compound or dope shall be used sparingly applied to male pipe threads
only. In the case of gas connections for liquefied petroleum gases (propane, butane or butane-air
gases) the compound used in making joints shall be resistant to the action of such gases.
J. No device shall be inserted into gas piping that will reduce the cross sectional area or otherwise
obstruct the free flow of gas.
K. Gas pipes running from one building to another shall be placed underground, and shall be sized
according to Table 2, but in no case shall pipe smaller than one-half inch ('/2") be used.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 51/336
Underground piping shall be protected against corrosion with one coat of Sherwin-Williams Ebonol
or equal paint.
L. All branch outlet pipes shall be taken from the top or sides of horizontal lines and not from the
bottom. Where a branch outlet is placed on a main supply line before it is known what size of pipe
will be connected to it, the outlet shall be of the same size as the line which supplies it.
M. An individual control valve shall be provided for each separate house line in buildings arranged
with more than one house line. Every gas cock or valve must be readily accessible for operation or
repair. Piping systems that are supplied by separate meters shall not be inter-connected. Three (3)
way valves are not permissible in any case.
N. When connecting two (2) sizes of pipe, a reducing fitting shall be used. Gas shall not be supplied
from a smaller pipe to a larger pipe. When extensions to house piping systems are made, all
provisions hereof shall be complied with.
O. All house piping shall be secured and fastened to the building with pipe straps or pipe hooks. The
maximum spacing of supports shall be:
1/2" pipe 6 feet 11/4 inch and larger 10 feet
3/4" and 1" pipe 8 feet vertical risers each floor
Beams or joists shall not be notched or cut without approval of the proper administrative authority.
In the absence of established rules by the administrative authority, where it is necessary to notch
beams or joists, the piping should not be more than twenty four inches (24") from the wall or
support under the beam, such notching shall not exceed one-fifth (1/5) of the depth of the timber.
P. No gas piping shall be run closer than six inches (6") to knob and tube or nonmetallic cable. No gas
piping shall be placed underground closer than two feet (2') from a sewer or eight inches (8") from
a water pipe. When gas pipes enter the foundation walls of a building, the hole must be securely
sealed around the pipe.
Q. Each outlet, including a valve or cock outlet, shall be securely closed gas tight with a threaded iron
plug or cap immediately after installation and shall be left closed until an appliance or piping is
connected thereto. Likewise, when an appliance is removed from an outlet and the outlet is not to
be used again immediately, it shall be securely closed gas tight. In no case shall an outlet be
closed with tin caps, wooden plugs, corks and the like.
R. It shall be unlawful for a consumer or property owner to maintain simultaneously in a single building
or structure a system of piping for natural gas with either a system of piping in which liquefied
petroleum gas or wet gas is used or a system of piping connected to a liquified petroleum gas plant
or apparatus, whether such systems are physically interconnected or not. No distributor of natural
gas shall be required to turn natural gas into a building or structure where:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 52/336
1. A system of piping exists in which liquefied petroleum gas or wet gas is used.
2. A system of piping is connected to a liquefied petroleum gas plant or apparatus or connected to
a system of piping using wet gas.
3. A liquefied gas plant or apparatus is maintained.
S. Underground extensions of house piping to outdoor appliances shall be properly sized, but shall not
be less than one-half inch (1/2") iron pipe size and shall be protected against corrosion.
T. Underground gas piping shall not be installed under houses or buildings which are built on a
concrete slab foundation. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-32: GAS METERS:
A. The Gas Company will specify the location of the meter. Meters shall be placed where readily
accessible to Gas Company employees. Consumer or builder will bring piping to meter location
and provide necessary fittings for connecting the outlet side of the meter. Piping shall not
necessitate the placing of a meter under steps, under a window, in any unventilated closet, near a
furnace or boiler, or in any location where it will be subject to damage or excessive corrosion.
B. Where two (2) or more meters are installed on the same premises, but supply separate customers,
the piping system shall not be interconnected on the outlet side of the meters. The Gas Company
may serve a multiple meter installation through one service line. House piping to multiple meter
installation should terminate at the meter location selected by the Gas Company. Piping to multiple
meter installation shall be plainly marked by a metal tag installed by the plumber; designating the
part of the building being supplied.
C. Each dwelling unit or commercial building shall be served as an individually metered customer,
where such units or structures are on individual lots.
Customer's gas line shall not cross streets, alleys or adjacent property lines for the purpose of
serving multiple dwelling units from a single meter installation.
D. The meter installation shall be of adequate strength to support meters therein and other
appurtenances. Bottom of meter shall be placed not less than six inches (6") above finished grade.
E. No person unless an employee of the Gas Company or having permission from the Gas Company
shall repair, alter, open or make connection to the service pipe, or do any other work on the parts
of the gas supply system up to and including the meter. Likewise, no person unless an employee
of the Gas Company or having permission from the Gas Company shall disconnect the inlet of the
meter nor move the meter. A plumber may disconnect the outlet of a meter from the house piping
only when necessary. He shall remake the joint at the meter outlet and shall leave the meter turned
off. In case any work done by a plumber discloses the need for repairs or alterations by the Gas
Company on any part of the supply system containing unmeasured gas, the Gas Company shall
be notified promptly of this fact. If gas is leaking from any part of the gas supply system containing
unmeasured gas, a plumber not in the employ of the Gas Company may make necessary
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 53/336
temporary repairs and shall promptly notify the Gas Company to make permanent repairs. This
Section shall not apply to acts done in case of emergency. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-33: APPLIANCE INSTALLATION; GENERAL:
A. Appliance Design: All gas appliances installed shall be of a design to meet the American Standard
Approval or Listing Requirements as to safety and efficiency of operation and durability of
construction, except such apparatus as is not covered by said requirements. An appliance bearing
the seal of a nationally recognized testing agency, such as the American Gas Association, Inc.,
Laboratories and Underwriters' Laboratories, Inc., shall be considered as complying with this
Chapter. In the absence of such laboratory approval, the Building Inspector shall have the power to
approve equipment, provided it is demonstrated as meeting existing American Standard
Association requirements, or, in the absence of such requirements, will meet generally accepted
safe practices. Used appliances may be reinstalled when, in the opinion of the said Inspector, they
may be used without danger of life or property.
1. It shall be determined that the appliance has been designed for use with the gas to which it will
be connected. No attempt shall be made to convert the appliance from the gas specified on the
rating plate for use with a different gas without consulting the Building Inspector.
2. All gas appliances, and their flue or vent connectors, shall be installed so that continued or
intermittent operation will not create a hazard to persons or property. (See American Standard
for Installation of Gas Piping and Gas Appliance in Buildings, ASA Z21.30-1954, or the latest
revision thereof.)
3. Appliances shall be adequately supported and so connected to the piping as not to exert undue
strain on the connection.
4. Appliances shall be installed in a location in which the facilities for ventilation permit satisfactory
combustion of gas and proper venting, under normal conditions of use. While all forms of
building construction cannot be covered in detail, this requirement may usually be met by
application of one of the following methods in ordinary building construction.
a. In buildings of conventional frame, brick or stone construction, without enclosed appliance
rooms, basement storm windows or tight stair doors, infiltration is normally adequate to
provide air for combustion and draft hood dilution.
b. Where appliances are installed in a confined space within a building not having adequate air
infiltration, provisions shall be made for supplying this space with air for combustion and
ventilation. This may be accomplished by two (2) permanent openings freely communicating
with interior areas of adequate infiltration, each to provide the equivalent of one square inch
free area for each one thousand (1,000) BTU per hour of appliance input. Registers must not
be blocked by drapes or other furnishings. Each opening shall comply with the above
specifications; one opening shall be located at the top portion of the room inlet and one at the
bottom portion thereof. If necessary, continuous ducts having cross-sectional areas equal to
the opening shall be utilized to communicate with the source of air supply. The minimum
dimension for a rectangular air duct shall not be less than three inches (3").
c. Where appliances are installed in a confined space within a building of an unusual type
construction, air for combustion and ventilation must be obtained from outdoors or from
spaces (crawl or attic) freely communicating with the outdoors. Under these conditions, two (2)
openings having a combined area of not less than one square inch per one thousand (1,000)
BTU per hour of input rating will be provided. One opening shall be near the top of the
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 54/336
enclosure and one near the bottom. These openings shall be of approximately equal area and
shall communicate with the selected source or sources of adequate air supply, by ducts.
Where ducts are required, they shall be continuous and of the same cross-sectional area as
the openings to which they connect. The minimum dimension of rectangular air ducts shall be
not less than three inches (3"). Any duct from the top openings must be horizontal or pitched
upward.
d. Where appliances are installed in unconfined spaces, such as in full basements, within a
building of unusually tight construction, air for combustion and ventilation must be obtained
from outdoors or from spaces freely communicating with the outdoors. Under these conditions
a permanent opening or openings having a total free area of not less than one square inch per
one thousand (1,000) BTU per hour of input rating shall be provided. Where ducts are
required, they shall be of the same cross-sectional area as the openings to which they
connect. The minimum dimension of rectangular air ducts shall be not less than three inches
(3").
e. Operation of exhaust fans, kitchen ventilating systems or fireplaces may create conditions
requiring special attention to avoid unsatisfactory appliance operation.
5. Such nonportable appliances as central heating, water heating and similar equipment, shall be
connected to the gas piping with rigid pipe or by listed semi-rigid tubing not more than two feet
(2') in length. Domestic gas ranges, hot plates, refrigerators, and similar equipment shall be
connected to the gas piping with rigid pipe, listed semi-rigid tubing or listed appliance connectors
of flexible metal tubing and fittings. When a semi-rigid tubing connector or a connector of flexible
metal tubing and fittings is used, it shall be connected to an outlet in the same room as the
appliance. The length of the connector shall not exceed six feet (6'). The connector shall be
installed so as to be protected against physical damage.
6. The connection of an appliance with any type of gas hose is prohibited, except when used with
laboratory, shop or ironing equipment that requires mobility during operation. Such connections
shall have the shut-off or stop cock installed at the connection to the building piping. Where gas
hose is used, it shall be of the minimum practical length, but not to exceed six feet (6'), and shall
not extend from one room to another or pass through any walls, partitions, ceilings or floors.
Under no circumstances shall gas hose be concealed from view or used in a concealed location.
Only listed gas hose shall be used. Listed gas hose shall be used only in accordance with the
terms of its listing. Gas hose shall not be used where it is likely to be subject to excessive
temperatures (above 125 degrees F.).
7. When air or oxygen under pressure is used in connection with the gas supply, effective means
shall be provided to prevent the air or oxygen from going back into the gas piping.
8. Appliances and their connections shall be installed and tested and found gas tight after the gas
is turned on.
9. Every appliance shall be properly adjusted after being installed and the customer shall be
instructed as to its safe operation.
10. All electrical connections between gas appliances and building wiring shall conform to the
National Electrical Code, ASA C1-1953, or the latest revision thereof. The gas piping shall not be
used for an electrical ground nor shall electric circuits utilize gas piping, casing of controls,
panels, or other metal parts in lieu of wiring. No devices employing or depending upon on
electrical current shall be used to control or ignite a gas supply if of such character that failure of
the electrical current could result in the escape of unburned gas or in failure to reduce the supply
of gas under conditions which would normally result in its reduction unless other means are
provided to prevent the development of dangerous temperatures, pressures or the escape of
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 55/336
gas. This provision shall not apply to low voltage control and ignition circuits or to electronic
flame detection device circuits incorporated as part of the appliance. The electrical circuit
employed for operating the main gas control valve, automatic pilot, room temperature
thermostat, limit control or other electrical devices used with the gas appliances, shall be in
accordance with the wiring diagram supplied with the appliance. All gas appliances using
electrical controls shall have the controls connected to a permanently live electric circuit, i.e.,
one that is not controlled by a light switch. Central hearing gas appliances for domestic use shall
be provided with a separate electric circuit.
11. Gas appliance pressure regulators requiring access to the atmosphere for successful operation
shall be equipped with a vent pipe leading to the outer air or into the combustion chamber
adjacent to a constantly burning pilot, unless construction is such as to limit the escape of gas
from the vent opening in the event of diaphragm failure to not more than 1.0 cubic feet per hour
of a 0.6 specific gravity gas at seven inches (7") water column pressure. In case of vents leading
to the outer air, means shall be employed to prevent water from entering this pipe and also to
prevent stoppage by insects and foreign matter. In case of vents entering the combustion
chamber, the vents shall be located so that the escaping gas will be readily ignited by the pilot
flame and the heat liberated will not adversely affect the operation of the thermal element. The
terminus of the vent shall be securely held in a fixed position relative to the pilot flame.
12. Where the meter shut-off valve is not readily accessible from the appliance location, an
individual control valve shall be provided at the appliance ahead of the union connection.
B. Installation Of Water Heaters:
1. Water heaters shall not be installed in bathrooms, bedrooms, or in any occupied rooms normally
kept closed. Water heaters shall be located as close as practicable to the flue or vent. They
should be so located as to provide short runs of piping to fixtures. Water heaters shall be
installed in compliance with the clearances given in their listing requirements. Water heaters
shall be connected in a manner to permit observation, maintenance and servicing. Unlisted
water heaters shall be installed with a clearance of twelve inches (12") on all sides and rear.
Combustible floors under unlisted water heaters shall be protected in an approved manner.
2. No water heater shall be installed in a closed system of water piping unless an approved water
pressure relief valve is provided. The installation and adjustment of temperature, pressure and
vacuum relief valves or combinations thereof, and automatic gas shutoff valves, shall be in
accordance with the requirements of the Building Inspector or with the manufacturer's
instructions accompanying such devices.
3. The gas line shall be a separate line direct from the meter to the appliance, unless existing gas
line is of ample capacity. Any contemplated use of existing gas piping shall be verified with the
pipe capacity chart herein.
C. Installation Of Ranges:
1. The location of a domestic gas range shall be such as not to constitute a hazard to persons or
property. In the application of this requirement, appropriate consideration shall be given to the
design and construction of the range and the combustibility of the floor, wall or partition. Ranges
when installed on combustible floors shall be set on their own bases or legs. Ranges listed as
flush-to-wall models may be installed flush on all sides; others may be installed in compliance
with the clearance requirements of their listing. Unlisted domestic gas ranges shall be installed
with et least six inch (6") clearance from back and sides. Combustible floors under unlisted
appliances shall be protected. Domestic gas ranges shall have a vertical clearance above the
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 56/336
cooking top of not less than thirty six inches (36") to combustible construction. When the
underside of such combustible construction is protected with asbestos millboard, at least onequarter
inch ('/4") thick, covered with sheet metal of not less than No. 28 U.S. gauge, the
distance shall be not less than twenty four inches (24"). The projection shall extend nine inches
(9") beyond the sides of the range. All gas ranges shall be installed so that the cooking top and
oven racks are level.
2. Listed hotel and restaurant ranges, deep fat fryers and unit boilers, when set on their own bases
or legs, may be installed on unprotected combustible floors unless marked "For use only in
fireproof locations". Hotel and restaurant ranges, deep fat fryers, and unit boilers which are not
listed for mounting on combustible floors, shall be installed with at least six inch (6") clearance
from back and sides. Combustible floors under unlisted appliances shall be protected.
D. Installation Of Heating Equipment:
1. Room Or Space Heater: A room or space heater shall be placed so as not to cause a hazard to
walls, floors, curtains, furniture, doors when open, etc., and to the free movement of persons
within the room. Appliances designed and marked "For use in incombustible fire-resistive
fireplace only", shall not be installed elsewhere. Listed room or space heaters shall be installed
with clearance in compliance with their listing requirements. Unlisted room or space heaters
shall be installed with clearances from combustible construction not less than the following:
a. Circulating Type: Room heaters having an outer jacket surrounding the combustion chamber,
air circulates between the inner and outer jacket and without openings in the outer jacket to
permit direct radiation shall have clearances at side and rear of not less than twelve inches
(12").
b. Radiating Type: Room heaters other than those described above as of circulating type shall
have clearances at sides and rear of not less than eighteen inches (18"); except that heaters
which make use of metal, asbestos or ceramic material to direct radiation to the front of the
appliance shall have a clearance of thirty six inches (36") in front, and if constructed with a
double back of metal or ceramic may be installed with a clearance of eighteen inches (18") at
sides and twelve inches (12") at rear.
Combustible floors under unlisted room or space heaters shall be protected in an approved
manner. In no case shall the clearances be such as to interfere with the requirements for
combustion air and accessibility.
a. Wall Type Room Heaters: Wall type room or space heaters shall not be installed in walls of
combustible construction unless listed for such installation.
b. Venting: Room or space heaters shall be vented as specified in the venting requirements
herein. Room or space heaters installed in all sleeping quarters or rooms generally kept
closed shall be connected to an effective flue or vent and equipped with an automatic pilot.
2. Central Heating Boilers And Furnaces - Installation Or Conversion: The gas line shall be a
separate line direct from the meter to the boiler or furnace, unless the existing gas line is of
ample capacity. Where a complete shut-off type automatic pilot system is not utilized, a manual
main shut-off valve shall be provided ahead of all controls except the manual pilot gas valve.
When a complete shut-off type automatic system is utilized, a manual main shut-off valve shall
be provided ahead of all the controls. A suitable manual valve shall be provided for shutting off
the main gas burner independently of the pilot gas. A union connection shall be provided
downstream from the manual main shut-off valve to permit removal of the controls. Listed central
heating boilers and furnaces shall be installed with clearances not less than those specified in
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 57/336
their listing requirements. Unlisted central heating boilers and furnaces shall be installed with
clearances from combustible construction of not less than eighteen inches (18") above the
appliance and at sides, front and rear, and nine inches (9") from projecting flue box or draft
hood, except that the clearance above and at the sides and rear may be six inches (6") for
appliances of the following types:
a. Mechanical warm air furnaces which are automatically fired and equipped with a fan to
circulate the air and with approved automatic temperature limit controls that cannot be set
higher than two hundred fifty degrees (250?) Fahrenheit.
b. Steam boilers operating at not over fifteen (15) pounds gauge pressure and hot water boilers
operating at not in excess of two hundred fifty degrees (250?) Fahrenheit of the water-wall
type or having a jacket or lining of masonry or other satisfactory insulating material.
In no case shall the clearance be such as to interfere with the requirements for combustion air
and accessibility.
A central heating boiler or furnace shall be erected in accordance with the manufacturer's
instructions and shall be installed on a firm, level, fireproof foundation unless listed for
installation on a combustible floor. The installation of central heating boilers and furnaces shall
be such as to make them accessible for cleaning of heating surfaces, removal of burners,
replacement of sections, motors, controls, filters, draft hoods, and other working parts, and for
adjustment and lubrication of parts requiring such attention. Steam and hot water boilers shall be
provided with approved automatic devices to shut down the burners in the event of undue
pressure or low water in a steam boiler or overheating in a hot water boiler. Steam and hot water
boilers shall also be provided with a drain valve, by means of which the boiler may be flushed or
drained, and a direct connection to a water supply through an individual control valve.
The method of connecting the flow and return pipes on steam and hot water boilers shall
facilitate a rapid circulation of steam or water. For common piping systems, reference may be
made to the American Society of Heating and Air Conditioning Engineers' Heating, Ventilating,
Air Conditioning Guide, and to the Institute of Boiler and Radiator Manufacturers' (IBR) Guides.
A plenum chamber when not a part of a furnace shall be constructed in accordance with the
manufacturer's instructions. The method of connecting supply and return ducts shall facilitate
proper circulation of air. Reference may be made to the Standards of the National Board of Fire
Underwriters for the Installation of Air Conditioning, Warm Air Heating, Air Cooling and
Ventilating System, NBFU Pamphlet No. 90, and to the Design and Installation Manuals of the
National Warm Air Heating and Air Conditioning Association. Where the furnace is installed
within a confined space, the air circulated by the furnace shall be handled by ducts which are
sealed to the furnace casing and are entirely separate from the means provided for supply
combustion and ventilation air. In residential forced warm air central heating installations, a total
free area to the suction of the fan (return air and outside air) shall be provided so that the free
area of grilles or the minimum cross-sectional area of ducts shall be not less than two (2) square
inches for each one thousand (1,000) BTU of rated input.
3. Recessed Heaters: Listed recessed heaters may be installed in combustible construction.
Unlisted recessed heaters shall not be installed in combustible construction. Because of the
necessity for closely correlating the installation of recessed heaters with the building
construction, the Building Inspector shall be consulted for the proper installation methods to be
followed. Recessed heaters shall be installed in accordance with the manufacturers' instructions.
Recessed heaters shall be located so as not to cause a hazard to walls, floors, curtains,
furniture, doors, etc. Recessed heaters installed between a bathroom and adjoining room shall
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 58/336
not circulate air from the bathroom to other parts of the building. The gas line shall be a separate
line direct from the meter to the recessed heater, unless the existing gas line is of ample
capacity. A manual main shut-off valve shall be installed ahead of all controls including the pilot
gas valve. All parts of recessed heaters shall be easily accessible for cleaning and maintenance.
Panels, grilles, and access doors which must be removed for normal servicing operations shall
not be attached to the building construction. Adequate combustion and circulating air shall be
provided.
4. Floor Furnaces: Listed floor furnaces may be installed in combustible floors. Unlisted floor
furnaces shall not be installed in combustible floors. A separate manual main shut-off valve shall
be provided ahead of all controls and a union connection shall be provided downstream from this
valve to permit removal of the controls or the floor furnace.
Fixed ventilation by means of a duct or grille arranged to supply air from a permanently
ventilated attic or under floor space shall be provided to any confined space which encloses the
floor furnace.
The duct or grille shall be screened and have a free area of at least twice the area of the vent
collar, or one square inch per one thousand (1,000) BTU per hour of gas input, whichever is the
greater, and shall be installed in such a manner as to insure proper combustion. The following
are requirements that will serve in properly placing the furnace or furnaces to serve one story:
a. Floor Furnaces: No floor furnace shall be installed in the floor of any aisle or passageway of
any auditorium, public hall, or place of assembly, or in any exitway from any such room or
space.
b. Walls And Corners: With the exception of wall register models, a floor furnace shall not be
placed closer than six inches (6") to the nearest wall, and wall register models shall not be
placed closer than six inches (6") to a corner.
c. Draperies: The furnace shall be so placed that drapery or similar object cannot be nearer than
twelve inches (12") to any portion of the register of the floor furnace. No door shall open over
register of furnace.
d. Support: Floor around the furnace shall be braced and headed with a framework of material
not lighter than the joist. Means shall be provided to support the furnace when the floor grille is
removed.
e. Clearance: The lowest portion of the floor furnace shall have at least a six inch (6") clearance
from the general ground level, except where the lower six inch (6") portion of the floor furnace
is sealed by the manufacturer to prevent entrance of water, the clearance may be reduced to
not less than two inches (2"). Where these clearances are not present, the ground below and
to the side shall be excavated to form a "basin-like" pit under the furnace so that the required
clearance is provided beneath the lowest portion of the furnace. A twelve inch (12") clearance
shall be provided on all sides except the control side, which shall have on eighteen inch (18")
clearance.
f. Access: Provisions shall be made for access to the floor furnace by means of an opening in
the foundation wall of at least eighteen by twenty four inches (18" x 24") or through a trap door
of at least twenty four by twenty four inches (24" x 24"), located at some convenient point, and
a clear and unobstructed passageway to the floor furnace of at least eighteen inches high by
twenty four inches (18" x 24") wide. The Building Inspector should be consulted with reference
to the access facilities for service.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 59/336
g. Upper Floor Installation: Listed gas floor furnaces may be installed in an upper floor provided
that the furnace assembly projects below into a utility room, closet, garage or similar
nonhabitable space. The Building Inspector should be consulted prior to making such an
installation.
5. Duct Furnaces: The gas line shall be a separate line direct from the meter to the duct furnace,
unless the existing gas line is of ample capacity. Listed gas-fired duct furnaces shall be installed
with clearances of at least six inches (6") between adjacent walls, ceiling and floors of
combustible construction and the appliance, projecting flue box or draft hood except that duct
furnaces listed for installation at lesser clearances may be installed in accordance with their
listing. In no case shall the clearance be such as to interfere with the requirements for
combustion air and accessibility.
A duct furnace shall be accessible for cleaning and repair, and shall be firmly supported in
accordance with the manufacturer's instructions. The ducts connected to or enclosing duct
furnaces shall have removal access panels on both the upstream and downstream side of the
furnace. The controls and draft hoods shall be located in the same enclosure from which
combustion air is taken. Circulating air shall not be taken from the same enclosure in which the
furnace is located.
Duct furnaces when used in conjunction with a refrigeration system shall not be located
downstream from the evaporator coil.
6. Gas Fired Unit Heaters: Suspended type gas-fired unit heaters shall be safely and adequately
supported with due consideration given to their weight and vibration characteristics. Listed gasfired
unit heaters shall be installed with minimum clearances from combustible construction of
six inches (6") between the appliance, projecting flue box or draft hood and not less than
eighteen inches (18") at the sides and bottom unless listed for installation at lesser clearances.
The location of any unit heater or the duct work attached thereto shall be such that a negative
pressure will not be created in the room in which the unit heater is located. A unit heater shall
not be attached to a warm air duct system unless listed for such installation.
Unit heaters installed in garages for more than three (3) motor vehicles or in airplane hangars
shall be of a type listed for such use and shall be installed at least eight feet (8') above the floor.
E. Installation Of Gas-Fired Clothes Dryers: Listed clothes dryers shall be installed with a minimum
clearance of six inches (6") from adjacent combustible construction, except that clothes dryers
listed for installation at lesser clearances may be installed in accordance with their listing.
Moisture exhaust ducts shall be installed with clearances for high temperature duct systems in
accordance with the Standards for the Installation of Air Conditioning, Warm Air Heating, Air
Cooling and Ventilating Systems, NFPA-NBFU pamphlet No. 90 or the latest revision thereof.
A minimum clearance of eighteen inches (18") shall be provided between the lower surface of any
combustible material located above the dryer and the top of any other vent outlet not protected by
a two hundred fifty degrees (250?) Fahrenheit or lower limit control.
Gas-fired clothes dryers installed for multiple-family use shall be equipped with approved
automatic pilots.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 60/336
F. Installation Of Gas Refrigerators: Gas refrigerators shall be provided with adequate clearances for
ventilation at the top and back. They shall be installed in accordance with the manufacturer's
instructions. If such instructions are not available, at least two inches (2") shall be provided
between the back of the refrigerator and the wall, and at least a twelve inch (12") clearance above
the top.
G. Installation Of Gas-Fired Incinerators: Listed gas-fired incinerators shall be installed as close as
practicable to a chimney with at least twelve inches (12") clearance between sides and
combustible construction except that appliances listed for installation at lesser clearances may be
installed in accordance with their listing. In no case shall the clearance to combustible construction
be less than three inches (3") or be such as to interfere with the requirements for combustion air
and accessibility. The clarence above a charging door shall be not less than forty eight inches
(48"). Incinerators of wall type shall be installed in a non-combustible wall communicating directly
with a chimney flue.
No draft hood shall be connected into the flue pipe of an incinerator. Where conditions permit, it is
preferable to have the flue pipe connected to a separate chimney flue. Smoke pipes shall have at
least eighteen inches (18") clearance from combustible construction unless guarded by a
ventilated thimble twelve inches (12") larger in diameter than the flue or the vent connector.
H. Installation Of Gas Equipment In Large Boilers: These requirements shall be applicable to unlisted
steam or hot water boilers that have inputs in excess of four hundred thousand (400,000) BTU per
hour and which have a working pressure of not over fifteen (15) pounds per square inch, and
furnish steam, hot water or both, for either heating, processing or power purposes.
1. Combustion Air: In absence of the manufacturer's instructions, if combustion air is taken from
the space in which the boiler is located, an opening to the outside air shall be provided having an
area of 0.5 square feet or more for each one million (1,000,000) BTU per hour of gas burned.
2. Flues And Vent Connectors: Adequate means for limiting draft shall be installed for each boiler.
When a manually operated damper is used to limit draft, positive means shall be provided to lock
the damper in position. The manually operated damper shall be installed between the boiler and
any application of automatic or modulating draft limiting devices. Adjustable (modulating)
dampers, where used for fuel-air ratio control, shall be equipped with suitable located minimum
and maximum operating stops. The minimum operating stops for such dampers shall be located
to obtain sufficient air for complete combustion at the minimum burner input. These dampers
shall be counter-balanced to open in the event of breakage or failure of their operating means.
Automatically operated dampers where used on automatically lighted boilers shall be interlocked
with the burner input control to prevent lighting the burner unless the damper is open.
3. Burners: The main burner or burners and their component parts shall be installed according to
the manufacturer's instructions and shall be properly and firmly secured in place to maintain
correct alignment in normal use and shall be readily accessible for cleaning and inspection. The
burner or burners shall be so installed and adjusted that there will be no injurious flame
impingement on walls or heating surfaces in a manner that will cause incomplete combustion or
damage to boiler ports. Burners shall maintain complete and stable combustion at the minimum
rate of firing or during any sudden change in the gas-firing rate between maximum and minimum
rates.
4. Air Intakes: Air openings shall be provided of sufficient area to supply an adequate amount of air
for complete combustion under the specified draft conditions and at the maximum rate of firing.
The air shall be introduced in a manner so as to assure thorough mixing of the gas and air in
order to complete the combustion within the space provided. The continued safe combustion or
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 61/336
cut-off of the gas supply shall be assured for boilers having forced or induced draft, or both, in
the event of draft failure. For forced or induced draft installations, a mechanical timer shall be
used to require a fifteen (15) second purge period or the purging of three (3) times the volume of
combustion space and gas passages containing combustion gases up to the blower or damper,
whichever requires the largest volume of air, prior to pilot ignition after shut down. No spark or
ignition shall be allowed to occur in the fire box during the purging cycle. If the firing rate is
automatically changed, the gas-air ratio shall be automatically maintained to produce stable
combustion at all firing rates.
5. Pilots: An adequate gas pilot or pilots shall be used to assure ignition of the burner or burners.
For all automatically lighted boilers, an automatic pilot device or flame-safe guard so constructed
and installed that no gas can flow to the main burner or burner group unless satisfactory ignition
is assured shall be employed at each burner or group of burners operating as a unit. Gas to
main burners and to intermittent or ignition pilots shall be automatically shut off in case of flame
failure at point of supervision. The response time of the flame safeguard to de-energize the gas
shutoff device on flame failure shall not exceed five (5) seconds for boilers having inputs in
excess of two million five hundred thousand (2,500,000) BTU per hour. Pilots supervision by
such flame safeguard shall be only at the point where the flame will effectively ignite the gas at
the main burner or burners. Electric ignition systems shall ignite only a pilot. The input to the pilot
shall not exceed three percent (3%) of the maximum input to the main burner as fired. If ignition
of the pilot is not obtained within fifteen (15) seconds, the gas shall be turned off automatically.
Means shall be provided to permit ready observation of all pilot burners, flame safeguard units
and the main burner or burners while firing. Pilot burners shall be placed so that they can be
safely lighted manually, if required. The gas supply pressure to the pilot or group of pilots shall
be regulated independently of the main burner supply.
6. Manual Shut-Off Valves: Pilot lines shall be connected to vertical main as supply pipes or to the
sides or top of horizontal pipes upstream from all gas control valves and they shall be
independently controlled by a manually operated pilot shut-off valve. In multiple installations, a
manually operated pilot firing valve downstream from the pilot shut-off valve shall be provided for
each pilot. Each boiler burner assembly shall have a lubricated plug type main burner shut-off
valve with handle permanently attached which will shut off the gas to the burner and control
valve assembly. Each burner shall have a separate firing valve designed for the maximum
operating gas pressure on the burner.
7. Control Valves: All boiler input control valves and safety shut-off valves shall be installed
downstream from the main burner shut-off valves. For manually lighted boilers, reopening the
safety shut-off valve after it has closed shall require a manual operation. No wiring or control
shall be subjected to heat from the burner unless specifically designed to withstand such
temperatures. Automatically operated main burner input control valve assemblies on boilers
having inputs in excess of two million five hundred thousand (2,500,000) BTU per hour shall
provide for the firing rate during turn on to be more or less uniformly increased from minimum to
maximum in not less than five (5) seconds and shall provide for the firing rate during turn-off to
be more or less uniformly decreased from maximum to minimum in not less than three (3)
seconds. It is not intended that this time limitation apply to emergency safety shut-off valves
used in conjunction with a modulating control valve.
8. Gas Pressure Regulators: Where gas supply pressure is higher than that at which the burners
are designed to operate, a gas pressure regulator shall be employed. In no case shall a weight
and lever type of regulator be used. A gas pressure regulator, except a zero regulator used in
connection with air-gas mixers, requiring access to atmosphere for successful operation, shall
be vented to a safe location.
9. Limiting Devices: Automatically lighted boilers shall be equipped with safety devices arranged to
prevent excessive steam pressures of water temperatures and to prevent firing a dry boiler or
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 62/336
one in which the water is dangerously low by shutting off the gas. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-34: FLUE CONNECTIONS:
A. Appliances of the following types must be connected to an effective flue or vent:
1. Central heating appliances including steam and hot water boilers, warm air furnaces, floor
furnaces and vented recessed heaters.
2. Unit heaters, duct furnaces and gas-fired incinerators.
3. Water heaters with inputs in excess of five thousand (5,000) BTU per hour.
4. Room heaters listed for vented use only. This includes the, space heating section of gas ranges.
5. Room heaters installed in sleeping quarters for use of transients or in institutions such as homes
for the aged, sanitariums, convalescent homes, orphanages, etc. Such heaters must be
equipped with an automatic pilot.
6. Appliances equipped with gas conversion burners.
7. Appliances which have draft hoods supplied by the appliance manufacturer except room heaters
listed for either vented or unvented use.
B. The following listed appliances are not required to be vented except when any or all of the
appliances below are installed so that the total input rating exceeds thirty (30) BTU per hour per
cubic foot of room space in which located.
1. Gas ranges, hot plates, laundry stoves.
C. Every vented appliance, except incinerators, dual oven type combination ranges, and units
designed for power burners or for forced venting, shall have a draft hood. If the draft hood is not a
part of the appliance or supplied by the appliance manufacturer, it shall be supplied by the installer.
Where the draft hood is part of the appliance or is supplied by the appliance manufacturer, it shall
be installed without alterations in accordance with the manufacturer's instructions. In the absence
of manufacturer's instructions, the draft hood shall be attached to the flue collar of the appliance or
as near to the appliance as conditions permit. In no case shall a draft hood be installed in a false
ceiling, in a different room or in any manner that will permit a difference in pressure between the
draft hood relief opening and the combustion air supply.
D. The flue or vent to which the flue or vent connector is connected shall be of a size that is equal to
the size indicated by the vent collar of the appliance, but in no case shall the area of the vent be
less than the area of a three inch (3") diameter pipe. When more than one appliance vents into a
flue or vent, the flue or vent area shall not be less than the area of the largest flue or vent
connector plus fifty percent (50%) of the areas of the additional flue or vent connectors. An
elliptical flue or vent may be used provided its flue gas venting capacity is equal to the capacity of
round pipe for which it is substituted.
E. Automatic gas appliances shall not be connected to the same flue serving equipment for solid or
liquid fuel.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 63/336
F. The material used for vent pipe shall be of noncombustible, corrosion resistant, and of sufficient
thickness, cross-sectional area, and heat insulating quality to avoid excessive temperature on
adjacent combustible material, and certified by a nationally recognized testing agency. The manner
in which vents are run and passed through walls, partitions, attics, etc., shall meet the
specifications set by the American Standard Installation of Gas Piping and Gas Appliances in
Buildings, ASA Z21.30-1954, Part V, Venting, or the latest revision thereof.
G. The vent shall extend high enough above the building or other neighboring obstructions so that
wind from any direction will not strike the vent from an angle above horizontal. Unless the
obstruction is of great magnitude, it is the usual experience that a vent extended at least two feet
(2') above flat roofs or two feet (2') above the highest part of a wall parapets and peak roofs within
thirty feet (30') will be reasonably free from down drafts.
H. No manually operated damper shall be placed in any vent connector of any appliance having a
draft hood furnished by the manufacturer. Fixed baffles at the head of draft hoods are not classified
as dampers.
I. Before connecting a vent or vent connector, the installation shall be examined to ascertain that it is
properly constructed, clear, and will freely conduct the products of combustion to the outer air.
(Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-35: TESTS, INSPECTION AND CERTIFICATE OF INSPECTION:
A. When gas house piping has been installed in a building or structure, whether the same be new
construction, repairs or extensions, the same must be inspected and tested in the presence of the
Building Inspector or one of his assistants. After satisfactory test and inspection, an inspection tag
shall be attached to such piping.
B. Before any system of gas house piping is finally put in service, it shall be carefully tested to insure
that it is gas tight. Where any part of the system is to be enclosed or concealed, this test shall
precede the work of closing in. The piping must stand a pressure of air equal to that exerted by a
column of mercury six inches (6") high for a period of ten (10) minutes without showing any
pressure drop.
1. If the house piping will operate a pressure higher than one psig, the test pressure shall be at
least twice the pressure to which the piping will be subjected in operation.
2. No fire-test or water-test shall be permitted, and a water-tested gas piping shall be condemned
as faulty. In no case shall oxygen ever by used to test gas piping. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-36: DUTIES OF THE GAS COMPANY:
A. It shall be unlawful for the Gas Company to turn gas into any new or altered or repaired system of
gas piping until a certificate of inspection has been provided, but when the Building Inspector has
certified to the inspection herein provided, no further inspection by the Gas Company shall be
required; however, the Gas Company may elect to perform shut-in tests.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 64/336
B. Before turning gas under pressure into any piping, the person turning on the gas shall assure
himself that there are no openings from which the gas can escape.
C. Before leaving the premises, all air must be purged from piping and appliances.
D. Every person learning of a leak or defect in any gas piping or appliance shall forthwith report all
facts in connection therewith by phone to the Building Inspector. The Building Inspector shall
thereupon inspect all gas equipment at location named in such report, and if he finds leaks or
defects, he may order the Gas Company to turn off the gas, and it shall be unlawful thereafter for
the Gas Company to turn the gas on again until the Building Inspector has certified that such leak
or defect has been repaired or removed. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-37: DEFINITION OF TERMS:
When used in this Chapter, these terms shall have the following meaning:
APPLIANCE: A gas appliance which utilizes gas fuel to produce light, heat or power.
AUTOMATICALLY CONTROLLED: Appliances equipped with an automatic device which:
A. Accomplishes complete turn-on or shut-off gas to the main burner or burners or
B.Graduates the gas supply to the burner or burners, but does not effect complete shut-off of the
gas.
BTU: The abbreviation for British Thermal Unit. The quantity of heat required to raise the temperature
of one pound of water one degree Fahrenheit.
CENTRAL HEATING APPLIANCE: A gas appliance normally used as the primary means of heating
premises, including gas boilers, warm-air furnaces, and floor furnaces, but not unit heaters, space
heaters, or industrial boilers.
DIVERSITY FACTOR: The ratio of the maximum probable demand to the maximum possible demand.
DRAFT HOOD: A device placed in and made a part of the flue pipe or the appliance itself, which is
designed to:
A. Insure the ready escape of the products of combustion in the event of no draft, back draft or
stoppage beyond the draft hood;
B. Prevent a back draft from entering the appliance and
C. Neutralize the effect of stack action or draft of the chimney flue upon the operation of the
appliances.
FLEXIBLE TUBING: A gas conduit which depends for tightness on joint packing or on any wall
structure other than that formed by a continuous one piece metallic tubing member.
FLUE: The general term for the passages and conduits through which flue gases pass from the
combustion chamber to the outer air.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 65/336
GAS UNDER PRESSURE: Gas in piping or appliance which is under pressure imparted from the
source of the gas supply.
HEATING VALUE TOTAL: The number of British Thermal Units produced by the combustion, at
constant pressure, of one cubic foot of gas when the products of combustion are cooled to the initial
temperature of the gas and air, when the water vapor formed during combustion is condensed, and
when all the necessary corrections have been applied.
HOUSE PIPING: The gas piping beyond the outlet of the meter and extending to the appliance or the
appliance connector.
LIQUEFIED PETROLEUM GAS: A liquid containing certain combination of hydrocarbons consisting of
butane, propane and mixtures thereof which may be liquefied at atmospheric temperatures without
excessive pressure and will completely vaporize upon release at atmospheric pressure.
LISTED APPLIANCES AND ACCESSORIES: The word "listed" used in connection with appliances
and accessories throughout this Chapter refers to appliances and accessories which are shown in a
list published by an approved nationally recognized testing agency (The American Gas Association,
Inc., Laboratories and Underwriter's Laboratories, Inc., are such nation-ally recognized testing
agencies), qualified and equipped for experimental testing, and maintaining an adequate periodic
inspection of current production of listed models and whose listing states either that the appliance or
accessory complies with nationally recognized safety requirements or has been tested and found safe
for use in a specified manner.
METER: The instrument installed to measure the volume of gas delivered through it.
PILOT: A small flame which is utilized to ignite the gas at the main burner or burners.
PROTECTIVE COATING: Iron and steel pipe which has been thoroughly cleaned, primed, painted
with asphalt or coal tar, and wrapped with asbestos or coal tar, shall be considered pipe with
protective coating.
REGULATOR: A device for controlling and maintaining a uniform gas supply pressure.
RIGID CONNECTION: Any wrought iron or steel pipe and/or fitting which complies with the American
Standards Association standard B36.10-1950, or its latest revision, used to connect gas burning
equipment.
SEMI-RIGID A gas conduit having semi-flexible metallic wall TUBING: structure.
SERVICE PIPE: The pipe which brings the gas from the gas main to the meter.
WET GAS: Raw, casinghead gas, residue gas or any gas not conforming to standards of the
distribution of gas or gas not suitable for use in the gas distributor's equipment for maintaining uniform
pressure, desired heating content, or proper ordorization.
In addition to the provisions of this Chapter, the regulations of the State of Idaho General Order No. 98
and the provisions of the National Board of Fire Underwriters are to be fulfilled in any gas installation.
Such regulations and provisions take precedence over the provisions of this Chapter in the event of
conflict. (Ord. 372, 1-7-1957)
4-5-38: VIOLATIONS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 66/336
Any person who violates, causes or permits any violation of the provisions of this Chapter shall be
deemed guilty of an offense and subject to the punishment as prescribed in this Code. Each such
person shall be deemed guilty of a separate offense for every day during which any violation of any
provision of this Chapter is committed, continued or permitted by such person and shall be punishable
therefor as provided herein.
A. The issuance or granting of a permit or approval of plans and specifications shall not be deemed or
construed to be a permit for or an approval of any violation of any provision of this Chapter. No
permit presuming to give authority to violate or cancel the provisions of this Chapter shall be valid,
except insofar as the work or use which it authorizes is lawful.
B. The issuance of a permit upon plans and specifications shall not prevent the Building Inspector
from thereafter requiring the correction of errors in said plans and specification or from preventing
construction operations being carried on thereunder when in violation of this Chapter or of any
other provision of this Code.
C. Every permit issued by the Building Inspector under the provisions of this Chapter shall expire by
limitation and become null and void if the work authorized by such permit is not commenced within
sixty (60) days from the date of such permit, or if the work authorized by such permit is suspended
or abandoned at any time after the work is commenced for a period of sixty (60) days. Before such
work can be recommenced a new permit shall be first obtained to do so.
D. Exception: When work has to be suspended on account of abnormal weather conditions, acute
shortage of labor and/or materials, strikes or public emergency beyond the control of the permittee,
the Building Inspector may grant such an extension of time as he deems necessary. Any request
for an extension of time must be made in writing by the permittee and filed office of the Building
Inspector. (Ord. 372; 1-7-1957)

There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing rules and regulations for the construction,
alteration, removal, demolition, equipment, use and occupancy, location and maintenance of buildings
and structures, that certain Housing Code known as the Uniform Housing Code, copyrighted by the

hereby adopted and incorporated as fully as if set out at length herein and the provisions thereof shall
be controlling in the construction of all buildings and other structures. (1970 Code)
Chapter 7
AWNINGS
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.

4-7-1: HEIGHT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to construct, have, keep, maintain or place an awning on buildings
and structures abutting on the streets in any manner so that any part of such awning attached to said

Chapter 8
BILLBOARDS
4-8-1: BILLBOARDS TO BE KEPT ORDERLY:
All persons engaged in the business or occupation of bill posting, bill distributing, sign tacking, sign,
wall or bulletin painting, shall keep all billboards, sign or bulletin boards or outdoor advertising
contrivances or devices, free and clean of loose paper or other rubbish and not suffer or permit any
paper or any other material from any such billboard, sign or bulletin board or outdoor advertising
contrivance or device to become scattered, blown or deposited in or about any street or alley or other
public place. (3-605; 1947 Code)
4-8-2: THROWING ADVERTISING PROHIBITED:
The throwing of any form of advertising matter, such as dodgers, handbills, circulars, samples or like
matter on any lawn or parking is strictly prohibited. All such advertising matter must be placed inside
the screen or immediately under the door, or in the jamb of the door or in a receptacle provided for the
receipt of such advertising matter. (3-606; 1947 Code)
4-8-3: NONCOMPLYING BILLBOARDS:
If the inspecting officer shall find that any billboard, sign or bulletin board or other structure for
advertising now or hereafter erected is erected or maintained in an unsafe, unsecured or
unsatisfactory manner, he may order the same repaired and if not so repaired within ten (10) days
from the date of said order he must report such facts to the Council who shall, if it finds the report of
the inspecting officer correct, order the permit of the person owning or operating such unsafe,
unsecure or unsatisfactory or unsightly billboard, sign or bulletin board or other contrivance for
advertising purposes revoked. All such billboards, signs or bulletin boards or other contrivances for
outdoor advertising purposes, must have placed and maintained on the top of each, the name of the
person owning same, or who is in possession or control thereof. (3-607; 1947 Code)
4-8-4: ADVERTISING SIGNS:
No sign, tags, sheet display or bulletin painting shall be placed on any walls, fences, roofs or buildings
or other structures other than billboards, sign or bulletin boards constructed and erected according to
the provisions of Section 4-8-5 of this Chapter, provided that nothing in this Chapter shall be construed
to apply to the posting of regular notices by public officers, nor the right of any newspaper of regular
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 68/336
issue to distribute its papers throughout the City, nor to any merchant advertising his own business by
the distribution of circulars, nor the placing as required by law of wood, lettered, painted, metal or
electric signs over, upon or in front of business buildings, offices, houses, etc., for advertising the
name or business of any person occupying same, or the goods sold therein or the signs of real estate
firms, advertising the property on which said signs are located for sale or rent. (3-608; 1947 Code)
4-8-5: BILLBOARDS; SPECIFICATIONS:
All billboards, signs or bulletin boards shall not exceed eleven feet (11') in height, clear posting
painting or display surface, and shall be constructed in a good substantial and workmanlike manner,
and kept and maintained in a safe and secure condition at all times. All billboards, sign or bulletin
boards hereafter erected shall be constructed of galvanized iron or some other equally
noncombustible material, except that the stringers, uprights and braces may be of Oregon fir or some
other equally strong or durable material, and all such billboards, signs or bulletin boards shall be
wholly within the property lines. No billboard, sign or bulletin board shall hereafter be placed, affixed to
nor upon the roof of any building except such as are constructed of well braced iron or steel and
properly equipped with electric lights in a manner directed by the Building Inspector or some other
designated person. (3-604; 1947 Code)
Chapter 9
BUILDING CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITIES; REGULATIONS
4-9-1: DUST CONTROL:
Every person, engaged in the construction of buildings and other improvements shall use such means
and methods, as may be necessary, so as to lay any dust and prevent the same from arising from
such premises.
A violation of Section 4-9-1 shall be and constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable as
provided by Section 1-4-6 of the City Code. (Ord. 518, 7-19-1979)
Chapter 10
FLOOD HAZARD REGULATIONS
4-10-1: STATUTORY AUTHORIZATION:
The legislature of the state has in title 50, chapter 3 and title 67, chapter 65, delegated the
responsibility to local governmental units to adopt regulations designed to promote the public health,
safety and general welfare of its citizenry. (Ord. 592, 10-3-1994)
4-10-2: FINDINGS OF FACT:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 69/336
A. The flood hazard areas of the city are subject to periodic inundation which results in loss of life and
property, health and safety hazards, disruption of commerce and government services,
extraordinary public expenditures for flood protection and relief and impairment of the tax base, all
of which adversely affect the public health, safety and general welfare.
B. These flood losses are caused by the cumulative effect of obstructions in areas of special flood
hazards which increase flood heights and velocities, and when inadequately anchored, damage
uses in other areas. Uses that are inadequately floodproofed, elevated or otherwise protected from
flood damage also contribute to the flood loss. (Ord. 592, 10-3-1994)
4-10-3: STATEMENT OF PURPOSE:
It is the purpose of this chapter to promote the public health, safety and general welfare, and to
minimize public and private losses due to flood conditions in specific areas by provisions designed to:
A. Protect human life and health;
B. Minimize expenditure of public money for costly flood control projects;
C. Minimize the need for rescue and relief efforts associated with flooding and generally undertaken at
the expense of the general public;
D. Minimize prolonged business interruptions;
E. Minimize damage to public facilities and utilities such as water and gas mains, electric, telephone
and sewer lines, and streets and bridges located in areas of special flood hazard;
F. Help maintain a stable tax base by providing for the second use and development of areas of
special flood hazard so as to minimize future flood blight areas;
G. Ensure that potential buyers are notified that property is in an area of special flood hazard; and
H. Ensure that those who occupy the areas of special flood hazard assume responsibility for their
actions. (Ord. 592, 10-3-1994)
4-10-4: METHOD OF REDUCING FLOOD LOSSES:
In order to accomplish its purpose, this chapter includes methods and provisions for:
A. Restricting or prohibiting uses which are dangerous to health, safety and property due to water or
erosion hazards, or which result in damaging increases in erosion or in flood heights or velocities;
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 70/336
B. Requiring that uses vulnerable to floods, including facilities which serve such uses, be protected
against flood damage at the time of initial construction;
C. Controlling the alteration of natural flood plains, streams, channels and natural protective barriers,
which help accommodate or channel flood waters;
D. Controlling filling, grading, dredging and other development which may increase flood damage; and
E. Preventing or regulating the construction of flood barriers which will unnaturally divert flood waters
or which may increase flood hazards in other areas. (Ord. 592, 10-3-1994)
4-10-5: DEFINITIONS:
Unless specifically defined below, words or phrases used in this Chapter shall be interpreted so as to
give them the meaning they have in common usage and to give this Chapter its most reasonable
application.
AREA OF SPECIAL FLOOD HAZARD: The land in the flood plain within a community subject to a one
percent (1%) or greater chance of flooding in any given year, which are designated on maps as Zone
A or V.
BASE FLOOD: The flood having a one percent (1%) chance of being equalled or exceeded in any
given year.
DEVELOPMENT: Any man-made change to improved or unimproved real estate, including, but not
limited to, buildings or other structures, mining, dredging, filling, grading, paving, excavation or drilling
operations located within the area of special flood hazard.
FLOOD or FLOODING: A general and temporary condition of partial or complete inundation of
normally dry land areas from:
A. The overflow of inland or tidal waters; and/or
B. The unusual and rapid accumulation of runoff of surface waters from any source.
FLOOD HAZARD BOUNDARY MAP (FHBM): An official map issued by the Federal Insurance
Administration where the areas of special flood hazard have been designated Zone A or V.
LOWEST FLOOR: The lowest floor of the lowest enclosed area (including basement). An unfinished
or flood resistant enclosure, usable solely for parking vehicles, building access or storage, in an area
other than a basement area, is not considered a building's lowest floor, provided that such enclosure
is not built so as to render the structure in violation of the applicable nonelevation design requirements
of this Chapter found at subsection 4-10-8B1.
MANUFACTURED HOME: A structure that is transportable in one or more sections, which is built on a
permanent chassis, and is designed for use with or without a permanent foundation when connected
to the required utilities. For flood plain management purposes the term "manufactured home" also
includes park trailers, travel trailers, and other similar vehicles placed on a site for greater than one
hundred eighty (180) consecutive days. For insurance purposes the term "manufactured home" does
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 71/336
not include park trailers, travel trailers and other similar vehicles.
STRUCTURE: A walled and roofed building or mobile home, or a gas or liquid storage tank, that is
principally above ground.
SUBSTANTIAL IMPROVEMENT: Any repair, reconstruction or improvement of a structure the cost of
which equals or exceeds fifty percent (50%) of the market value of the structure either before the
improvement or repair is started or if the structure has been damaged and is being restored, before
the damage occurred.
For the purposes of this definition, "substantial improvement" is considered to occur when the first
alteration of any wall, ceiling, floor or other structural part of the building commences, whether or not
the alteration affects the external dimensions of the structure.
The term does not, however, include either:
A. Any project for improvement of a structure to comply with existing State or local health, sanitary
or safety code specifications which are solely necessary to assure safe living conditions; or
B. Any alteration of a structure listed on the National Register of Historic Places or a State
Inventory of Historic Places. (Ord. 592, 10-3-1994)
4-10-6: GENERAL PROVISIONS:
A. Lands Affected: This Chapter shall apply to all areas of special flood hazards within the jurisdiction
of the City.
B. Basis For Establishing Areas Of Special Flood Hazard: The areas of special flood hazard identified
by the Federal Insurance Administration in a scientific and engineering report entitled "The Flood
Insurance Study for the City of Gooding", dated December 14, 1984, with accompanying flood
insurance maps is hereby adopted by reference and declared to be a part of this Chapter. The
flood insurance study is now on file at City Hall, 308 5th Avenue West, Gooding, Idaho.
C. Abrogation And Greater Restrictions: This Chapter is not intended to repeal, abrogate or impair any
existing easements, covenants or deed restrictions. However, where this Chapter and another
ordinance, easement, covenant or deed restriction conflict or overlap, whichever imposes the more
stringent restrictions shall prevail.
D. Interpretation: In the interpretation and application of this Chapter, all provisions shall be:
1. Considered as minimum requirements;
2. Liberally construed in favor of the governing body; and
3. Deemed neither to limit or repeal any other powers granted under State statutes.
E. Warning And Disclaimer Of Liability: The degree of flood protection required by this Chapter is
considered reasonable for regulatory purposes and is based on scientific and engineering
considerations.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 72/336
Larger floods can and will occur on rare occasions. Flood heights may be increased by man-made
or natural causes. This Chapter does not imply that land outside the areas of special flood hazards
or uses permitted within such areas will be free from flooding or flood dam-ages. This Chapter
shall not create liability on the part of the City, any officer or employee thereof or the Federal
Insurance Administration for any flood damages that result from reliance on this Chapter or any
administrative decision lawfully made thereunder. (Ord 592, 10-3-1994)
4-10-7: ADMINISTRATION:
A. Development Permit:
1. Permit Required: A development permit shall be obtained before construction or development
begins within any area of special flood hazard established in subsection 4-10-6B. The permit
shall be for all structures, including manufactured homes, as set forth in Section 4-10-5 of this
Chapter and for all development including fill and other activities, also as set forth in Section 4-
10-5 of this Chapter.
2. Application For Permit: Application for a development permit shall be made on forms furnished
by the Building Inspector and may include, but not be limited to: plans in duplicate drawn to
scale showing the nature, location, dimensions and evaluations of the area in question; existing
or proposed structures, fill storage of materials, drainage facilities and the location of the
foregoing. Specifically, the flooding information required is:
a. Elevation in relation to mean sea level, of the lowest floor (including basement) of all
structures;
b. Elevation in relation to mean sea level to which any structure has been floodproofed;
c. Certification by a registered professional engineer or architect that the floodproofing methods
for any nonresidential structure meet the floodproofing criteria in subsection 4-10-882; and
d. Description of the extent to which any watercourse will be altered or relocated as a result of
proposed development.
B. Designation Of Administrator: The Building Inspector is hereby appointed to administer and
implement this Chapter by granting or denying development permit applications in accordance with
its provisions.
C. Duties And Responsibilities Of Administrator: Duties of the Building Inspector shall include, but not
be limited to:
1. Permit Review:
a. Review all development permits to determine that the permit requirements of this Chapter
have been satisfied.
b. Review all development permits to determine that all necessary permits have been obtained
from those Federal, State or local governmental agencies from which prior approval is
required.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 73/336
c. Review all development permits to determine if the proposed development is located in the
floodway. If located in the floodway, assure that the encroachment provisions of subsection 4-
10-8C1 are met.
(1) If it is determined that there is no adverse effect, then the permit shall be granted
consistent with the provisions of this Chapter.
(2) If it is determined that there is an adverse effect, then flood damage mitigation measures
shall be made a condition of the permit.
2. Use Of Other Base Flood Data: When base flood evaluation data has not been provided in
accordance with subsection 4-10-6B "Basis For Establishing Areas Of Special Flood Hazard",
the Building Inspector shall obtain, review and reasonably utilize any base flood evaluation and
floodway data available from a Federal, State or other source, in order to administer subsection
4-10-8B, "Specific Standards" and subsection 4-10-8C, "Floodways".
3. Information To Be Obtained And Maintained:
a. Where base flood elevation data is provided through the Flood Insurance Study or required as
in subsection 4-10-7C2 herein, obtain and record the actual elevation (in relation to mean sea
level) of the lowest floor (including basement) of all new or substantially improved structures,
and whether or not the structure contains a basement.
b. For all new or substantially improved floodproofed structures:
(1) Obtain and record the actual elevation (in relation to mean sea level) to which the structure
has been floodproofed;
(2) Maintain the floodproofing certifications required in subsection 4-10-7Alc.
c. Maintain for public inspection, all records pertaining to the provisions of this Chapter.
4. Alteration Of Watercourses:
a. Notify adjacent communities and the Idaho Department of Resources prior to any alteration or
relocation of a watercourse and submit evidence of such notification to the Federal Insurance
Administration.
b. Require that maintenance is provided within the altered or relocated portion of said
