however, that nothing herein contained shall be deemed to prohibit or restrict the free admission of
police officers engaged in the performance of police duties to any place of public entertainment or
amusement. (1970 Code)
6-1-2: ASSAULT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit "assault" which is hereby defined as any conduct which
places another in reasonable apprehension of receiving a battery. (1970 Code)
6-1-3: ASSEMBLY, UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful for two (2) or more persons to assemble together for the purpose of disturbing the
peace or for the purpose of committing an unlawful act and not to disperse upon the command of an
officer so to do. (1970 Code)
6-1-4: BARBED WIRE AND ELECTRIC FENCES:
(Rep. by Ord. 679, 12-3-2012)
6-1-5: BATTERY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit battery. A person commits battery if he: a) intentionally or
knowingly without legal justification and by any means causes bodily harm to an individual, or b)
makes physical contact of an insulting or provoking nature with an individual. (1970 Code)
6-1-6: BIRDS; INJURY TO:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 105/336
It shall be unlawful for any person to kill or wound, or attempt or kill or wound, by use of a firearm,
slingshot, bow and arrow or otherwise, any bird other than English sparrows, or to take the eggs or
young of any bird. (1970 Code)
6-1-7: BURGLAR TOOLS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his possession any nippers of any description known as
burglar's nippers, picklock, skeleton key, jimmy or other burglar's instrument or tool of any description,
unless it be shown that the possession is innocent or for a lawful purpose. (1970 Code)
6-1-8: CIGARETTES OR TOBACCO, SALE OF TO MINORS:
A. It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or give away, directly or indirectly, to any person under the
age of eighteen (18) years any cigarettes, tobacco, or any compounds of tobacco used in filling up
or making up of a cigarette or to give or sell any cigarette papers to minors.
B. It shall be unlawful for any person under eighteen (18) years of age to buy, accept, or have in his or
her possession any cigarette, cigar or tobacco in any form or to buy, accept or have in his or her
possession any cigarette paper or other wrapper intended for the wrapping of tobacco in the form
of a cigarette or to have in his or her possession any compounds of tobacco used in the filling or
makeup of cigarettes. (Ord. 536, 10-5-1981)
6-1-9: COHABITATION, LEWD:
It shall be unlawful for any man or woman not being married to each other, to live and cohabit together
as man and wife, or lewdly and notoriously to associate together. (1970 Code)
6-1-10: COLLECTING CROWDS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to collect within the city a crowd of people to the annoyance of the
citizens thereof or to the annoyance or injury of the public. (1970 Code)
6-1-11: CONCEALING KNOWLEDGE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to conceal knowledge of the commission of any offense or to
conceal knowledge of any unlawful act as defined in this code. (1970 Code)
6-1-12: CONTRACEPTIVES, SALE OF:
A. It shall be unlawful for any person to vend, sell, distribute or give away in any manner whatsoever
any article, drug or medical preparation, manufactured, produced or intended for use, or which
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 106/336
may be used as a contraceptive; provided however, that the provisions hereof shall not apply to
regularly licensed practitioners of medicine, or drugstores employing a registered pharmacist.
B. It shall be unlawful to vend, sell, give away or distribute any such articles, drugs or medicines for
use as, or possible for use as, contraceptives, by means of machines, or peddling or canvassing
within the city. The proprietor of any premises wherein any such drugs, medicines, or articles are
kept, contrary to the provisions of this section shall be presumed to be the vendor or distributor of
the medicines, drugs or articles. (1970 Code)
6-1-13: CRUELTY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to cruelly or inhumanely whip, injure, beat or mistreat his own wife,
child, stepchild or apprentice, or other child under his care. (1970 Code)
6-1-14: DELINQUENCY, ENCOURAGING:
It shall be unlawful for any person by any act or neglect to encourage, aid or cause a child to come
within the purview of the juvenile authorities; and it shall likewise be unlawful for any person after such
notice that a driver's license of any child has been suspended or revoked to permit such child to
operate a motor vehicle during the period that such driver's license is suspended. (1970 Code)
6-1-15: DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
A. Any person who shall be guilty of any violent, noisy, riotous or disorderly conduct, or who shall use
any profane, abusive or obscene language, or in any way commit a breach of the peace, or do
anything that shall be offensive to the senses or dangerous to the peace of the inhabitants of the
City shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor.
B. Every person shall be guilty of disorderly conduct when he:
1. Solicits anyone to engage in, or engages in, lewd or dissolute conduct in any public place or in
any place open to the public or exposed to public view; or
2. Accosts other persons in any public place or in any place open to the public for the purpose of
begging or soliciting alms; or
3. Loiters in, about or upon any street, alley or other public way or public place, or in any place
open to the public, without lawful business and conducting himself in a lewd, wanton or
lascivious manner in speech or behavior; or
4. Has upon her person or in his possession any instrument, tool or other implement for picking
locks or pockets or any implement that is usually employed or that reasonably may be inferred to
have been designed to be employed in the commission of any felony, misdemeanor or the
violation of any ordinance, and who shall fail to account for the possession of same; or
5. Loiters, remains, or wanders upon the streets or from place to place without apparent reason or
business and who refuses to identify himself and to account for his presence when requested by
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 107/336
a police officer so to do, if the surrounding circumstances are such to indicate to a reasonable
man that the public safety demands such identification; or
6. Occupies, lodges or sleeps in any building, structure or place, whether public or private, or any
automobile, truck, railroad car or other similar vehicles or equipment without the permission of
the owner or person entitled to the possession or in control thereof; or
7. Is found in any public place or in any place open to the public or exposed to public view under
the influence of intoxicating liquor or any drug or any substance defined as a poison and
regulated as a poison, pursuant to the provisions of chapter 27, title 37, Idaho Code, or under
the influence of any combination of any intoxicating liquor, drug or substances, in such a
condition that he is unable to exercise care for his own safety or the safety of others, or by
reason of his being under the influence of intoxicating liquor, or any drug or the influence of any
substance as defined and regulated by said chapter 27 of title 37, Idaho Code, or under the
influence of any combination of any intoxicating liquor, drug or any such substance, interferes
with or obstructs the free use of any street, sidewalk or other public way or any place open to the
public or exposed to public view; or
8. Loiters, prowls or wanders upon the private property of another, without visible or lawful
business with the owner or occupants thereof; or
9. Loiters or remains in or about a school, not having any reason or relationship involving custody
of or responsibility for a pupil or student, or any other specific, legitimate reason for the same.
C. A person shall commit a misdemeanor if he loiters, prowls, remains or wanders in a place, at a time
or in a manner not usual for law-abiding individuals under circumstances that warrant alarm for the
safety of persons or property in the vicinity. Among the circumstances which may be considered in
determining whether such alarm is warranted is the fact that the actor takes flight upon appearance
of a police officer, refuses to identify himself or manifestly endeavors or by deliberate furtive action,
attempts to conceal himself or any object. Unless flight by the actor or other circumstances make it
impracticable, a police officer shall, prior to any arrest for an offense under this Section, afford the
actor an opportunity to dispel any alarm which would otherwise be warranted, by requesting him to
identify himself and explain his presence and conduct. No person shall be convicted of an offense
under this Section if the police officer did not comply with the preceding sentence, or if it appears
at trial that the explanation given by the actor was true and, if believed by the police officer at the
time, would have dispelled the alarm.
D. Any person who commits any of the acts prescribed and defined by subsections B1 through B9 of
this Section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 506, 9-5-1978)
6-1-16: DISTURBING THE PEACE:
It shall be unlawful for any person, wilfully, maliciously, intentionally or unnecessarily, to disturb the
peace and quiet of another or of any neighborhood or family or religious congregation or other
assembly by loud or unusual noises or indecent behavior or by offensive or unbecoming conduct or for
any person to threaten, quarrel, fight or provoke an assault or battery or curse or swear or utter any
obscene or vulgar or indecent language in the presence of another. (1970 Code)
6-1-17: DRUNKENNESS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 108/336
It shall be unlawful for any person to be found drunk, intoxicated or under the influence of intoxicating
liquor upon any public thoroughfare or other public place. (1970 Code)
6-1-18: ESCAPE, AID IN:
It shall be unlawful for any person to aid or assist any person to escape from lawful confinement or to
assist any person to escape from the custody of any peace officer. (1970 Code)
6-1-19: ESCAPES:
It shall be unlawful for any person convicted of any offense or in lawful custody to escape or attempt to
escape from custody. (1970 Code)
6-1-20: EXPECTORATING ON SIDEWALK OR IN PUBLIC BUILDINGS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to expectorate or spit upon any sidewalk or upon the floor of any
public building or room used for public assemblies. (1970 Code)
6-1-21: FALSE PRETENSES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to obtain any food, drink, goods, wares or merchandise under false
pretenses, or to enter any public place and call for refreshments or other articles and receive and
refuse to pay for same, or depart without paying for or satisfying the person from whom he received
the food, goods, wares and merchandise. (1970 Code)
6-1-22: FALSE REPRESENTATION:
It shall be unlawful for any person to represent falsely himself to be an officer of the City or who shall
attempt to impersonate any such officer or who shall without authority perform any official act therein
on behalf of an officer. (1970 Code)
6-1-23: GENERAL OFFENSE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit any act or fail to perform any requirement which is
prohibited or required by State law, insofar as such laws are applicable to municipal government.
(1970 Code)
6-1-24: HYPNOTISTS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to practice hypnotism or for any person to be a subject for such
hypnotist provided that this shall not apply to hypnotism as used in the treatment of patients by an
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 109/336
accredited Doctor of Medicine or Doctor of Dentistry nor shall it prohibit the teaching of hypnotism in
any state accredited educational institution which maintains an academic standard of the college level.
(1970 Code)
6-1-25: INDECENT EXPOSURE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to appear in a state of nudity or in any indecent or lewd dress or
condition in any public place or in any such place to make any indecent exposure of his or her person
or private parts thereof or the private parts of another or to conduct himself in a lewd or lascivious
manner or to appear in any such place in a dress not belonging to his sex. (1970 Code)
6-1-26: INJURIOUS MATERIAL ON THOROUGHFARES, DEPOSITS OF:
It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit, place or allow to remain in or upon any public
thoroughfare any material or substance injurious to person or property. (1970 Code)
6-1-27: JUNK, KEEPING OF RESTRICTED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to store or keep any old articles or materials which may be
classified as junk adjacent to or in close proximity to any schoolhouse, church, public parks, public
grounds, business buildings or residences without first providing proper and tight buildings for the
storage of the same. (1970 Code)
6-1-28: LETTING PREMISES FOR UNLAWFUL PURPOSES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to rent, use or allow to be used any building or property owned by
him, for any purpose whereby riotous or disorderly persons are gathered. (1970 Code)
6-1-29: LIQUOR; AGE MISREPRESENTATION1:
A. It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of nineteen (19) years to, by any means, represent
to any person licensed to sell beer or intoxicating liquor, or to any agent or employee of such retail
licensee, that he is nineteen (19) or more years of age for the purpose of inducing such retail
licensee, his agent or employee, to sell, serve or dispense beer or intoxicating liquor to him.
B. It shall be unlawful for any person to, by any means, represent to any such retail licensee, his agent
or employee, that any other person is nineteen (19) or more years of age, when in fact such other
person is under the age of nineteen (19) years, for the purpose of inducing such retail licensee, his
agent or employee, to sell, serve or dispense beer or intoxicating liquor to such other person. (Ord.
471, 9-16-1974)
6-1-30: LOUD SPEAKERS OR SOUND TRUCKS:

https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 110/336
It shall be unlawful to play, operate, or use any device known as a sound truck, loud speaker or sound

character which emits loud and raucous noises and is attached to and upon any vehicle unless such
person in charge of such vehicle shall have first applied to and received permission from the Chief of

6-1-31: LUG WHEELS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for tractors with wheels injurious to pavement to be permitted upon the public
thoroughfares unless the operator of such vehicle shall first plank such streets. (1970 Code)
6-1-32: MINORS IN POOL, BILLIARD HALLS:
It shall be unlawful for any minor under the age of twenty (20) years to enter, remain or loiter in or
around a pool or billiard hall or in any room or rooms wherein such amusement is carried on or
maintained. (Ord. 332, 2-18-1952)
6-1-33: MUFFLERS; UNNECESSARY NOISE2:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a motor vehicle which shall not at all times be equipped
with a muffler upon the exhaust thereof in good working order and in constant operation to prevent
excessive or unusual noise and it shall be unlawful for any person operating any motor vehicle to use
a cutout, by-pass or similar muffler elimination appliance. (1970 Code)
6-1-34: OBSCENE CONDUCT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to urinate or stool in any place open to the public view, or to be
guilty of any lewd, lascivious or obscene conduct or to sing any lewd or obscene song, ballad or other
words in any public place or any other place where other persons are present or indecently to exhibit
any animals. (1970 Code)
6-1-35: OBSCENE LITERATURE, DISTRIBUTION OF:
It shall be unlawful for any person to exhibit, pass, give or deliver to another any obscene, lewd or
indecent book, pamphlet, picture, card, print, paper, writing, mold, cast, or figure or to have same in
his possession. (19790 Code)
6-1-36: OBSTRUCTING STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct or cause to be obstructed any of the sidewalks, streets
or alleys without first having obtained permission to do so from the Chief of Police or Street
Commissioner. (Ord. 367, 12-5-1955)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 111/336
6-1-37: OFFENSE, AID TO AN:
It shall be unlawful for any person, in any way or manner, to aid, abet, counsel, advise or encourage
any other person in the commission of any of the acts mentioned herein or in any manner encourage
the commission of such offense hereby defined. (1970 Code)
6-1-38: PETIT THEFT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit petit theft which is hereby defined as a theft when the
property taken is of a value of less than one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00). (1970 Code)
6-1-39: PLAYING BALL ON STREETS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to play ball or throw any ball to and fro upon any public
thoroughfare in the City. (1970 Code)
6-1-40: PICKETING:
It shall be unlawful for any person, not an employee, past, present or expectant of the owner or
proprietor of the business attempted to be picketed and who has no personal dispute with the owner
or proprietor concerning terms and conditions of employment to stand, sit or walk on any street or
sidewalk in the City with the intent and purpose of dissuading or discouraging any person from
patronizing the place of business. (1970 Code)
6-1-41: PICNICS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to rent, use or allow to be used any yard, ground or grave or other
real estate within the City for public picnics or open air dances, to be conducted in such manner as to
be on annoyance or injury to the public. (1970 Code)
6-1-42: POLICE OFFICERS, ASSISTANCE TO:
It shall be unlawful for any male citizen over the age of eighteen (18) years to refuse or neglect to
render assistance to any police officer when called upon for such assistance or aid in the suppression
of riot or other unlawful assemblage or in the arrest of any person who has committed an offense.
(1970 Code)
6-1-43: POSTING BILLS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to paste, post, paint, print or nail any handbill, sign, poster,
advertisement or notice of any kind on any curbstone, flagstone or any other portion or part of any
sidewalk, or upon any tree, lamppost, hitchpost, telegraph pole, hydrant or upon any private wall, door
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 112/336
or gate, without the consent in writing of the owner of the wall, door or gate; provided, however, that
this Section shall not prevent posting by proper City and County officials of election signs, polling
place signs and other signs or placards necessary under the law to the conduct of elections. (1970
Code)
6-1-44: PROPERTY, MALICIOUS INJURY TO:
It shall be unlawful for any person wilfully and maliciously to injure, deface, mutilate, remove, pull
down, break or in any manner interfere with or molest or secrete or destroy any real or personal
property belonging to or under the control of any person. (1970 Code)
6-1-45: PROSTITUTION:
It shall be unlawful for any person to pursue or advertise in any manner her vocation as a prostitute or
for any person to advertise the profession of a prostitute or solicit for a prostitute. (1970 Code)
6-1-46: PROSTITUTION, HOUSE OF:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or assist in the keeping of a house of ill-fame or prostitution
or knowingly to reside therein or knowingly to rent, lease or permit any person to occupy any house or
room owned, leased or controlled by him for this purpose. (1970 Code)
6-1-47: RESISTING AN OFFICER:
It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere wilfully with, resist, delay, obstruct, molest or threaten to
molest any officer of the City in the exercise of his official duties. (1970 Code)
6-1-48: RIOT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse immediately to disperse upon an order to do so by a
police officer, when two (2) or more persons are assembled for the purpose of disturbing the peace or
for the purpose of committing any unlawful act. (1970 Code)
6-1-49: SWINDLING:
It shall be unlawful for any person who by color, or aid of any trick or sleight of hand performance or by
fraud or by fraudulent scheme, cards, dice or device to win for himself or for another any money or
property or a representative of either. (1970 Code)
6-1-50: TRESPASSING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to take down any fence or to let down any bars or to open any gate
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 113/336
in or on the property of another without the consent of the owner, occupant or person in charge
thereof. (1970 Code)
6-1-51: VAGRANCY:
It shall be unlawful for any person without visible means of support and the physical ability to work not
to seek employment or labor, or to refuse to work when employment is offered him; for any person to
seek alms as a business; for any person to roam about from place to place without any lawful
business; for any idle or dissolute person or associate of known thieves to wander about the streets at
a late and unusual hour of the night, or to lodge in any other place than is kept for lodging purposes
without the permission of the owner of the property or the person in possession thereof; or for any
person to consort habitually with common prostitutes, habitual drunkards or any user of narcotics.
(1970 Code)
6-1-52: VEHICLES, INJURY TO3:
It shall be unlawful for any person to individually, or in association with one or more others, wilfully
break, injure, tamper with or remove any part or parts of any vehicle for the purpose of injuring,
defacing or destroying such vehicle, or temporarily or permanently preventing its useful operation, or
for any purpose against the will or without the consent of the owner of such vehicle or to in any other
manner wilfully or maliciously interfere with or prevent the running or operation of such vehicle. (1970
Code)
6-1-53: VENEREAL DISEASES; LITERATURE CONCERNING:
A. No person shall offer to sell, or give away, distribute or have in his possession with intent to give
away, sell or distribute, any book, pamphlet, circular, handbill or advertisement of any kind
purporting to treat diseases known as "venereal diseases" describing or explaining the genital
organs, giving the nature and remedies of diseases peculiar to females, or the nature or causes of
nervous debility, impotency, sterility or barrenness, gonorrhea, gleet, stricture, syphilis, infection of
the prostate gland or the remedies therefor, or the cause or remedies for abortion or miscarriage,
or articles or means of preventing conception.
B. No person shall sell, give, distribute or have in his possession, with intent to give away, sell or
distribute any book, pamphlet, circular, handbill, advertisement or notice of any kind, giving or
purporting to give information from whom or where medicine or anything whatever may be
obtained for the cure, prevention or treatment of uterine diseases, or diseases peculiar to females,
venereal diseases, or diseases of the genital organs, or nervous debility, impotency, sterility or
barrenness, gonorrhea, gleet, stricture, syphilis, infection of the prostate gland, abortion or
miscarriage, or articles or means of preventing conception. (1970 Code)
6-1-54: WATER FLOWING UPON STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any water to flow into or upon any public thoroughfare.
(1970 Code)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 114/336
6-1-55: WEAPONS, FURNISHING TO PRISONERS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to furnish or attempt to furnish or take into jail or to deliver or
attempt to deliver to any prisoner therein confined, or in the custody of any officer, any weapon, tool,
intoxicating liquors, drug or other article without the consent of the officer in charge. (1970 Code)
6-1-56: WINDOW PEEPING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to look, peer or peep into, or to be found loitering around or within
view of any window not on his own property with the intent of watching or looking through said
window. (Ord. 374, 8-5-1957)
6-1-57: WINDOW SILLS TO BE KEPT CLEAR:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place or keep on any window sill, porch or other projection above
the first story of any building abutting on any sidewalk any article which might do injury by falling upon
any person on the sidewalk in front of such building, unless said article be securely fastened or
protected by screens. (1970 Code)
6-1-58: WEAPONS, DISCHARGE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge any weapon, air gun, sparrow gun, flipper, firearm or
any similar device or contrivance within the limits of the City. Exceptions to the above provisions are
as follows:
A. Police or law enforcement officers in their line of duty.
B. Gooding police officers upon the consent of the City Council to control animals within the City limits.
(Ord. 610, 7-26-1999)
6-1-59: MUNICIPAL SWIMMING POOL; UNAUTHORIZED PERSONS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person, without the specific authorization of the Mayor, a member of the
Council, Chief of Police, or any department head, to attempt to enter, enter or be in the Gooding
Municipal Swimming Pool, including the dressing rooms and other structures adjacent thereto, at any
time when the said swimming pool facilities are not open to the general public. (Ord. 488, 8-2-1976)
6-1-60: LIQUOR CONSUMPTION IN PUBLIC PLACES:
A. It shall be unlawful for any person to consume or cause to be consumed any beer or intoxicating
liquor in any public place or building or at any public gathering, within the limits of the City.
Provided, however, that this shall not apply to premises which hold a current and valid license to
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 115/336
dispense beer or intoxicating liquor. "Public place", as defined in this Section, includes any place,
building or conveyance, to which the public has or is permitted to have access, and any place,
highway, street, lane, park or place of public resort or amusement, within the limits of the City.
B. Any person violating any of the provisions of this section shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in
any sum not less than twenty five dollars ($25.00) nor more than three hundred dollars ($300.00),
or imprisonment in the city jail for a period not to exceed thirty (30) days, or by both such fine and
imprisonment. (Ord. 503, 6-5-1978)
6-1-61: NOISE:
A. Definitions: For the purposes of this section, the following definitions shall apply:
CITY: Gooding, Idaho, or the area within the city limits of Gooding, Idaho.
COMMON AREA(S): The area(s) of a facility, complex, apartment unit, motel or the like that is
open either to the general public or person with the permission of the owner or agent of the owner
of the area. This definition would include, but not be limited to, the following: swimming pools,
restaurants, patios, meeting rooms, lounges, bars or other areas with a facility that are either
constructed or designed for use in this manner.
EMERGENCY: Any occurrence or set of circumstances involving actual or imminent physical
trauma or property damaged demanding immediate attention.
EMERGENCY VEHICLE: A motor vehicle owned or leased by a city, county or fire district; an
ambulance; or a motor vehicle owned or leased by a federal, state, county or municipal law
enforcement agency.
PERSON: Any individual, association, organization or entity having a legally recognized existence,
whether public or private.
PLACE OF RESIDENCE: Any building or portion thereof adapted or used and intended for the
overnight accommodation of persons. In the event a building used for multiple individual units,
such as an apartment, condominium, motel or other multi-family residence, each individual unit
shall be considered a separate residence for the purpose of this section.
PLAINLY AUDIBLE: Any audible sound that can be detected by a person using his or her unaided
hearing faculties.
B. Operation Of Any Device: It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or permit the operation of
any device in such a manner that the sound therefrom:
1. Is plainly audible within any place of residence not the source of the sound; or
2. Is plainly audible upon a public right of way or street at a distance of one hundred feet (100') or
more from the source of such sound.
C. Jake Brakes: It shall be unlawful to use engine compression brakes, commonly known as "jake
brakes", within the city limits of the city of Gooding, Idaho.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 116/336
D. Erection, Demolition And Major Alterations: It shall be unlawful to engage in the erection, including
excavating, of new buildings and demolition and major alteration or repair of any existing buildings
other than between the hours of seven thirty o'clock (7:30) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) P.M.
Monday through Saturday, except in the case of urgent necessity in the interest of public health
and safety. Major alteration or repair is defined as having a value in excess of two thousand dollars
($2,000.00).
E. Appliances, Blasting Agents And Explosives: It shall be unlawful to operate any pile driver, steam
shovel, pneumatic hammer, derrick, ram or electric hoist or other appliance, blasting devices or
other explosives, the use of which is attended by loud or unusual noise, other than between the
hours of seven thirty o'clock (7:30) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. Monday through Saturday,
except in case of urgent necessity in the interest of public health and safety.
F. Exemptions: The following sounds shall be exempt from the provisions of this section:
1. Sounds caused by any emergency vehicle or personnel in responding to an emergency call or
acting in time of an emergency.
2. Sounds caused by activities upon any outdoor municipal, school, religious or publicly owned
property or facility, provided that such activities have been authorized by the owner of such
property or facility or by its agent.
3. Sounds from parades, firework displays or any other event for which a permit for that type of
activity is required and has been obtained from the appropriate governmental entity within the
limits imposed by any such permit.
4. Sounds caused by locomotives or other railroad equipment.
5. Sounds from burglar alarms that are not in violation of law.
6. Sounds caused by safety warning devices which are required by law.
7. Sounds caused from devices associated with lawful land uses within the zoning district from
which the noise emanated, including any sound lawful under the terms of a special use permit.
8. Sounds emanating from devices used within the common area of a multi-unit residential
dwelling, whose use has been approved by the persons who have lawful authority to manage
the common areas. This exemption only applies in relation to persons complaining about sounds
from other units within the same multi-unit facility.
G. Relationship To Other Laws: The provisions of this section are intended to be cumulative and not
exclusive and shall not affect any other prohibition or regulation of noise or sound now adopted by
the city of Gooding or by any other jurisdiction with authority to administer laws within the city limits
of Gooding, Idaho.
H. Penalty: Any person who violates a term or provision of this section shall be guilty of an infraction
punishable by a fine of fifty dollars ($50.00), including court costs and fees. (Ord. 642, 4-4-2005)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 117/336
Chapter 2
CURFEW
6-2-1: CURFEW ESTABLISHED:
It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of eighteen (18) years to be or remain and it shall be
unlawful for any parent, guardian or adult person having the care and custody of any person under the
age of eighteen (18) years to allow or permit such person to be or remain in or upon the streets, alleys
or public places or grounds between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and five o'clock
(5:00) A.M. (Ord. 470, 9-16-1974)
6-2-2: EXCEPTIONS TO PROHIBITION:
The provisions of section 6-2-1 of this chapter shall not apply to any person who is accompanied by
his parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of such person, nor to any
person who is in the performance of an errand or duty directed by such person, parent, guardian or
other adult person having the care and custody of such person (which direction must be in writing,
signed and bearing the date of such errand or duty), nor to any person who is actually at the time
engaged in legitimate employment for profit. (1947 Code § 6-202)
Chapter 3
DOGS
6-3-1: DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE:
It shall be unlawful for any owner, possessor or person who keeps any dog to permit the same to run
at large upon the private premises of others or upon the streets, alleys, sidewalks, highways, vacant
lots, school grounds or other public places within the city of Gooding.
A dog shall be deemed to be running at large when off or away from the premises of the owner,
possessor, or keeper thereof, and not under the immediate control of such owner, possessor, or
keeper, or his agent or servant or a member of his immediate family, either by leash, cord or chain,
provided, however, that any dog on the premises of a city park or school grounds must be controlled
by a leash not exceeding ten feet (10') in length held in the hand of the person controlling the dog.
Procuring a license and tag shall not authorize the running at large of said dog.
Dogs in a vehicle, whether in the front, back, on top, or on the hood shall be secured so they cannot
jump out of the vehicle. Persons failing to secure such dog shall be punished as set forth in section 6-
3-14 of this chapter, as amended. (Ord. 684, 9-16-2013)
6-3-2: NUISANCES:
A. It shall be unlawful for any owner or other keeper of a dog or other animal, to fail to exercise proper
care and control of such animal to prevent it from becoming a public nuisance. Frequent,
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 118/336
continuous or untimely barking, molesting passersby, chasing vehicles, habitually attacking other
domestic animals, trespassing upon public or private property shall be deemed a nuisance.
B. It shall be unlawful for any owner or other keeper of an animal to fail to provide such animal with
sufficient and wholesome food and water, proper shelter and protection, and veterinary care when
needed to prevent suffering.
C. Any dog that bites or molests any person upon the public streets, alleys, or other public places, or
private premises other than those controlled by the owner, possessor or person who keeps such
dog, shall upon a complaint being filed by the person bitten, be put to death in a humane manner;
provided, however, nothing contained in this section shall be deemed to apply to any dog who bites
any person in actual defense of such dog's owner or immediate family when such owner or family
member is actually and unlawfully attacked by the person bitten.
D. If any fierce, dangerous or vicious dog is found at large which cannot be taken up and impounded,
such dog may be slain by any police officer or animal control officer. A "vicious dog" is hereby
defined as any dog which bites or snaps at a human being upon the public streets or ways, or
maims or kills other domestic animals. (Ord. 666, 3-16-2009)
6-3-3: AUTHORITY TO IMPOUND:
Any police officer, animal control officer or any other person authorized by the city may seize and
impound all dogs as required by this chapter, including any and all dogs or any other animal found
running at large upon the public streets, alleys or other public places or private premises without the
permission of the owner of said premises. (Ord. 666, 3-16-2009)
6-3-4: HEARING REGARDING IMPOUNDED ANIMALS:
A hearing may be held at the request of any animal owner whose animal has been impounded. Said
hearing shall be requested by contacting the city chief of police and shall be requested within two (2)
weeks of said impoundment. (Ord. 559, 3-7-1988)
6-3-5: LAWFUL TO GO ON PREMISES:
In the enforcement of any provision of this chapter, any police officer, deputy sheriff and/or animal
control officer or his assistant are authorized to enter the private property of any person to take
possession of a dog when in fresh pursuit of such dog at the time the dog goes onto private property.
(Ord. 666, 3-16-2009)
6-3-6: FEMALE IN HEAT PROHIBITED FROM RUNNING AT LARGE:
A. The owner of a female dog shall cause such dog, when in season, to be penned or closed in such
manner as to preclude other dogs from attacking such female dog or being attracted to such
female dog so as to create a public nuisance.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 119/336
B. It shall be unlawful for the owner or person having possession, charge, custody, or control of any
female dog to cause, permit, or allow the same to stray or run, or in any other manner be at large
in or upon any street or sidewalk while such dog is in copulating season. If a female dog cannot be
controlled by the owner during the copulating season, the female dog may be impounded by the
animal control officer or any police officer. (Ord. 559, 3-7-1988)
6-3-7: SUSPECTED RABIES:
A dog which is known to have bitten, or injured any person so as to cause an abrasion of the skin, or a
suspected rabid dog, shall be placed in confinement under observation of a veterinary hospital and
shall not be killed or released until it is at least ten (10) days after the onset of symptoms suggestive of
rabies. Any other animal subject to rabies that has bitten a person shall likewise be confined and
observed for at least ten (10) days. If the animal dies or has been killed, its head shall be removed
and immediately taken to the state health laboratory to be examined for rabies.
No person shall fail, refuse or neglect to allow an official of the city of Gooding to make an inspection
or examination thereof at any time during said period. No such dog or animal shall be removed from
the place of quarantine without written permission of the city of Gooding. If the animal shall be
determined to be free of rabies, the same shall be returned to the owner upon payment of all costs
and fees incurred by the city as set forth hereafter for impounded dogs. If such fee is not paid within
twenty four (24) hours the dog shall be subject to disposal as set forth hereafter. (Ord. 666, 3-16-2009)
6-3-8: LICENSE:
It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to own or harbor any dog within the corporate limits of
the city of Gooding without first obtaining a license therefor as herein provided; any owner or harborer
of any dog within the corporate limits of the city is hereby required to secure about the neck of such
dog a collar with license tag attached thereto which license tag shall be obtained from the city office.
The license fee required to be paid by the owner or harborer of such dog shall be ten dollars ($10.00)
for each dog. Such license fee shall be paid annually within thirty (30) days after January 1 of every
year. (Ord. 666, 3-16-2009)
6-3-9: CRUELTY PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to maltreat or torture any dog or other animal, or, having the right or
authority to kill any dog or other animal, to kill such dog or other animal in an inhumane manner. (Ord.
559, 3-7-1988)
6-3-10: UNLAWFUL TO POISON:
It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to administer or cause to be administered poison of any
sort whatsoever to any animal which is the property of another, or poison food where same is
accessible to any dog or other animal. Any person or persons so offending shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor. (Ord. 559, 3-7-1988)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 120/336
6-3-11: DUTIES OF POLICE DEPARTMENT:
It shall be the duty of the Gooding police department to carry out and enforce all the provisions of this
chapter; to enforce the licensing and the control of dogs in the city of Gooding as hereinbefore
provided; to file complaints in the magistrate court against any person, persons, firm or corporation
failing to license any dog as hereinbefore provided; or who otherwise fails to comply with any
provisions of this chapter; and to capture and secure all dogs found running at large contrary to the
provisions of this chapter; to remove such dogs in a humane manner to the pound; to hold dogs as
impounded for a period of not less than seventy two (72) hours. (Ord. 666, 3-16-2009)
6-3-12: REDEMPTION OF IMPOUNDED DOGS:
Any dog impounded may be taken from the pound by the owner, or any authorized person, upon
exhibiting to the animal control officer or other authorized person having charge of said pound a
receipt, from the city, showing that the license fee has been paid for such dog, and upon paying the
city an impounding fee of ten dollars ($10.00) for the first offense, forty dollars ($40.00) for the second
offense and eighty dollars ($80.00) for the third offense. Any dogs committing more than three (3)
offenses shall be disposed of in a humane manner. All impounded dogs not redeemed within seventy
two (72) hours may be offered for sale at a price not less than the costs of impoundment and keeping,
or any additional sum determined to be reasonable by the animal control officer, including any license
fee. Alternatively, such dog shall be turned over to an animal rescue group, that has appeared before
and been approved by the council, if adoptable. (Ord. 684, 9-16-2013)
6-3-13: DOG TRAPS:
It shall be unlawful and constitute a misdemeanor for any person to release a dog or dogs from a dog
trap owned or under the control of the city, or to any way injure, destroy or tamper with a dog trap
owned or under the control of the city. (Ord. 561, 4-18-1988)
6-3-14: PENALTIES:
Any owner, possessor or person violating any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction or entry
of a guilty plea, be guilty of an infraction and shall be fined as follows:
A. First offense: Fifty dollars ($50.00) plus court costs.
B. Second offense: One hundred dollars ($100.00) plus court costs.
C. Third offense, and thereafter: One hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) plus court costs. (Ord. 684, 9-16-
2013)
6-3-15: KENNEL LICENSE:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 121/336
A. It shall be unlawful to keep, maintain, harbor or possess upon the premises of any one household
or property, more than four (4) dogs, unless the owner or person having custody or harboring such
dogs shall have obtained a kennel license and unless the area is zoned for the allowance of
kennels. Provided, however, that dogs under three (3) months old shall not be considered when
determining the number of dogs. In zoning areas allowing kennels, a kennel license may be
obtained pursuant to the following procedure:
1. Upon the application of any person owning, harboring or maintaining more than four (4) dogs,
must be accompanied by the written consent of at least seventy five percent (75%) of all persons
in possession of the premises within a radius of three hundred feet (300') of the premises upon
which said kennel is to be maintained.
2. The application shall state the name and address of the owner where the kennel is to be located
and the number of dogs to be kept.
3. The issuance of a kennel license shall not obviate the necessity of obtaining an individual dog
license, nor shall any of the provisions hereof be deemed to vary or alter any of the zoning
regulations of the city of Gooding.
4. All applications for a kennel license shall be accompanied by a fee of one hundred dollars
($100.00) or such other fee as may from time to time be adopted by the Gooding city council.
5. Kennel licenses must be renewed annually and such application must meet all of the
requirements of this section each year.
B. It is the intent of this section to permit nonconforming uses to continue. It is the further intent of this
section that nonconforming uses shall not be enlarged upon nor be grounds for adding additional
animals. Property that is presently being used to house animals shall be grandfathered, if they are
legal under the ordinances currently in effect. However, in the event any animal is sold it must be
replaced within six (6) months or this section shall control the use of the land.
In the event any current property owner sells the property upon which the restricted animals are
currently kept, the new owner shall be governed by this section. (Ord. 637, 10-4-2004)
Chapter 4
ANIMALS AND FOWL
6-4-1: FOWLS RUNNING AT LARGE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or suffer any chickens, ducks, turkeys or geese or any
other fowl owned by them to run at large upon the streets, alleys or sidewalks of the city or upon the
private property of any person without the consent of the owner thereof. (1947 Code § 6-301)
6-4-2: POISONING OR KILLING ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully kill or administer poison to any domestic animal without
the consent of the owner thereof, or to expose any poisonous substance with the intention that it shall
be taken by any domestic animal. (1947 Code § 6-302)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 122/336
6-4-3: KEEPING CERTAIN ANIMALS:
A. It shall be a public health nuisance for any ungulate, including, but not limited to, horse, cow, goat,
sheep, or any chicken, duck, goose or other fowl regardless of age or sex, to be kept within the city
limits of the city of Gooding, Idaho.
B. The mayor and/or his designated appointee shall notify any person in violation or nonconformance
with subsection A of this section by written notice of abatement setting forth the violation and
allowing forty eight (48) hours to abate such nuisance. Said notification shall be personally served
upon the landowner, occupant or any other person allowing such nuisance to exist.
C. If the nuisance is not remedied within forty eight (48) hours of serving such notice, the chief of
police, or his designee, shall immediately cause the same to be abated by removing the offending
animal(s), impounding the same and notifying the owner, occupant, or other person having control
over the animal(s) that the owner, occupant or other person, shall have five (5) days to redeem the
animal(s) and that after the five (5) day period the animal(s) will be sold or destroyed.
D. The owner shall be obligated to the city of Gooding for the costs of impoundment and board and no
animal will be redeemed until such costs are paid in full. In the event the animal(s) is sold the
proceeds shall be first applied to the costs of impoundment, boarding and sale and the remainder
shall be delivered to the owner of such animal(s). In the event an animal is destroyed the owner
will still be obligated for all of the above costs plus costs of removal and destruction. (Ord. 637, 10-
4-2004)
6-4-4: KEEPING SWINE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep either on his premises or on the premises of another any
hog, pig or shoat. (1947 Code § 6-305)
6-4-5: GRAZING ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person owning livestock or the agent or employee of such person to allow
any horses, mules, jacks, sheep, cattle, hogs or any animal to range or graze within the limits of the
city. All stock driven through the city must be accompanied by a competent herder who shall not
permit the said stock to enter upon ditches or sidewalks or injure shade trees or shrubbery, and no
stock of any kind or nature shall be driven down, through or upon Main Street. No stock shall be kept
within the city limits overnight unless the said stock be confined within a barn or enclosure. (1947
Code § 6-306)
6-4-6: CHIEF OF POLICE TO IMPOUND ANIMALS:
It shall be the duty of the chief of police to take up and impound any such stock mentioned in this
chapter found in violation of any of its provisions. (1947 Code § 6-307)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 123/336
6-4-7: NOTICE OF IMPOUNDING:
When the chief of police shall seize and impound any animal mentioned in this chapter, he shall, if the
owner of such animal is known to him, give personal notice to such owner of such seizure either by
serving a written notice personally or placing it in the post office stamped, sealed and addressed to
such person. If the owner be unknown, the chief of police shall post in at least four (4) conspicuous
public places for not less than five (5) days prior to the time of sale, a written or printed notice
containing the description of the animal seized by him, with their marks or brands, the date of seizure
and the time and place where the same will be sold, provided that no sale shall be made within five (5)
days from the date of such seizure. (1947 Code § 6-308)
6-4-8: UNCLAIMED ANIMALS:
Any animal seized or impounded if unclaimed, or if claimed and upon which the legal charges have
not been paid, shall be branded and sold by the chief of police at public sale to the highest bidder for
cash at the time and place mentioned in the notice of sale. The money received by the chief of police
for the sale of any animal so seized and impounded shall, after deducting the cost of such seizure,
keeping, posting notice and sale, be paid to the treasurer. (1947 Code § 6-309)
6-4-9: IMPOUNDED ANIMALS:
Any animal so seized and impounded shall be provided with proper care, food and water by the chief
of police or pound keeper. (1947 Code § 6-310)
6-4-10: POUND TO BE PROVIDED:
The chief of police shall erect, or cause to be erected or maintained, a suitable enclosure to be kept
locked when any animal or animals shall be impounded therein, which shall be designated as the city
pound, or he may rent a suitable enclosure for such purposes at a rental not to exceed three dollars
($3.00) per month. (1947 Code § 6-311)
6-4-11: REDEMPTION OF ANIMALS:
If at any time prior to the sale of any impounded animal the person entitled to the possession thereof
shall claim the same, he shall prove his ownership or his right to the possession of such animal and
upon the payment to the chief of police of a penalty of one dollar ($1.00) and all legal charges and
expenses incident to taking up and keeping such animal the same shall be delivered to him. (1947
Code § 6-312)
6-4-12: FEES FOR IMPOUNDING:
The chief of police shall be allowed the following fees for seizing, impounding, branding or selling any
animal under the provisions of this chapter:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 124/336
A. Impounding:
1. For taking up and impounding horses, mules, jackasses, burros and cattle per head: Two dollars
($2.00).
2. For sheep, goats and swine per head: One dollar ($1.00).
B. Keeping And Feeding:
1. For keeping and feeding per head for each day for horses, mules, jackasses, burros and cattle:
Fifty cents ($0.50).
2. For sheep, goats and swine: Fifteen cents ($0.15).
C. Posting: For posting notices: Fifty cents ($0.50). (1947 Code § 6-313)
6-4-13: REPORT OF CHIEF OF POLICE:
The chief of police shall at the first regular meeting of each month of the council, file a report showing
the animals so impounded, when seized, the date of sale, the amounts received for penalties and on
the sale of such animals, the amount of his fees, the amount paid the treasurer and names of the
owner if known to him. He shall receive a receipt from the treasurer for all such monies paid and file
the same with his report. (1947 Code § 6-314)
6-4-14: MONIES RECEIVED OVER COSTS:
Should it appear from the report of the chief of police, provided for under this chapter, that the amount
received upon any sale is greater than the gross sum of penalty, expenses and charges, the treasurer
shall hold the excess as a special deposit to be paid to the owner of such animal on demand or proof
of ownership or right of possession to such animal as at any time prior to the expiration of three (3)
months from date of sale. If claim be not made for the special deposit within the three (3) months, the
treasurer shall place the money in the general fund for the use of the city. (1947 Code § 6-315)
6-4-15: BREAKING INTO POUND:
Any person who shall break into the city pound or take therefrom any animal impounded therein or
shall attempt to take any such animal or animals from the chief of police while on his way to the
pound, shall, on conviction thereof, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (1947 Code § 6-316)
6-4-16: HORSES AND MULES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to leave a horse or mule standing without having the same securely
fastened and tied. (1947 Code § 6-317)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 125/336
6-4-17: HITCHING TO TREES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to hitch any animal to any tree situated on the streets of the city or
to hitch or tie any animal so that said animal will cause the injury of any shade tree or to any ditch in
said street. (1947 Code § 6-318)
6-4-18: IMPROPER HITCHING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to hitch or fasten any animal to or in such manner as to destroy or
injure any growing or living shade tree, ornamental or fruit tree, or any box or case around such tree.
(1947 Code § 6-319)
6-4-19: SLAUGHTERING OR BUTCHERING PROHIBITED:
A. It shall be unlawful for any person to kill any animal for slaughter or butchering within the city of
Gooding, except in the normal course of business by a duly licensed slaughterhouse.
B. Any person violating any provision of this section shall be, upon conviction or entry of a guilty plea,
found guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished by a fine not to exceed three hundred dollars
($300.00) and/or sentenced to the county jail for a term not to exceed six (6) months. (Ord. 612, 1-
3-2000)
Chapter 5
GUN DEALERS
6-5-1: RECORDS:
Any person buying, selling, trading or dealing in new, used or secondhand shotguns, rifles, pistols and
other firearms of every kind capable of being carried on or about the person shall keep a permanent
legible written record in a bound volume showing and containing the following information relative
thereto: a) the date acquired or sold; b) name and address of person from whom acquired or to whom
sold; c) name and make; d) serial, factory or other identification numbers; e) date sold or bought; f)
name and address of person from whom bought or to whom sold. Such records shall be open for
inspection by any member of the police force at any and all reasonable times. (Ord. 358, 6-6-1955)
6-5-2: INFORMATION REQUIRED:
Any and all customers or persons buying, selling or trading any such firearms from any such dealer,
shall furnish said information upon request. (Ord. 358, 6-6-1955)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 126/336
Chapter 6
BICYCLE SALES
6-6-1: DEFINITION:
The term "bicycle" as used herein means and includes any and all two (2) wheeled vehicles having a
tandem arrangement of the wheels, a saddle or seat for the rider, handle bars and levers or pedals for
propulsion of the vehicle by the feet of the rider. (10-201; 1947 Code)
6-6-2: BICYCLES TO BE REGISTERED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to ride, operate or propel any bicycle, or permit any bicycle to stand
or be parked on the streets or alleys unless such bicycle has been registered with the Clerk and
unless there is properly attached thereto a registry plate secured from said Clerk as hereinafter
provided. (10-202; 1947 Code)
6-6-3: REGISTRATION:
Annually on or before the first day of January every bicycle in the City must be registered with the
Clerk and such registry shall show the true name and address of the owner of each bicycle, the make,
serial number, the name of the person or dealer from whom such bicycle was purchased, the date of
its purchase, and such information as may be demanded by said Clerk. (10-203; 1947 Code)
6-6-4: PLATES TO BE ATTACHED:
As each registration is effected a number plate shall be assigned to said bicycle, which number plate
must be attached to the front of said bicycle in such manner that said plate and the numbers thereon
will be in plain view while such bicycle is in motion or parked, and such number plate shall remain so
attached throughout the current registration year; and any number plate issued during any year shall
be invalid and shall be detached from the bicycle on and after the first day of January following its
issuance; and only one plate shall be displayed upon a bicycle. (10-204, 1947 Code)
6-6-5: SALE OR TRANSFER:
In case of the sale or transfer of a bicycle, the purchaser or transferee shall immediately report such
sale or transfer to the Clerk and give the Clerk the name and address of the new owner, and the
registration number plate shall thereupon be transferred to such new owner or transferee, and the
number plate originally assigned to such bicycle must remain attached thereto until the end of the
current registration period. (10-205, 1947 Code)
6-6-6: REGISTRATION FEE:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 127/336
Every bicycle owner shall pay a fee of fifty cents ($0.50) for each bicycle registered and to which a
number plate is so issued, and upon each transfer of a bicycle the purchaser or transferee shall pay a
like sum upon his registration as provided in Section 6-6-5 herein; the Clerk shall be responsible under
his official bond for all monies collected under this Chapter and such monies shall be delivered to the
Treasurer on the first day of each month. (10-206, 1947 Code)
6-6-7: VEHICLE LAWS:
Every person riding a bicycle upon any highway, street or alley shall be subject to all the laws, rules
and regulations applicable to the driver of any vehicle except those provisions which by their very
nature can have no application. (10-207, 1947 Code)
6-6-8: WARNING DEVICE REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to ride, use or operate a bicycle upon the highways, streets, alleys
and public places unless the same be equipped with a bell, gong or some sounding device sufficient
for giving others upon such ways timely warning of the approach of said bicycle; and the operators of
all bicycles upon such ways shall use such warning device for said purpose; however, that sirens may
not be used on bicycles. (10-208, 1947 Code)
6-6-9: LIGHTS REQUIRED:
No person shall ride a bicycle upon the streets, alleys or public places during the night time without
having such bicycle equipped with a headlight which shall be so constructed and attached as to be the
clearly discernible by any normal person for a distance of at least three hundred feet (300') in front of
said bicycle, and also with a reflector attached to the rear of said bicycle so that it may be readily
observed by traffic approaching from the rear. (10-209, 1947 Code)
6-6-10: PARKING BICYCLES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate, use, park or leave a bicycle upon any of the sidewalks
and no bicycle shall be parked or left in a parking space or lane established and marked on the street
or curb by the City officials for the use of automobiles, but shall be parked and left in racks and similar
spaces provided or to be provided for the use of bicycles, or in spaces not marked off and reserved for
automobiles and similar vehicles. (10-210, 1947 Code)
6-6-11: NUMBER ON BICYCLE PROHIBITED; HOLDING ONTO VEHICLE:
Two (2) or more riders on the same bicycle is prohibited at all times, and no one while riding a bicycle
shall hold onto or be in any way attached to any other vehicle or person thereon. (10-211, 1947 Code)
6-6-12: SERIAL NUMBER:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 128/336
No bicycle shall be sold or registered unless it shall have embossed, cut or impressed on some
portion thereof a serial or manufacturer's number; any person who has in his possession a bicycle
from which the serial or manufacturer's number has been removed or defaced shall immediately
present such bicycle to the Chief of Police, who shall issue numbers to the owner to be placed on
such bicycle and registered as its serial number before a number plate shall be issued therefor. (10-
212, 1947 Code)
6-6-13: RACING PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to run or engage in or cause to be run or engaged in any bicycle
race except with the express permission and under the direct supervision of the Chief of Police, which
official is hereby given authority to designate the times and places such races may be held and
prescribe regulations therefor. (10-213, 1947 Code)
6-6-14: RECKLESS RIDING:
It shall be unlawful to ride a bicycle in a reckless or careless manner, or in any manner that will be
dangerous to the person or property of the person operating such bicycle or to others, and all persons
riding bicycles are expressly forbidden to weave from left to right or vice versa. (10-214, 1947 Code)
6-6-15: UNCLAIMED BICYCLES:
Any and all bicycles left and abandoned on any street, alley, public place or vacant lot shall be taken
up and held by the Chief of Police, and if the same are not claimed by the owner or his authorized
agent within a period of ninety (90) days may sold by the Chief of Police at public auction to the
highest bidder for cash. Provided, that if the owner of any such bicycle be known to the Chief of
Police, or if he can identify the owner by reference to the bicycle registry of the City, he shall
immediately notify such owner in writing, describing the bicycle and advising where the same may be
obtained. (Ord. 355, 6-21-1954)
6-6-16: NOTICE REQUIRED:
Before sale of such bicycles, notice thereof shall be given in two (2) issues of the Enterprise, which
notice shall describe the bicycles so to be sold by giving the name, color, make and any other
distinguishing information, and such notice shall also give the time, place and terms of sale, and shall
state that the owner may claim and receive his bicycle at or before the time of such sale by submitting
proof of his ownership and paying costs of the notice. (Ord. 355, 6-21-1954; amd. Ord. 501, 1-16-
1978)
6-6-17: SALE; TITLE:
Any person purchasing a bicycle at such sale will succeed to all the title and interest thereto, will be
deemed the owner thereof by the City and may register the same and be issued a license in the
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 129/336
manner provided in this Chapter. All monies received from the sale of any such bicycles shall be
turned into the City's General Fund. (Ord. 355,6-21-1954)
Chapter 7
ABANDONED VEHICLES
6-7-1: DECLARED NUISANCES:
The accumulation and storage of abandoned, wrecked or junked vehicles, major household
furnishings or appliances or machinery, or parts thereof, on public or private property within the City is
found to create a condition tending to reduce the value of property, to promote blight and deterioration,
to invite plundering, to create fire hazards, to constitute attractive nuisances creating a hazard to
health and safety of minors, injurious to the health, safety and general welfare; and the presence of
such items on public or private property within the City except as expressly permitted in this Chapter,
is declared to constitute and be a public nuisance which may be abated as such in accordance with
the provisions of this Chapter. (Ord. 562, 6-6-1988)
6-7-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this Chapter, the following words and phrases shall have the meanings
respectively ascribed to them by this Section:
ABANDONED, WRECKED AND JUNKED: With reference to vehicles, an unsightly motor vehicle
which meets any one of the following qualifications:
A. Does not carry a current valid State registration and license plate:
B. Cannot be safely operated under its own power.
MACHINERY: All articles of industrial, farm or domestic machinery or equipment and any and all metal
or wooden machinery, motors, equipment or tools.
MAJOR HOUSEHOLD FURNISHINGS AND APPLIANCES: All articles usually referred to as major
household furnishings and appliances used in house-keeping, including, but not limited to, chairs,
tables, davenports, beds, refrigerators, stoves, washers, dryers, furnaces and grease, oil and paint
containers of five (5) gallons or over capacity.
MOTOR VEHICLES: Any vehicle propelled or drawn by power other than muscular power designed to
travel on the ground by wheels, treads, runners or slides and to transport persons or property or pull
machinery including, but not limited to, automobiles, trucks, trailers, motorcycles and tractors.
PERSON: Any individual, corporation or partnership. (Ord. 562, 6-6-1988)
6-7-3: PLACEMENT IN STREET UNLAWFUL:
It is unlawful for any person to place, allow, discard, maintain, park or store any abandoned, wrecked
or junked vehicle, major household furnishing or appliance or machinery, or parts thereof, as defined
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 130/336
in Section 6-7-2 upon any public street, alley, sidewalk or other public property within the City. (Ord.
562,6-6-1988)
6-7-4: PLACEMENT IN OPEN VIEW ON PRIVATE PROPERTY UNLAWFUL:
It is unlawful for any person, whether he be owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise of any
private property or premises, to place, allow, discard, maintain, park, store or permit to be placed,
allowed, discarded, maintained, parked or stored upon such property or premises for a period of time
exceeding thirty (30) days any abandoned, wrecked or junked vehicle, major household furnishing or
appliance or machinery, or parts thereof, as defined in Section 6-7-2; provided, however, that the
provisions of this Section shall not apply to any property or premises where the vehicle, furnishing,
appliance or machinery, or part thereof, is housed within a building or fence so as to not be visible
from the street or other public or private property, or stored or parked in a lawful manner in connection
with or incidental to a business or commercial enterprise which is the primary or principal use of such
property or premises. (Ord. 562, 6-6-1988)
6-7-5: ABATEMENT:
A. By the order of the Mayor or any member of the City Council, any duly sworn police officer of the
City may order any abandoned, wrecked, or junked vehicle, a major household furnishing or
appliance or machinery, or parts thereof removed from the premises from which they reside within
ten (10) days.
B. Notice of the order shall be placed by the policeman upon the vehicle, furnishing, appliance,
machinery, or parts thereof, and a copy of the notice shall additionally be served upon any adult
person occupying the premises upon which same item is located and upon the owner of the item, if
said person is known.
C. If there be no occupant or owner of the premises, any notice affixed to any building or upon any
other prominent object upon the premises shall constitute notice to such owner or occupant of the
premises or the owner of the item involved; provided, however, that if such owner or occupant is
only temporarily absent, such notice shall be by certified mail.
D. If removal is not accomplished within the time and in the manner prescribed by the order and
notice, the Police Department by the direction of the Mayor and City Council, may seek an order
from the appropriate court of competent jurisdiction, directed to the owner or occupant to show
cause why the item of abandoned, wrecked or junked vehicle, major household furnishing or
appliance, or machinery, or part thereof should not be removed.
E. Upon obtaining a proper order, the Police Department may cause such item of abandoned,
wrecked, or junked vehicle, a major household furnishing, or appliance, or machinery or parts
thereof to be removed at the expense of the owner and placed in an impounding yard where it
shall be offered for sale to the highest and best bidder at a public auction after two (2) publications
in any newspaper published within the City, only in full accordance with such laws and regulations
as may govern such dispositions of abandoned or junked vehicles as established by the proper
agency of the State.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 131/336
F. The proceeds of such a sale shall be used to pay expense of removal, impounding and sale, and if
the proceeds are not sufficient therefor the balance shall immediately become due alone from the
owner or occupant of the premises if not paid by such owner. (Ord. 562, 6-6-1988)
6-7-6: INTERFERENCE WITH CITY OFFICIALS PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person to interfere with, hinder or refuse to allow any authorized City officer or
employee to enter upon private or public property during usual business hours to enforce any
provision of this Chapter. (Ord. 562, 6-6-1988)
6-7-7: VIOLATION DEEMED MISDEMEANOR:
Any person violating any provision of this Chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord.
562, 6-6-1988)
Chapter 8
FIREWORKS
6-8-1: FIREWORKS:
A. Fireworks shall include blank cartridges, toy cannons, toy canes or toy guns in which explosives are
used, fire balloons (balloons of a type which have burning material of any kind attached thereto or
which require fire underneath to propel them), firecrackers, torpedoes, skyrockets, Roman candles,
fountain wheels, dago bombs, sparklers and other fireworks of like construction and any fireworks
containing any combustible or explosive substance for the purpose of producing a visible or
audible effect by combustion, deflagration, explosion or detonation.
B. Exempted from this part are all toy pistols, toy cannons, toy guns and toy canes, and similar
devices such as party poppers or party favors, in which paper caps containing not more than
twenty five one-hundredths (.25) grain of explosive compound per cap are used, and such caps
whether single, roll or tape type. (1970 Code)
6-8-2: DANGEROUS FIREWORKS:
Dangerous fireworks includes any of the following:
A. Firecrackers, cannon crackers, giant crackers, salutes, silver tube salutes, cherry bombs, mines,
ground bombardment, grasshoppers and other explosive articles of similar nature;
B. Blank cartridges;
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 132/336
C. Skyrockets and rockets, including all similar devices employing any combustible or explosive
material and which ride in the air during discharge;
D. Roman candles, including all devices which discharge balls of fire into the air;
E. Chasers and whistles, including all devices which dart or travel about the surface of the ground
during discharge;
F. Snakes and hats containing bichloride of mercury;
G. Sparklers more than ten inches (10") in length or one-quarter inch (1/,") in diameter or made with
other than iron wires;
H. All articles for pyrotechnic display such as aerial shells, salutes, flash shells, sky battles, parachute
shells, mines, dago bombs and similar fireworks devices including cracker balls;
I. All torpedoes which explode by means of friction, or which contain arsenic, and all other similar
fireworks devices including cracker balls;
J. Fire balloons or balloons of any type which have burning material of any kind attached thereto.
(1970 Code)
6-8-3: SAFE AND SANE FIREWORKS:
Safe and sane fireworks include any of the following:
A. Cane fountains with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding fifty (50) grams each;
B. Cylindrical fountains, whether base, spike or handle with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding
seventy five (75) grams each and inside tube diameter not exceeding three-fourths inch (3/4");
C. Sparklers and dipped sticks not more than ten inches (10") in length or one-fourth inch ('/4") in
diameter made of steel or iron wire and suzuki and Morning Glories with pyrotechnic composition
not exceeding four (4) grams each;
D. Snakes which do not contain bichloride of mercury and pyrotechnic composition not exceeding two
(2) grams each;
E. Wheels with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding sixty (60) grains for each driver unit or two
hundred forty (240) grains for each complete wheel. The inside tube diameter of driver unit shall
not exceed one-half inch ('/2");
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 133/336
F. Whistles, without report and which do not dart or travel about the ground during discharge with
pyrotechnic composition not exceeding six (6) grams and containing no picric or gallic acid. (1970
Code)
6-8-4: PERMITS:
A. It shall be unlawful for any person in the City to import, export, offer for sale, sell, possess, keep or
store, or permit the keeping or storing of any dangerous fireworks for any use or purpose, except
that a person holding a dangerous fireworks permit issued pursuant to the terms and conditions of
this Chapter may use dangerous fireworks for a safely supervised and conducted public display of
fireworks, and said fireworks may be stored for a period not exceeding four (4) days immediately
preceding the date of said public display.
B. No person, without having a valid safe fireworks permit issued pursuant to the terms and conditions
set forth in this Chapter shall import, export, possess for the purpose of sale, offer for sale, or sell
any safe and sane fireworks for any use or purpose. (1970 Code)
6-8-5: APPLICATION:
A. Any reputable person in reasonable pursuit or furtherance of any legitimate personal business or
charitable purpose, desiring to engage in the sale of safe and sane fireworks within the City, shall
first make written application to the Clerk for a safe and sane fireworks permit. Each applicant shall
pay to the Clerk a fee of ten dollars ($10.00) at the time he files his application, and shall not be
refundable in any event.
B. Any reputable person in reasonable pursuit or furtherance of any legitimate personal business or
charitable purpose, desiring to make a public display of dangerous fireworks shall first make
written application to the Clerk for a dangerous fireworks permit. Each applicant shall pay to the
Clerk a fee of ten dollars ($10.00) at the time he files his application, and shall not be refundable in
any event. (Ord. 476, 4-21-1975)
6-8-6: FORM OF APPLICATION:
Each applicant for a safe and sane fireworks permit or a dangerous fireworks permit shall file his
application with the Clerk. Each application shall show the following:
A. Name and address of applicant.
B. The purpose for which the applicant is primarily existing and for which it was organized.
C. The names and addresses of the officers, trustees and/or directors, if any, of the applicant.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 134/336
D. The location where the applicant requests permission to sell safe and sane fireworks or display
dangerous fireworks.
E. When and where the applicant was organized and established, or, if a natural person, the
applicant's age.
F. The location of the applicant's principal and permanent meeting place or places, or principal place
of business.
G. The applicant's State Sales Tax Permit Number.
H. If the applicant is an entity other than a sole proprietorship, the name and a general description of
the business activities of each parent or subsidiary company, business or entity, and a general
description of the ownership organization of each parent or subsidiary, if any.
I. Such other information as the Clerk may require on a standard form submitted to all applicants and
which is reasonably necessary to protect the public health, safety and morals. (1970 Code)
6-8-7: INVESTIGATION:
The Clerk shall cause an investigation to be made of each application and applicant and shall submit
a written report of his findings and recommendations for or against the issuance of the permit,
together with his reasons therefor, to the Mayor and Councilmen of the City, which report shall not be
public information except on request of the applicant or by order of a court of competent jurisdiction.
(1970 Code)
6-8-8: POWER TO DENY:
The Mayor and Councilmen of the City shall have the power in its discretion to grant or deny any
application, subject to such reasonable conditions, if any, as it shall prescribe so long as the denial of
the application is reasonably necessary for protection of the public health, safety and morals. (1970
Code)
6-8-9: TERM OF PERMIT:
A safe and sane fireworks permit or a dangerous fireworks permit issued pursuant to this Chapter
shall be valid only within the calendar year in which issued. A permit shall be valid only for the specific
premises or location designated in the permit. However, subject to reasonable conditions necessary
for protection of the public health, safety and morals, an applicant may be granted permits for more
than one site or location within the City. No permit shall be transferable or assignable. (1970 Code)
6-8-10: TIME OF FILING:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=893 135/336
Each application' for a permit to sell safe and sane fireworks at retail shall be filed with the Clerk on or
before June 1 of the calendar year for which the permit is sought. (Ord. 476, 4-21-1975)
6-8-11: LIABILITY INSURANCE:
Each applicant for a safe and sane fireworks permit or for a dangerous fireworks permit shall have
filed with the Clerk prior to the issuance and validity of any permit a policy, or a certified true copy
thereof, of public liability and products liability insurance, including both accident and occurrence
coverage. The insurance coverage limits for both public liability coverage and products liability
coverage limits shall be at least one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) per person per
